- Repeated thermal challenges from opponents who can match or exceed his output, each leaving traces in the form of brief unflamed periods immediately after (rest cycles he attributes to choice rather than necessity).
- Repeated near-drownings, each producing a slightly longer startle window the next time water is encountered unexpectedly.
- Repeated suffocation events in vacuum, smoke, and confined spaces, with cumulative effect on his unconscious threat-mapping of enclosed environments.
- Chronic mild caloric deficit during high-operations windows; the subject's metabolism through this period demands intake that occasionally outpaces his discipline to maintain, with corresponding micro-fatigue events that he masks through stimulant intake (caffeine, primarily; nothing harder, consistent with the father-pattern abstinence).
- Sleep debt accumulated in clusters around losses and crises, repaid in extended sleep periods that the family learns to recognize and protect.

None of this presents as visible pathology. The subject looks, throughout the period, like a man in his early thirties in excellent condition. The accumulation is internal and is one of the substrates that makes the late-period sacrifice possible — the body that flies into the Negative Zone portal at the end of this chronology has been **rehearsing dying** for fifteen years.

---

## 9. THE APPROACH TO THE LAST STAND

The closing window of the middle period — the months leading into the Negative Zone death — shows a subject who has, by the file's reading, *quieted.* The flirtation rate is down. The commercial ventures have stopped. The arguments with Sue are shorter and end faster. The pranks on Ben are gentler. He is spending more time with the children. He is more often the one who volunteers for the dangerous half of any operational split.

A reader of the record in real time would not have predicted the sacrifice. A reader of the record in retrospect can see the subject **arriving at the readiness to perform it** through small adjustments accumulated across the back half of this period. He is not seeking death. He is, however, no longer fleeing the stillness with quite the same velocity. The grief he has spent his life outrunning has, in some measure, caught up to him. He has not learned to speak to it. He has learned to stand near it without combusting.

When the portal closes — when he is on the wrong side of it, alone, with the army coming — he does what the middle period has prepared him for. He performs the act for which there is, finally, no audience but a brother in hand-sign through a closing door. The performance and the person become, for one moment, the same thing.

This is the end of the middle period and the beginning of everything that follows.

— END CHRONOLOGY III —


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

*Subject: Jonathan Lowell Spencer Storm. Reporting window: post-resurrection through present operational period. Source base: post-Hickman FF, Fraction FF, Robinson FF, "Final Days"/death-of-the-FF interval, Uncanny Avengers (Duggan run), Inhumans/Inhuman (Soule), Inhumans: Once and Future Kings, Civil War II, Marvel Two-in-One (Zdarsky), Fantastic Four relaunch (Slott), Fantastic Four (North), associated event tie-ins. File compiled to surveillance-grade granularity; behavioral inference annotated as such.*

---

## A. The Re-Entry Period — After the Negative Zone

The subject's resurrection is not, in the strict clinical sense, a return. The body that comes back is younger-presenting than the body that died — observers in the immediate post-resurrection window note a smoothness around the eyes incongruent with the man's chronological history — and the cognition that comes back has been seasoned, by his own admission only under duress, by an indeterminate stretch of subjective time inside Annihilus's holding cycle: killed, regenerated, killed, regenerated, eventually elevated, eventually given an army, eventually a throne, eventually a war. The numbers he has given, in the few moments he has discussed it, are inconsistent — sometimes "weeks," sometimes "I don't want to talk about it" — and the inconsistency is itself diagnostic. He has compressed the period in narrative the way trauma survivors routinely compress.

The first six to nine months back on Earth, by all behavioral indicators, are a man counterfeiting his prior self. He overdoes the smile. He overdoes the entrance. He flies more recklessly than at any point since his early twenties — observers including Spider-Man and the Thing log multiple unnecessary aerial flourishes and one near-collision with a Stark-licensed delivery drone, ostensibly a stunt, almost certainly a test of whether he could still feel anything in the controls. He sleeps in fragments. He keeps the lights on. He cannot stand the cold; the brownstone's thermostat in his suite is logged at 78°F minimum. The shower runs hot to scalding. He eats more than before, even adjusting for metabolic baseline; the additional caloric load goes into ambient warmth-generation, a low-grade unflame thermal halo that is documented in the Future Foundation environmental sensors as a persistent +1.2°C anomaly in any room he occupies for longer than ten minutes.

Recurring, throughout this period: a refusal to take Reed's debriefs seriously. He answers the technical questions, he sits through the medical workup, he submits to the psychic-tampering screening Sue insists upon, and at every point at which the conversation could turn to what the captivity *was,* he produces a joke. The joke is sometimes funny. The joke is, every time, on himself — never on the captors, never on the situation. **He is preemptively diminishing the experience so no one else has to.** That this is the same maneuver his sister used to perform on him as a child — making things smaller so he could carry them — is unlikely to be conscious.

The first sustained intimate relationship of the re-entry period is a brief, badly-judged rekindling with Crystal. The Inhumans are at this point in political flux (pre-Terrigen cloud release), Crystal is widowed-divorced-complicated re: Quicksilver, and Johnny in this window is structurally hunting for the partner who has always represented the safest version of love because her departure is built into the relationship's architecture. They part within months, civilly. Witnesses describe the parting as warm. He flies home alone over the Hudson at low altitude — surveillance footage retained — and lands on the Baxter Building roof rather than enter through the front. He sits, unflamed, for forty minutes before going inside. The behavior is unprecedented in his prior file.

## B. The Fraction Interval and the Slow Power Failure

During Reed's "we're going on a year-long family field trip into the multiverse" decision, the subject's power profile begins to glitch. Brief failures of ignition. Plasma sheath flickering at one-eighth normal intensity. He hides it from Sue and Reed by the most basic available expedient: he does not flame on when they are in the room, and when pressed, he claims to be "saving it for the fight." It is Ben, of course, who notices first; Ben does not say anything to Reed.

The failures are eventually diagnosed as a metabolic mismatch downstream of the resurrection — his body's flame-generation pathway, optimized through millions of subjective combat-hours in the Zone, has overdeveloped to a degree that his Earth-baseline endocrine system can no longer feed reliably. The fix, after several months, is partial. He goes through a period of weeks at one point in which he cannot fly under his own power and is reduced to riding shotgun in the Fantasti-Car like a passenger. The film of him in that car, posture collapsed, hand against the window, is the single most useful piece of body-language intelligence in the file. He does not perform when he believes he is not being watched. He sits like a man much older than the body he is in.

This is also the period in which his relationship with Reed reaches its most strained point in the modern era. The disagreement is not quite an argument — Reed is constitutionally bad at argument — but a sustained, low-grade misalignment around the question of *what to do with Johnny while he is not at full power.* Reed's instinct is to keep him in the Building, to study the metabolic anomaly, to be useful in the lab in some adjacent capacity. Johnny's response is the worst available one: he picks up his old hot-rod from the Glenville storage unit (the car has been kept, lovingly, in trust for sixty publication-years), drives it back to Manhattan, and very publicly takes up the celebrity circuit again. Nightclubs, sponsorships, a brief and embarrassing dalliance with a reality-television production company. The performance is desperate enough that even the gossip press registers something off. He does not let Reed see him land.

## C. The "Death" of the Fantastic Four

The dissolution of the Fantastic Four following Secret Wars is the single most destabilizing event in the subject's adult life, larger in impact than his own death. He has died before; he had not previously lost the unit.

For roughly the publication interval between Secret Wars' close and the FF's restoration, Reed and Sue are believed dead/missing; the children are gone with them; the Baxter Building is sold; the brand is dismantled by Parker Industries; Ben is on a long-term contract with the Guardians of the Galaxy. The subject is, in immediate terms, alone for the first time in his adult life. The Glenville-orphan substrate, which the family had been bandaging for sixty years, is exposed.

His response is two-track and instructive.

**Track one (visible).** He joins the Uncanny Avengers under Steve Rogers' aegis. He performs the role of team flier and morale center competently and with visible effort. He is a good Avenger. He is, by deliberate choice, *not* a leader on the team; he takes a clearly subordinate role under Rogers and later Wilson, and the choice to subordinate is itself unusual for him — it is the man without family seeking a substitute hierarchy, a clear command structure to lean into when his own internal compass has lost the magnet. He bonds, somewhat unexpectedly, with the Wasp. He banters productively with Deadpool. He fights Hydra-Cap during the Secret Empire crisis with conviction. None of this is faked. None of it touches the wound.

**Track two (private).** He becomes seriously involved with Medusa during a stretch in which the Inhumans are reconstructing themselves post-Inhumanity, and then, more durably, with Sky — a newly-Terrigenized Inhuman with solar-plasma-adjacent abilities. The Sky relationship is the most psychologically interesting romantic engagement of his life. She is, for the first time, a partner whose powers are *compatible* with his at a physical level — he does not have to be careful around her, she does not have to fear him, the relationship can include the body. They live together for an extended period at Attilan-in-exile. He is, by every report, content. He is also, by every report, only partly present; Sky is documented at one point telling him, quietly, that she can feel him flying somewhere else even when his body is in the room.

The relationship with Sky ends in the unwinding of the Inhuman political situation — Death of the Inhumans, the murder of much of the royal family, the reduction of Attilan's population, the eventual sidelining of the Inhuman project entirely. Sky survives but the world they had built around them does not. The parting, again, is amicable. He flies back to a Manhattan that does not yet have a Baxter Building to land on.

## D. The Return of the Family — The Slott Period

The reconstitution of the Fantastic Four upon Reed and Sue's return is one of two events in the modern file that produces a documented, sustained spike in the subject's baseline mood. (The other is Franklin and Valeria's reappearance specifically. He sees the children before he sees Reed and Sue, by accident of circumstance, and the recorded reaction — he sits down on the curb and laughs until he cries — is, again, unique in his behavioral history.)

The Slott-era restoration period is, on the surface, a return to baseline operations. Wedding of Ben and Alicia (the *real* Alicia, the original Alicia, the Alicia who is the unresolved geological feature of his life). Johnny is best man. The choice to make him best man is Ben's, deliberate, and is correctly received by the subject as the absolution he had not dared to ask for. Behavioral footage of the ceremony shows the subject holding it together until the moment of the ring exchange and then crying without performance for the duration of the vows. He gives a toast. The toast is short, funny, and ends with the phrase *"he's the best man I've ever known,"* delivered without any winking acknowledgment of the role-title joke. The lack of joke is the signal.

The wedding, however, does not fix the substrate. The subject's powers continue to be intermittently unreliable through this period — a recurring write-down rather than a single crisis, a series of "I can't quite get there today" episodes that he conceals from Reed and discusses, sparingly, with Ben. The Slott run also stages two interlocking developments that should be marked:

**1. The brief alliance/marriage of convenience with the Skrull princess Anaelle / royal entanglement.** Through a combination of diplomatic emergency and the subject's chronic inability to refuse a gesture, he ends up legally bound to a Skrull royal in a politically arranged union. The marriage is not consummated; it is functional, diplomatic, and creates a long-tail problem for him with the Skrull Empire that has not been fully resolved. The fact that he, again, married a Skrull — and again, did not intend to — is the kind of repetition that a file like this is required to flag. He has not, to public knowledge, recognized the pattern aloud.

**2. The reconnection with, and partial reconciliation around, the Lyja material.** Lyja resurfaces in the modern era. Johnny does not run toward her; he does not run away. He speaks with her. He apologizes for things he did not previously know he needed to apologize for. The conversation is, by his standards, an act of staggering emotional maturity. He does not get back together with her. He does not pretend the years did not happen. This is one of the half-dozen data points in the file that suggests the subject is, slowly, growing in a direction the regression-pattern has historically prevented.

## E. The Zdarsky Two-in-One Interlude

During the period before Reed and Sue's return is publicly confirmed, the subject and Ben undertake a journey through the multiverse on the pretext of finding the family. The journey is, structurally, a long conversation between the two of them about grief, with cosmology as the scenery. Surveillance value of the interval is high.

Notable behavioral data:

- The subject lies, sustainedly, to Ben for the duration of the trip — he believes (incorrectly, at the outset) that Reed and Sue are gone, and he conceals this from Ben because he believes Ben cannot bear the loss. **He takes on the burden of Ben's grief preemptively.** The reversal of their lifelong dynamic (Ben as the load-bearing adult, Johnny as the volatile child) is the most significant interpersonal reorganization in the subject's mature history. He is not capable of sustaining it — the lie collapses — but the *attempt* is on the record.
- He demonstrates, in the interval, a sustained operational competence in command roles. He plans the multiverse jumps. He manages resources. He keeps Ben fed and rested. He is, briefly, a person who could lead a team. This capacity recedes after the family is restored; he gives the reins back the moment Reed is available to take them, the way an oldest-child caretaker hands the baby back to the returning parent.
- He experiences, in one of the multiverse stops, an alternate reality in which he never received the powers — a baseline-human Johnny Storm, by every account a lesser man. The encounter visibly destabilizes him. He does not discuss it on return.

## F. The North Run — Current Operational Period

The current era finds the family geographically diffuse by deliberate choice — Reed and Sue on the road, the children with them or in safehouse rotation, the Baxter Building functional but underused. The subject is, at present, in a stable serious relationship with Alicia Masters — *not* the Alicia of his retconned marriage, but a parallel-universe Alicia who was widowed of an alternate Ben Grimm and who arrived in the prime universe under complicated circumstances. He is married to her, or in a partnership treated by all parties as a marriage; the legal status is muddied by interdimensional precedent.

This relationship is the single most consequential development in the subject's adult life that this file is currently tracking.

It is, simultaneously: (1) a final, decades-late closure on the Alicia-Skrull-Lyja wound, the original sin of his adulthood, resolved by the universe handing him an Alicia he is *permitted* to love; (2) the most psychologically loaded romantic choice he has ever made, given that this Alicia carries grief for a Ben Grimm he can never replace and that he is, at some level, marrying his brother's widow in a configuration the multiverse has technically authorized; (3) by every behavioral indicator, working. He is calmer than the file has ever recorded him. He sleeps in a bed for an entire night with regularity for the first time since the resurrection. The thermal halo has receded to +0.4°C. He has slowed his speech by a measurable cadence — observers including Reed have remarked on it, drily, as "Johnny pausing." He has, on at least three documented occasions, been the *first* person at a tactical briefing to suggest a non-combat approach.

The relationship is not without strain. He and Ben have had to negotiate, with deliberate adult care, what it means for Johnny to be married to a woman who wears the face of Ben's wife. The negotiation has been successful; the two men appear, on present evidence, closer than at any prior point in the canon, not despite the complication but because navigating it has required them to articulate love to each other directly, which neither has historically been able to do.

The subject is also, in the current period, taking on a sustained mentor role with several younger heroes — informal, unstructured, characteristic. He has been observed coaching a younger pyrokinetic through ignition control. He has been observed sitting through what amount to office hours for the rotating youth in the Future Foundation. He is, for the first time in the file, occupying the *uncle* role as a primary identity rather than a recreational one. The shift is real.

His combat capability is at or near lifetime peak. The metabolic anomaly has stabilized. The thermal ceiling is higher than pre-death baseline — he has been documented sustaining nova-class output for longer intervals than the historical record contained, an inheritance from the Zone training that he has, finally, stopped pretending not to have. He uses it sparingly. He no longer flame-trails his signature across the sky for civilian audiences without operational reason; the practice, once compulsive, has tapered to occasional and intentional.

## G. Present-State Assessment

The subject is, at the moment of compilation, the most settled he has been in his published life. This is not the same as the most happy and should not be confused with it.

Settled, in his case, means:

- **A primary attachment that does not have departure pre-loaded.** This is structurally novel for him and the system is, slowly, learning to trust it.
- **The family unit intact, geographically loose, communicating regularly.** He calls Sue. The calls are short, frequent, and almost entirely about logistics; the content is irrelevant — the call itself is the message. The pattern is, again, novel.
- **Ben at arm's length and proximate.** The two men live in different cities and see each other weekly minimum. The pranks have not stopped, but their frequency has dropped and their stakes have lowered — a sign of secure attachment, not of cooling.
- **A power profile he no longer needs to perform.** He has stopped showing off the flame and has, correspondingly, become more comfortable not flaming. He has been observed walking, on foot, through Manhattan, for blocks at a time, hands in pockets, unrecognized, by choice.
- **An identity outside the spectacle that he is tentatively occupying.** Husband. Uncle. Mentor. Brother. The roles are not yet load-bearing — pull any of them out and the structure would still wobble — but he is, for the first time, *practicing* them.

Settled does *not* mean processed. The Negative Zone remains undiscussed in any therapeutic frame. The maternal loss has never, in sixty years of recorded interaction, been addressed by the subject in his own voice longer than a sentence. The Franklin-Storm material is sealed; he has not visited the grave in over a decade of in-universe time. The grief is still in the body. The body has merely, finally, found a configuration in which it does not have to scream.

**Vulnerabilities, current.** A loss of Alicia — by death, by departure, by the multiverse reclaiming her — would, on present evidence, produce a collapse of a magnitude the file has never previously had to model for. A loss of Ben likewise. A return to the Negative Zone, in any form, would produce immediate decompensation; the somatic triggers (cold, suffocation, confinement) have not been desensitized, only avoided. A sustained period of solo deployment without family contact would, within weeks, regress him to the re-entry baseline.

**Strengths, current.** Operational courage, fully matured. Combat judgment, sharper than at any prior point. The capacity, demonstrated in the Two-in-One interval, to carry burden silently for someone he loves. The willingness, demonstrated repeatedly in the current era, to *pause.* The presence of a partner who can stand in the flame.

**Trajectory.** The pattern across the prior fifty years was: growth, regression, growth, regression, the regression always slightly less complete. The current period is the first in which the regression has failed to materialize on schedule. The file's working hypothesis is that the integration of the partner has stabilized the system enough that the historical oscillation is, for now, damped. Whether this is permanent or whether it is an unusually long upswing in a lifelong sine wave is not yet determinable. The subject himself, by all indicators, does not know. He is, characteristically, choosing not to think about it. He is, uncharacteristically, not setting fire to anything to avoid thinking about it.

He is forty-something in apparent age, looks late twenties, lives mostly in lower Manhattan, drives the Glenville hot-rod on weekends, calls his sister on Tuesdays, eats four meals a day plus snacks, sleeps approximately six hours, runs a core body temperature of 99.8°F, and laughs more quietly than he used to. He has not died in eleven years. The file will continue.

— END SECTION —


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: JONATHAN LOWELL SPENCER STORM

**File Designation:** UATU/MED/STORM-J/§2
**Cross-reference:** §1 History; §3 Psychological; §4 Psychiatric
**Compilation basis:** Reconstructed from canonical injury record, depicted physiological events, in-frame medical scenes (Reed Richards' Baxter Building infirmary logs being the de facto primary care record for Subject across most of adulthood), and somatic inferences drawn from observable behavior.

---

## I. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE — PRE-MUTATION (BIRTH TO AGE ~16)

### A. Inherited and Congenital

Subject is the second child and only son of Dr. Franklin Storm, M.D. (general surgeon, Glenville, NY) and Mary Storm (homemaker). No documented heritable disease in the immediate paternal line beyond what becomes Franklin's adult-onset alcohol use disorder — itself almost certainly bereavement-precipitated rather than diathesis-driven, but worth flagging as a familial vulnerability the Subject has not inherited behaviorally. Maternal line undocumented in canon; no recorded medical history. The pediatric records were presumably maintained by Dr. Storm personally, a fact that explains the *absence* of an external chart and that has downstream implications: Subject has never had a non-family primary-care relationship in his life.

Birth uncomplicated, by inference (no canon notation of perinatal injury). Childhood vaccinations presumed complete; childhood illnesses of the standard 1950s–60s pediatric profile (varicella, the usual respiratory cycle of a New York exurb child) presumed unremarkable. Subject demonstrates no learning disability, no early speech or motor delay. He is physically forward — coordinated young, an early bicycler, an early swimmer (a detail that becomes ironic after the Negative Zone).

### B. The Defining Pediatric Event

Maternal death by motor vehicle accident at approximately age six. Subject was not in the vehicle at time of impact in any consistent telling; he was, however, present in the immediate aftermath in at least one variant — and regardless of variant, he was a six-year-old who lost his mother suddenly, with paternal culpability woven through the event.

**There is no record of formal grief counseling or pediatric mental-health intervention.** Glenville, 1960s, son of the town surgeon, intact-appearing family-of-origin: this is a child who would have been handed a plate of casserole and told to be brave. The bereavement was managed in the cultural mode of the era and the social class — i.e., not managed. The somatic legacy of this is folded into every subsequent injury Subject sustains; the body that arrives at the cosmic-ray exposure ten years later is already a body that has learned not to display pain.

### C. Adolescent Pre-Powers Profile

By the cosmic flight, Subject is approximately sixteen, athletically built, slightly under typical adult male height (he finishes growing post-mutation, reaching ~5'10"), no record of significant illness or injury beyond the inevitable contusions and lacerations of a teenage hot-rodder. The hot-rodding itself is medically relevant: he had been working with combustion engines, gasoline, oxyacetylene torches in the garage, since perhaps age twelve. He had burned himself on manifolds. He had **been around fire and survived it** in the small mundane ways that condition a body to a fuel. The cosmic-ray event did not introduce him to flame; it married him to it.

No documented substance exposure pre-mutation. No tobacco use. Sexual debut chronologically consistent with peer cohort, undocumented.

---

## II. THE TRANSFORMATION (FF #1, AGE ~16)

### A. The Event

Cosmic-ray bombardment in low Earth orbit, in an inadequately shielded experimental vessel. The exposure was acute, whole-body, and of a spectrum modern medicine cannot characterize because it does not exist in modern medicine. Subject and three companions returned ambulatory but transformed; no formal radiologic workup was performed at any accredited facility, and the subsequent six decades of "follow-up" have been entirely intramural — i.e., Reed Richards' lab.

### B. Acute Phase

Subject's first symptomatic event was spontaneous combustion of his clothing and surrounding ignitable material on the return crash site, followed within hours by deliberate flame-on. The notable clinical detail is **the absence of pain.** Where Benjamin Grimm experienced his transformation as continuous, agonizing alienation from his own surface, Subject experienced his as the discovery of a capacity. This asymmetry is a medical datum, not merely a psychological one: the mutation in Subject's case wired a *reward* response into power expression. Flaming on releases something — endorphin-analog, dopaminergic, or simply the somatic relief of an exothermic outlet for a chronically over-energized system. He has reported, across decades, that *not* flaming on for extended periods feels worse than flaming on. This is the profile of a metabolic dependency on the power state. **The fire is, in a real sense, a medication he secretes for himself.**

### C. Stabilized Phenotype

The transformation, after acute phase, produced:

1. **Plasma sheathing** — voluntary conversion of an envelope of ambient air and emitted bodily output into self-sustaining plasma at variable temperature, ranging from candle-flame (~1,000°F) to, at theoretical maximum (the "nova flame"), in the millions of degrees Fahrenheit. The biological limiter on nova-flame is the metabolic cost: a full nova-burst is, for Subject's body, the equivalent of running a marathon at sprint pace while fasting. He is wrecked afterward — slurred speech, tremor, mild hypoglycemic confusion, days of recovery.

2. **Flight,** via combined thermal updraft and directional plasma jetting. Subject's flight control is intuitive-kinetic rather than calculated; he flies the way a competent driver drives, not the way a pilot pilots.

3. **Pyrokinesis** — projection, shaping, and remote control of flame distinct from his own envelope. Late-era development includes microcontrol fine enough to ignite a single match across a room and to write in fire mid-air.

4. **Thermal absorption** — uptake of ambient heat and combustion energy, with feeding effect (he can *eat* a hostile fire, which is why he is often the correct first responder to industrial blazes).

5. **Elevated resting metabolic rate** — caloric requirements estimated at 6,000–10,000 kcal/day at light activity, 20,000+ on combat days. Subject's relationship to food is therefore not appetite-driven in the ordinary sense; it is fuel-driven. He eats constantly, eats large, eats indiscriminately. He has never had to think about weight, which is among the small mercies of the mutation.

6. **Slightly elevated resting core temperature** unflamed — approximately 100.5–101°F. To touch, he runs warm. Partners across his life have remarked on it (it has, by canon and inference, been one of the small charms and small frictions of his romantic life — pleasant in winter, oppressive in summer).

7. **Accelerated wound healing** — not regenerative on the order of certain mutants, but two to three times baseline. Cuts close in hours, fractures in days, soft-tissue damage in a week where a baseline human would take six. This has produced a clinical pattern in which Subject **systematically underestimates injury severity** because he has learned that he will heal. This habit nearly killed him on at least four documented occasions and has produced cumulative joint and tendon wear that any orthopedist would call premature.

### D. The Vulnerability Inversion

The same mutation that bought him fire took proportionate price elsewhere. Subject is **fully vulnerable, and in some respects supranormally vulnerable, to:**

- **Oxygen deprivation** — flame consumes oxygen; flaming-on in an enclosed or vacuum environment produces rapid hypoxia. Subject has lost consciousness in this way more times than the team has tracked. His asphyxiation tolerance is, if anything, *worse* than baseline, because his powered state pulls O2 he cannot replace.
- **Drowning / immersion** — water snuffs the envelope and renders him a non-swimmer-grade civilian in the water (he can swim adequately, but he cannot fly, and immersion in volume is acutely disabling). Subject's history with Atlantean conflicts is essentially a history of being out-environmented.
- **Cold** — sub-zero exposure costs him disproportionately. He warms himself, but the cost is metabolic, and prolonged cold drains him to collapse.
- **Blunt-force trauma** — no enhancement. He bruises and breaks at the rate of a fit thirty-something male.
- **Suffocation by chemical foam, vacuum-sealing weaponry, and certain Inhuman/alien containment systems** — recurrent operational vulnerability.

The medical translation: **his powers and his weaknesses are the same axis.** What he can do, he cannot have done to him without compounding penalty.

---

## III. THE INJURY LEDGER (CHRONOLOGICAL, BY ERA)

A complete inventory is impossible — sixty-plus years of weekly combat with no centralized chart — but the documentable pattern is consistent enough to allow stratification.

### A. Early Years (Ages 16–22, FF #1 through mid-1960s)

The early file is dominated by **burns from supranormal opponents.** The Wizard's flame-retardant traps, Paste-Pot Pete's adhesives (asphyxiation risk repeatedly), the Sandman's smothering attacks. Notable serious events:

- **Repeated thermal threshold breaches** — facing opponents (Dragon Man, certain Sub-Mariner-deployed devices) whose energy output exceeded his tolerance. Subject sustained second- and third-degree burns on his own body — yes, the fireboy burns — multiple times in the Strange Tales solo period. These healed with minimal scarring due to accelerated healing.
- **Blunt-force concussive incidents** with the Trapster, Sandman, and at least one notable Hulk encounter; multiple mild-to-moderate traumatic brain injuries that in any conventional athlete would have been worked up for chronic traumatic encephalopathy by now. He has never been worked up.
- **Multiple submersions** by the Sub-Mariner with associated hypoxic episodes; the early conditioning of cold/water aversion begins here, layered beneath the later Negative Zone trauma.

He treated these as adventures. The somatic record of the period is of a teenager learning his body by breaking it.

### B. Young Adulthood (Ages ~22–30, late 60s through 70s)

- **Crystal-era injuries** — combat alongside the Inhumans introduced exposure to Terrigen-derived and Inhuman energy weaponry. Several near-fatal events; no permanent sequelae documented but cumulative joint wear continues.
- **The grief presentation after Crystal's departure** — recurrent insomnia, decreased appetite (notable because his appetite is normally metabolic, not psychological — when grief suppresses Johnny's eating, it is a *vital sign* of distress), and a documented uptick in reckless flight incidents. He was not "depressed" in the categorical sense; he was somatizing.
- **Frankie Raye era** — no significant physical injury but the loss-to-Galactus event produced a discrete somatic episode: depicted brief inability to ignite cleanly for several days following her departure. This is the first canonical instance of **conversion-pattern power dysfunction** in Subject, and it is the diagnostic template for every subsequent psychogenic power loss. His powers, in his body, are emotionally regulated.

### C. The Marriage Era (Late 80s — Englehart/Simonson)

The "Alicia" / Lyja period is medically uneventful in the gross-trauma sense but psychiatrically and somatically pivotal in retrospect: he was sustaining an intimate relationship with an organism whose biochemistry was not human. Skrull pheromonal and tactile signaling differ from human; whether this had subclinical effects on his endocrine baseline is unknowable but plausible. More importantly: **for years, he was sleeping next to someone who was not who he believed she was.** The body almost certainly registered cues the conscious mind ignored — Subject was a poor sleeper through this period in inferable retrospect, and the Lyja revelation correlates with a documented several-month stretch of clinical-grade insomnia and reduced flame intensity.

### D. The Nineties

Marked by ill-defined power fluctuations during and after the **Onslaught / Heroes Reborn** displacement — a metaphysical event with somatic consequences. Upon return, Subject reported (canonically and via behavior) brief periods of unstable ignition, intermittent thermal regulation failure (chills, sweats), and the disorientation appropriate to having been alive in a pocket universe and not knowing it. No formal workup. Reed's notes from this period would, in a proper chart, fill a binder.

### E. Civil War Beating (Mid-2000s)

**The single most important non-fatal physical assault in Subject's life.** Outside a Manhattan nightclub, civilian assailants — galvanized by anti-registration sentiment after the Stamford incident — beat Subject unconscious. He was not flamed-on; he was caught between the social-celebrity context (in line at a club) and the costume context. He sustained: orbital fracture, broken nose, multiple rib fractures, concussion of significant grade, soft-tissue trauma extensive. He was hospitalized for an extended period in a coma or quasi-comatose state.

The medical recovery was complete. **The psychological recovery was not.** Subject's relationship to public-facing visibility shifted in this period; he became, briefly, *avoidant* of the celebrity context that had been a load-bearing element of his identity. The avoidance did not last — the screw-up narrative reasserted, the performative bravado returned — but the body retained the lesson. Subject is, since this event, marginally hypervigilant in crowd contexts. He scans rooms now. He did not used to scan rooms.

### F. The Negative Zone Death (FF #587, c. 2011)

The clinical event of his life.

Subject held the Negative Zone portal alone against an Annihilation-Wave force, sustained massive cumulative trauma — burns at last from a true peer-level threat, blunt force, blade injury, eventually asphyxiation in the Zone's atmosphere (which is incompatible with human respiration for prolonged exposure). **Death was multi-causal:** exsanguination from combat injuries, hypoxic crisis, and combat exhaustion. He died.

He did not stay dead. He was resurrected, by canon, via Annihilus's regenerative technology — alien biotech of a kind no Earth physician has ever seen, repeatedly, **and for the purpose of being killed and resurrected again** as a gladiator-warlord captive of the Negative Zone hierarchy. The duration of this captivity (compressed in Earth time) included multiple deaths and multiple resurrections. Subject's body therefore carries, at the cellular level, alien intervention of unknown long-term implication. **A modern surveillance medical workup would flag him as a person of indefinite biological provenance from this point forward.** What Annihilus's machinery rebuilt him *from* is not on any baseline.

The injuries documented in the Negative Zone period — burns, fractures, lacerations, evidence of restraint (scarring at wrists and ankles consistent with prolonged shackling) — are present on his body if examined. He does not allow examination.

### G. Post-Resurrection (2011–present)

- **Persistent insomnia** with characteristic 0300-hour wake pattern (suffocation-content nightmares).
- **Cold-water startle reflex** — a measurable autonomic spike on contact with cold water or sudden cold air. Subject masks this in company; the mask is detectable to those who know him.
- **Episodic ignition failure** — periods, sometimes hours, sometimes days, in which flame-on does not initiate cleanly. These episodes correlate with emotional stressors, not with physiological ones. The body is, again, doing the talking.
- **Photophobia, mild,** in close darkness — a new symptom post-Zone. He sleeps with a low light.
- **Mild claustrophobia, new** — he can tolerate enclosed spaces operationally but he does not voluntarily choose them, where pre-Zone he was indifferent.

### H. Subsequent Era — The FF "Death," Inhumans Period, Uncanny Avengers, Sky

The post-Hickman years through Slott's run involve repeated medium-grade trauma, two further significant power-loss episodes (each producing the by-now-stereotyped identity crisis disproportionate to the physiological event), and continued cumulative wear. The Inhumans period exposed Subject to Terrigen byproducts at concentrations that would have killed or transformed many — his mutation appears to confer some protection against Terrigen response, though the mechanism is unclear and the data is anecdotal. The Sky relationship was, by inference, the most somatically stabilizing of his adult life: better sleep, fewer ignition failures, weight up slightly into a healthier range. Bodies tell on relationships.

---

## IV. SURGICAL AND PROCEDURAL HISTORY

Subject has no canonical surgical history of note **performed by external surgeons.** Every significant intervention has been performed by Reed Richards or by Reed's instrumentation, in the Baxter Building, off any institutional record. This includes:

- Multiple internal-injury repairs after high-trauma events.
- Power-modulation work (the period he was being studied for nova-flame upper limits involved invasive monitoring that in any other context would be classified as surgery).
- The post-Negative Zone debrief, which involved extensive imaging and tissue sampling that Reed has never published.

The implication for a surveillance file is that **the most reliable medical record on Subject is held by a single private individual who is also his de facto father-figure,** which is a clinical and operational singularity.

---

## V. SUBSTANCE HISTORY

Notable for its negative space. Subject is the son of a man who drank himself to manslaughter and prison. Subject runs with the 1980s–90s celebrity-hero social circuit — clubs, parties, the documented Manhattan after-hours life — without developing a substance use disorder. He drinks socially. He has never been shown publicly impaired. He has used no documented illicit substance.

This abstinence is **not abstinence by program or by overt resolution.** Subject has never, in any depicted moment, said "I won't drink heavily because my father did." The avoidance is preconscious — a body-level decision the verbal mind has never had to make. It is, in its own way, the cleanest evidence in the file that Subject has internalized the Glenville injury more deeply than he can articulate. The thing he will not become, he does not become.

Caffeine intake: high but unremarkable in his cohort. Anabolic or performance enhancement: none — he has no need and a temperamental aversion to anything that would feel like *cheating his body.* He is, oddly for a hedonist, somatically conservative about what he puts in himself.

---

## VI. SLEEP, NUTRITION, AND SEXUAL HEALTH

**Sleep.** Pre-Zone: heavy, deep, easy sleeper of the metabolically expensive type — eight or nine hours preferred, rapidly entered, hard to wake. Post-Zone: light, broken, six hours on a good night, with the recurrent 0300 wake and difficulty resettling. He compensates with naps and with the low light. He has never been prescribed a sleep aid because he has never seen a non-Reed physician about it.

**Nutrition.** Caloric volume enormous. Macronutrient preference: carbohydrate-heavy with high fat tolerance; he metabolizes anything. Subject is the kind of eater who orders two entrees and finishes both. He has no food aversions of note except a slight, post-Zone, aversion to certain protein textures associated with the Zone's flora — he avoids without naming the avoidance.

**Sexual health.** Active across decades, by canon and by inference; no documented STI history; the elevated core temperature has been noted by partners. The serial-monogamy pattern (see §3) is the clinically relevant frame here, not the act-frequency.

---

## VII. PSYCHOLOGICAL IMPACT OF THE MEDICAL HISTORY

Each major event reads twice — once in tissue, once in personality:

- **The maternal loss** is the unspoken floor of every subsequent affective response to bereavement. Subject does not grieve in language; he grieves in altitude. Every loss flies him higher and faster.

- **The cosmic transformation** gave him a body that *expresses* rather than *contains* affect. This is, paradoxically, both his great mental-health protective factor (he does not pool poison the way Ben does) and his great liability (he has never developed a vocabulary for what he feels because he has never had to hold it long enough to name it).

- **The chronic underestimation of injury** is a behavioral artifact of the accelerated healing, and it has trained him into a stance toward his own body that is fundamentally unserious. He treats himself the way he treats a car he is confident his mechanic can fix.

- **The Civil War beating** introduced civilian-context vigilance — a small, persistent re-weighting of his social world toward threat.

- **The Negative Zone death and captivity** is the unhealed wound. The insomnia, the cold-water startle, the ignition failures, the photophobia, the claustrophobia — all of it constellates as a PTSD picture that has never been treated and that he refuses to name. He is, on this front, a man with shrapnel he will not let anyone remove.

- **The repeated power losses** function, each time, as enforced confrontations with the question he otherwise outruns: *who am I when I am not on fire?* The fact that the answer is unstable each time is not a failure of character; it is the cost of having been given, at sixteen, an identity that did all the heavy lifting his developmental psychology never finished doing on its own.

---

## VIII. CURRENT MEDICAL POSTURE (SURVEILLANCE SUMMARY)

Subject is, at the moment of this compilation, in functional health. He is undertreated for unprocessed bereavement and partial-criteria PTSD. He is over-reliant on a single non-institutional medical relationship (Richards) that is also his primary parentified bond. He carries the cellular signature of alien resurrection, the cumulative orthopedic and neurologic wear of six decades of unprotected superhuman combat, and an autonomic baseline that has been quietly re-tuned by the Negative Zone toward hypervigilance he does not acknowledge.

He will not see another doctor. He will not be still long enough to be assessed. He will continue to under-report symptoms and to interpret somatic distress as a cue to increase rather than decrease activity. **The medical history is, in summary, a record of a body that has been used to escape a mind, by a man who is loved enough that no one has yet insisted he stop.**

— END §2 —


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: J. STORM

*Classification: Behavioral Surveillance Compendium, Bodily Pattern Index*
*Source basis: Sixty years of continuous observation across canon. Cross-referenced against the developmental and psychiatric workup in the analytical basis. Read this section as the body's testimony — the things the mouth does not say.*

---

## I. BASELINE ANTHROPOMETRICS AND RESTING CARRIAGE

**Build.** 5'10", approximately 170 lbs at the trim end of his weight band, 180 when training is lax. Mesomorph with a swimmer's distribution — long lats, defined deltoid cap, lean intercostals; thighs slightly underdeveloped relative to upper body, a tell that his propulsion is plasma-aided rather than terrestrial. Skin pale-to-fair with a faint persistent sub-flush at the cheeks and sternum, the visible epidermal record of an elevated core temperature.

**Resting temperature.** Surface skin runs 99.4–100.2°F at idle, palms and clavicular hollow warmer than extremities. Anyone who shakes his hand notices the heat for half a second and forgets it. People who hug him notice it longer. Lovers learn to sleep with the window open.

**Resting heart rate.** Mid-50s when truly idle (rare), low 70s in social baseline. Recovery from exertion is anomalously fast — within ninety seconds of cessation he is back to conversational baseline regardless of cardiovascular load.

**Resting posture.** He does not sit *in* furniture; he occupies it. Default seated position is sprawled — sacrum forward on the cushion, one arm draped along the back, the opposite ankle resting on the contralateral knee in the open figure-four characteristic of men trained by adolescence to take up room without apologizing for it. Standing baseline: weight on one leg, hip cocked, the other foot turned out fifteen degrees — a hot-rodder's lean, learned over engines at sixteen and never unlearned. Shoulders set slightly back and down, chest open. He does not slouch except in genuine private fatigue, and then he collapses entirely, head dropped almost to the sternum.

**Carriage in motion.** Gait is light-heeled with a forward weight bias, almost a perpetual half-step toward something. Stride length slightly longer than his height predicts. He bounces minutely on the ball of the foot at the toe-off — a habit indistinguishable from a man about to take flight, which he often is. Arms swing more from the elbow than the shoulder; he does not pump. In corridors he walks the centerline. In crowds he reads gaps before they open and threads them without breaking conversation.

---

## II. THE FACE — STATIC AND IN MOTION

**Facial topography.** Strong zygomatic arch, the smile a four-quadrant production rather than a polite lip-only signal: orbicularis oculi engaged (the Duchenne marker), maxillary canines fully exposed, the slight nasolabial deepening on the left more pronounced than the right — an asymmetric crinkle that photographs well and is the single most reliable feature of his public image. Eyes light blue, set wide, with a low-grade perpetual under-eye shadow from chronic short sleep that he conceals on camera-days and ignores otherwise.

**Brow.** Mobile. Right brow lifts independently — a learned ironic flag deployed in flirtation, deflection, and disbelief. Both brows together hike when genuinely surprised, which is rare; he prefers to *act* surprised even when he is, because the performance is more comfortable than the state.

**Mouth at rest.** Slightly parted, the lower lip carried a millimeter forward of the upper. Tongue habitually rests against the back of the upper incisors; under stress it presses harder, producing a faint thickening of speech he hears in himself and corrects.

**The "tells" — facial micro-expressions, ranked by frequency.**

1. *The half-smile-and-look-away.* When complimented sincerely (rare in his ecology), eyes break contact down-left and the smile reduces to one corner. Embarrassment he cannot acknowledge.
2. *The eyebrow-and-tongue-on-canine flick.* Pre-flirtation tell — happens approximately 0.4 seconds before any opening line.
3. *The jaw-set-and-nostril-flare.* Anger he is choosing not to discharge. Lasts under a second, then dissolves into a wider smile. Witnesses register the smile and miss the flare.
4. *The mouth-corner pull-down-with-blink.* Grief surfacing through the performance. Documented during any mention of his mother, of Frankie Raye, and (post-2011) of the Negative Zone. Almost always followed within four seconds by a deflective joke.
5. *The eyes-closed exhale-through-the-nose.* Forbearance with Reed's monologues. Indistinguishable on camera from contentment; the people who know him know.
6. *The slow blink at Sue.* Concession. The closest thing he has to saying *you're right.*
7. *The lip-bite (lower lip, left side, with the lateral incisor).* Concentration on a non-verbal problem — usually mechanical. Distinct from the flirtation lip-bite, which is centered and softer.

**Eye contact.** Aggressive in flirtation (sustained, with the chin tipped slightly down so the gaze runs through the brow), reduced in conflict with intimates (he will look at Sue's collarbone, Ben's shoulder, Reed's hands before he will look at their eyes when in trouble), unblinkingly direct with children, and *evasive at his own reflection* — he does not linger in mirrors except to perform a check, and the check is rapid, almost defiant.

---

## III. HANDS

**Resting state.** Long fingers, calloused at the pads (engine work, throttle-grips), nails kept short and clean — a vanity, but the nails are also a fire-management consideration; long keratin would scorch first on a partial flame-on. Knuckles unremarkable; no boxer's deformations.

**Habitual gestures.**

- *The mid-air match-flick.* When telling a story, he often mimes the strike of a match — thumb across middle finger, a small ignition pantomime. Frequently he forgets and *actually* ignites a small flame at the thumbnail. He has done this in restaurants, in press conferences, in bed.
- *The thumb-tap on the thigh.* Seated, listening, bored. Tempo correlates inversely with engagement: slow tap = patient, fast tap = about to interrupt.
- *The two-finger temple touch.* Concentration. Lifted from Reed unconsciously decades ago.
- *Hair-push.* Right hand, from forehead back through hair, four to six times an hour at baseline, twenty-plus per hour under stress. The single most reliable somatic stress index he produces.
- *The half-fist-into-palm.* A pre-flame-on physical priming gesture, often performed even when he isn't going to ignite — vestigial readiness.

**Touch patterns.**

- *With Sue:* hand on her upper arm, brief, frequent. Hugs initiated by him are usually one-armed and over before they begin; hugs initiated by her are received with both arms and a closed-eye exhale he is not aware he performs.
- *With Ben:* shoulder slaps, headlocks attempted (and failed), the occasional finger-poke to the chest plate. Physical contact is constant and rough. The single observed instance of a sustained embrace (the post-resurrection reunion) lasted eleven seconds and is the longest documented continuous physical contact between them.
- *With Reed:* almost none. A hand on the shoulder once a year. Reed initiates more than Johnny does.
- *With children:* lifts, swings, the carrying of a child on the hip while continuing other tasks. Hands at the child's back are *flame-suppressed by conscious effort* — there is a faint sub-perceptible cool zone he generates at the contact point. He does not advertise this.
- *With partners:* hands first, mouth second. Initiates intimacy with the palm at the jaw, thumb at the cheekbone, fingers curled at the nape — the same configuration regardless of partner, across decades. A signature.
- *With strangers:* handshake firm, slightly too warm, released a beat early.

---

## IV. VOICE AND BREATH

**Voice.** Tenor with a slight gravel at the bottom. Range about an octave and a half in conversational use. Default volume one notch above the room — he projects without being aware he is projecting. Vowels are East-Coast standard with residual Long Island in *ah* and *aw* sounds (*car, talk*); the regionalism strengthens under fatigue, stress, or proximity to old Glenville haunts.

**Cadence.** Quick-onset, mid-sentence accelerations, full stops slightly abrupt. He does not trail off; he punctuates. Punctuation is often a small gesture or a smile rather than a word. Interrupts intimates routinely, strangers rarely.

**Laugh.** Three documented variants.
1. *The performance laugh* — louder than necessary, head tipped back, sustained two to three seconds, eyes mostly closed. Public-facing.
2. *The real laugh* — quieter, shoulders shake, eyes water at the corners, sometimes accompanied by a single hand-clap or a slap to the nearest available surface (often Ben's arm, who has been the percussion section for sixty years).
3. *The breath laugh* — a single exhalation through the nose, half-smile, no sound. The one he uses when he finds something genuinely funny but is in mixed company or grieving.

**Breath.** Resting breath is shallow and clavicular — a stress-state breath that he has normalized into baseline. Diaphragmatic breathing surfaces only in sleep, in the moments before flame-on (a deliberate deep inhale, audible, ritual), and post-coitally. He sighs less than the average adult male; the affect that would produce sighing is rerouted into motion.

**Speech under state shift.**
- *Calm:* fluid, witty, lightly profane.
- *Flirtation:* lower in pitch, slower, with longer pauses.
- *Stress:* faster, higher, more wisecracks per minute, increased self-interruption.
- *Acute crisis:* the opposite — short declaratives, lower pitch, near-monosyllabic. Operational voice. Family members recognize it as the signal that the performance has stopped.
- *Grief:* near-silence, punctuated by a single bad joke at a wildly inappropriate moment which is in fact the most honest thing he has said all day.

---

## V. THERMAL SIGNATURE AND THE FLAME-ON RITUAL

**The pre-ignition sequence (sub-clinical, two seconds).** A small pre-roll observable to close watchers: weight shifts to the balls of the feet; chin lifts approximately ten degrees; the half-fist-into-palm gesture occurs or is suppressed; inhale through the nose, deep, audible at intimate range; eyes close for half a beat; the verbal cue — "*flame on*" — is delivered at a pitch a third below his speaking voice, almost an exhalation. The verbal cue is **not** thaumaturgically necessary. He still says it. The ritual is for him.

**The ignition itself.** Initiates at the sternum and the palms simultaneously, propagates over the body in approximately 0.3 seconds, settles into a stable plasma sheath at variable intensity. Eyes during sheathed flame are whited-out by glare; expression remains visible to those who know where to look (the brow and mouth-line read through the plasma).

**The flamed-on body.** Posture changes: shoulders rise marginally, hips square forward, hands tend to open palms-down at the sides. The slouch is impossible. The flame disciplines the carriage. He is physically more upright on fire than off it — a fact about him.

**Flame-off sequence.** Faster than ignition (0.1 seconds), accompanied by a brief shiver-shudder at the shoulders that he disguises as a roll-out, and a quick exhale. He is fractionally cold for two to three minutes after extended high-output flame, palms paler than baseline. He does not mention this. He reaches for hot coffee, leans toward sunlight, finds a warm surface to put his hands on.

**Sub-flame habits.** Throughout the day he produces unconscious micro-ignitions: a flame on the thumbnail to light another person's cigarette (he does not smoke himself), a candle-sized flame in the palm when bored in a meeting, the warming of a coffee cup he is holding by a degree or two without comment. The hands like to *do* something. Idle hands ignite.

---

## VI. EATING

**Caloric load.** Estimated 6,000–9,000 kcal/day at non-combat baseline; demonstrably higher during sustained operational tempo. The metabolism is the engine; the food is the fuel; the appetite is a medical fact, not a vice.

**Eating style.** Rapid. Forks loaded fully; chews efficiently but not delicately; can carry on conversation while clearing a plate twice the size of a normal entrée. Holds the fork in the right hand American-style, sometimes switches to a continental grip when in formal settings he wishes to navigate without notice. Drinks water cold, in volume — sub-second swallow rate, can finish a 16-oz glass in three pulls.

**Preferences.** Heavy on protein and carbohydrate, low on greens by inclination but he eats them when present. Pronounced preference for *hot* food — temperature, not spice; lukewarm food displeases him at a low-grade sensory level. Coffee black, frequent, throughout the day. Sweet tooth, suppressed in public, indulged privately — ice cream specifically (the pranks with Ben echo a real preference). Has a documented weakness for diner breakfasts, eaten at 3 a.m., counter seat, no companion.

**Eating under state.**
- *Calm:* lingers, talks more than he eats, asks for seconds.
- *Stress:* eats faster, finishes everything, orders dessert.
- *Grief:* loses appetite entirely for one to three days — diagnostically rare for him and therefore visible. He will pick at food while claiming he ate earlier.
- *Post-combat:* the body demands fuel within twenty minutes. Watch him after a flame-heavy fight: he eats whatever is nearest, standing, without sitting down.

---

## VII. SLEEP

**Architecture (baseline, pre-2011).** Total sleep 5.5–6.5 hours, late onset (1–3 a.m.), late wake (8–10 a.m. when permitted). Sleep latency short — under ten minutes when the day has been physically demanding. Sleeps on the right side, knee drawn up, right arm under the pillow. Snores lightly. Bedroom kept cool; he runs hot enough to be his own heater.

**Architecture (post-Negative Zone).** Total sleep degraded to 3.5–5 hours, fragmented. Sleep onset preserved but maintenance impaired — wakes between 3:30 and 4:30 a.m. with high frequency, frequently in a startled state. Has been observed by partners to bolt upright, sheet pushed off, palms open at his sides as if checking for ignition. Returns to sleep poorly; often abandons the attempt and reads, drives, or flies before dawn.

**Sleep-state physical signature.** Lower jaw drops slightly, mouth half-open, breathing diaphragmatic (the only time it consistently is). Right hand sometimes flexes and releases in a small repetitive motion — the half-fist priming gesture executed unconsciously. Twice-documented sleep-flame events: minor, brief, self-extinguishing; the protective somatic governor that prevents him from igniting his own bedding is one of the more remarkable features of his physiology.

**Dreams.** He does not discuss them. Two canonical instances of him waking and saying nothing about what he saw. The post-resurrection nightmares are inferred from the somatic record — the startle, the cold-sweat, the avoidance of discussing the Zone — rather than from his testimony, because he gives none.

**Naps.** Capable of sleeping anywhere — a Quinjet bench, a hospital chair, a sun-warmed roof. The body is opportunistic about rest because the night is unreliable.

---

## VIII. GROOMING

**Hair.** Worn medium-short, layered, with a side-sweep he maintains via the hair-push gesture. Trims every 4–5 weeks, same barber for years when in New York. Dyed not at all; the blond is native. He notices grays before they're visible and removes them privately.

**Facial hair.** Capable of full beard, rarely worn. Default is clean-shaven; during depressive intervals or post-mission recoveries the stubble accumulates two to four days before he deals with it. The stubble-length is a reliable index of his emotional state to those who know him.

**Skincare.** More than he admits, less than the celebrity profile would suggest. Moisturizer (the heat dries him out), sunscreen (vanity, and a slight residual photosensitivity from the cosmic-ray event). No fragrance — fragrance and flame are incompatible; alcohol-based scents ignite at sub-threshold ambient temperatures around his skin and he learned this once, painfully, in his twenties.

**Wardrobe.** Off-duty preference for fitted T-shirts (cotton, dark colors that hide ash), jeans, motorcycle boots or driving shoes. Owns more leather jackets than is reasonable. Wears a watch on the left wrist — analog, mechanical, set five minutes fast. Wears no rings (he tried once with Lyja; never again).

**Hygiene under state.** Shower frequency twice daily at baseline (the heat makes him sweat, and the sweat carries a faint ozone note he dislikes on himself). During depressive intervals, this collapses to once every two days, and the hair-push gesture intensifies as if to compensate.

---

## IX. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE PATTERNS

**Approach behavior.** Confident, fast-onset, low-stakes-framed. Opens with the eyebrow-and-tongue-on-canine flick, a sustained eye-line, and a question rather than a statement — questions invite participation, statements demand response, and he is a craftsman of the former. Touch escalation begins at the elbow, moves to the small of the back, arrives at the jaw within the first hour if reciprocated.

**Initiation signature.** Palm at the jaw, thumb at the cheekbone, fingers at the nape — invariant across documented partners. The kiss itself begins closed-mouth, soft, slightly too brief, then deepens on the second pass. He likes to be the one who decides when it ends.

**Thermal management in intimacy.** Conscious sub-perceptual cooling of the hands and chest at contact, sustained throughout. Partners report he is "warm but not hot" — the discipline is invisible. Loss of thermal control under arousal is documented in early canon (singed sheets, twice; nothing worse); he learned. He does not flame on during sex. He is, on this question, scrupulous.

**Post-coital pattern.** Diaphragmatic breath; the right arm draped across the partner's chest or waist; eyes open longer than expected, looking at the ceiling, not at the partner; the slow blink. He talks little. He sleeps fast.

**Long-relationship behavioral shifts.** With Crystal, with Lyja, with Sky — a settling of the carriage, less restless gesture, an observable reduction in the hair-push frequency. The body relaxes when the attachment is real. The body also tightens fast when the loss begins; he loses weight in the final weeks of every ending relationship, anticipating the grief somatically before he can articulate it.

**Sexual frequency.** High in young adulthood, moderated in the 30s-equivalent, partner-dependent. Not compulsive. Capable of long stretches of voluntary celibacy in mission-focused intervals; the appetite is not in command of him.

---

## X. MOTOR HABITS AROUND OBJECTS

**With engines.** Hands settle on a car or motorcycle with a possessive intimacy he does not direct at most people. Walks around a vehicle counterclockwise on first inspection, palm trailing along the hood, the door, the rear quarter. Listens to an engine with his head tilted right, ear to the manifold. Diagnoses by sound before sight. The face during this process is the most peaceful face he wears — softer than any face directed at a human.

**With tools.** Confident with hand tools, impatient with diagnostic electronics. Will rebuild a carburetor with focus that would surprise anyone who has only seen him in a press conference.

**With keys, coins, small objects.** Fidgets. A coin walks across his knuckles when he is thinking; a key spins on the index finger when he is waiting. Loses neither — fine motor control is excellent.

**With weapons (non-flame).** Adequate, uninterested. He does not carry. The body *is* the weapon and he has never adjusted to thinking otherwise.

**With phones.** Holds the phone in the right hand, thumbs at it left-handedly when typing — a cross-dominance habit from years of holding something else in the right (a wrench, a steering wheel, a flame). Checks the phone often. Photographs himself rarely. Photographs others, and Ben specifically (mid-complaint), often.

**With doors.** Pushes open with the heel of the palm rather than the fingers. Lets doors close behind him without holding them for follow-on traffic when distracted; holds them ostentatiously when he is performing. The inconsistency is diagnostic.

---

## XI. PUBLIC AND PRIVATE — THE STATE MATRIX

**On camera / in crowd.** Carriage maximally upright, chin lifted, smile in the four-quadrant configuration, gestures larger and slower than baseline for legibility, voice projected. Hair-push frequency suppressed by deliberate awareness. The performance is conscious, practiced, and reasonably sustainable for two to three hours before fatigue cracks it.

**In small social group of friends.** Sprawled posture, real laugh, faster speech, more profanity, increased physical contact with whoever is nearest. The body unspools.

**Alone in transit (flying, driving).** Face neutral or faintly amused; lips slightly moving as he talks to himself, sings under his breath, or rehearses lines. Genuinely relaxed. The body in motion is the body at home.

**Alone, stationary, unobserved.** Rare. When it occurs, the carriage collapses — head down, hands hanging, shoulders dropped, breath audible. He looks ten years older. Within two to three minutes he generates a task — stands, moves, ignites a small flame in the palm and stares at it, finds a reason to leave the room. The unobserved stillness is the state he most reliably escapes.

**Under threat (combat, civilian-protection).** Operational. The face goes still, the voice drops, the gestures economize. The hands open. He becomes spatially aware in a way invisible at any other time — tracks exits, civilians, ally positions, thermal updrafts all simultaneously. The performance entirely ceases. **This is the somatic state in which his family recognizes him most clearly as himself.**

**In intimacy with a beloved partner.** Quietest he ever is. The hair-push stops. The eyes go soft. The voice drops a third. The body finally permits stillness in the presence of another nervous system willing to be still with him.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

## Subject: Jonathan Lowell Spencer Storm

---

## I. The Foundational Wound: What Glenville Built

Every attachment Johnny Storm has ever formed runs through the same narrow door, and the door was installed in a frame house in Glenville, New York, sometime around his sixth year of life. Reconstructing the developmental sequence: a mother present, warm, and (in the consistent family mythology Sue carries forward) the emotional center of the home; a father, Franklin, a surgeon — therefore *competent,* *authoritative,* *the man who fixes things* — until he wasn't; a car crash that killed Mary Storm with Franklin behind the wheel or proximately responsible; Franklin's subsequent collapse into alcoholism; the loan-shark killing; the refused defense; the prison sentence. Johnny does not lose one parent. **He loses both, in quick succession, and the loss of the second is morally contaminated** — his father chose not to fight for him, chose drink over him, chose shame over him.

What remains is a sister roughly twelve years his senior who steps into a role she did not ask for and is not developmentally prepared for, and who performs it anyway, with the over-correction characteristic of a child made into a parent: too vigilant, too rule-bound, too quick to scold, also fiercely loving in a way that does not always know how to be gentle. **Sue raises Johnny while she herself is still being raised.** This is the relational template engine of his entire life.

From this substrate, four bedrock features of his attachment system can be extracted with confidence:

**(1) Primary love objects vanish.** This is not a fear. It is a learned expectation, evidentially confirmed once at age six and again immediately after. Mary did not choose to leave; Franklin chose to leave; the lesson the child's nervous system extracted does not discriminate between cause and intent. The lesson is: *people you love go away, and the going-away is irreversible.*

**(2) The remaining caregiver is also a peer.** Sue is sister-and-mother, an irreducibly compound figure. Johnny therefore cannot cleanly separate fraternal rivalry from filial dependency. Every interaction with Sue carries both registers simultaneously, which is why the smallest correction from her can detonate disproportionate responses and the smallest praise can carry the weight of maternal benediction.

**(3) Authority figures are humiliating.** Franklin was a doctor and became a drunk and a convict. Johnny learned in childhood that the men with credentials and offices and certainty fall, and they fall in ways that take the child's standing in the world with them. This colors his lifelong, ostensibly comic, almost reflexive irreverence toward institutional authority — police, government, military, even Reed when Reed is being most Reed.

**(4) Visibility is safety.** The orphan in the Glenville crowd disappears. The boy with the loud car, the loud jacket, the loudest joke at the table, is *located* and therefore *cannot be lost.* Spectacle, in his nervous system, is an attachment behavior — the equivalent of a baby's social smile, scaled up and weaponized.

These four features, in combination, produce an attachment style that does not map cleanly onto any single quadrant of the standard taxonomy. It is **anxious-preoccupied in its hunger for proximity and reassurance, avoidantly defended in its refusal to articulate emotional need, and disorganized in its oscillation between the two** depending on which danger is more proximate — the danger of being abandoned, or the danger of being seen needing.

---

## II. How He Bonds

Johnny bonds *fast,* and he bonds *bright.* The onboarding ritual for any new person of interest in his life follows a near-invariant sequence observable from Strange Tales #101 through the most recent canon:

**Phase 1 — Hot Approach (minutes to days).** Charm deployed at full power: eye contact held a beat longer than social baseline, the grin that has been a load-bearing facial muscle for sixty years, the small competitive flirtation (with women) or the small competitive ribbing (with men) that frames the encounter as *a game we are already playing together.* The implicit message is: *I have decided you are interesting and the only question is whether you can keep up.* This works because it is largely sincere — he genuinely does find new people interesting — but it is also a maneuver, because by establishing the game he establishes the terms.

**Phase 2 — Premature Inclusion (days to weeks).** The new person is *brought home.* Brought to the Baxter Building, introduced to Ben, plopped down at the Storm-Richards dinner table, told family stories before they have earned them, handed a controller for the video game Franklin Richards is already losing at. Johnny short-circuits the normal cadence of intimacy by importing strangers directly into the family theater. This is partly generosity and partly a stress test: *if you can survive Ben, Sue's appraising eyes, Reed's distracted politeness, and the Future Foundation children climbing on you, you are real to me.*

**Phase 3 — Idealization (weeks to months).** The new person becomes, briefly, *the one.* Best friend ever, woman of his life, partner he was meant for. He talks about them constantly. He restructures his schedule around them. He buys things — not as performance of wealth so much as performance of attentiveness, the small specific gift that proves *I listened when you said.* Crystal in the late 60s; Frankie Raye; "Alicia"/Lyja; Crystal again; Sky. The pattern is identical at the temperature gradient.

**Phase 4 — First Friction.** And then — invariably — the new person does or says or is something that punctures the idealization. They have an opinion he didn't expect. They want something he isn't prepared to give. They want *less* of him than he wants of them, or *more.* The friction is normal; Johnny's response to it is not. He does not negotiate. He **flares** — a small public flare, a joke that lands wrong, a stunt, a flirtation with someone else conducted in the partner's sight line, a disappearance for a night without explanation. The flare is a test: *will you stay through this?*

**Phase 5 — Either Stabilization or Loss.** A small percentage of partners — Ben, Sue, Reed, Franklin and Valeria, eventually Crystal in her mature register — pass through the flare and stay. With them, Johnny settles into a deep, durable, articulate-by-action affection. The vast majority do not pass through, and confirm the original template: *people you love go away.* And he files the confirmation and reaches for the next.

What is worth noting and is consistently underweighted by surface readings: **the bonding behavior is not fake.** Johnny is not running a script in the cynical sense. He genuinely loves quickly. The problem is structural, not moral: he is loving from a position of pre-loaded expected loss, and his entire courtship architecture is engineered to either secure proximity *now* or confirm abandonment *fast,* because the one outcome he cannot tolerate is the slow drift of ambiguity.

---

## III. How He Distrusts

Distrust in Johnny Storm is **late-arriving and disproportionate when it arrives.** He is by default a high-trust operator — he assumes the room is friendly, the stranger is interesting, the new teammate is fine, the partner means what they say. This default is partly temperament (high extraversion, high openness, low baseline neuroticism in the social channel) and partly a defended position: distrust would require sitting with the possibility of betrayal in advance, which would require sitting with the original betrayals, which is the thing the entire personality is engineered to avoid.

So Johnny does not *scan* for betrayal. He absorbs it when it arrives, and then it goes into him like a thorn that does not work itself back out.

The Lyja arc is the controlling datum. He married a woman believing she was his brother-figure's blind girlfriend; she was in fact a Skrull infiltrator who had been intimate with him for months under another identity. The injury he sustains from this is not primarily moral outrage at her. It is **the discovery that his own perception is unreliable** — that he can have lived inside a relationship for a year and not have known whose face he was kissing. For a man whose intelligence is pattern-by-feel rather than pattern-by-analysis, whose cognitive style is intuitive and kinetic, this discovery is metaphysically destabilizing. It tells him his primary instrument is broken. And because Lyja later proves to genuinely love him, the wound cannot even be cleanly metabolized as betrayal; it becomes a permanent, unfileable ambiguity. He has never fully trusted his own read on a romantic partner since. Every subsequent serious relationship contains a small, well-hidden hesitation — a beat where he is checking, not consciously but somatically, *is this real, is she real, am I being shown the actual face.*

When distrust does crystallize against a specific person, the form it takes is **withdrawal of attention, not confrontation.** Johnny will simply stop including the person. They will find themselves not invited, not joked with, not flown past. The freezing-out is silent and total. He does not stage scenes. He extinguishes the channel. This is one of the very few places in his behavioral repertoire where the absence of fire is the signal.

**With institutions, distrust is reflexive and pre-loaded** — police, registration bureaucracies, the press when it turns hostile, corporate boards he sat across from during his failed business ventures. The Civil War assault outside the nightclub crystallized into operating reality a distrust of the *crowd* that had previously been ambient: he learned that the same public that buys his trading cards can put him in a hospital, and the lesson took. Post-Civil War his attitude toward fame is subtly different — still extraversive, still spotlight-seeking, but with a thin new layer of *they could turn* underneath the grin.

---

## IV. How He Betrays

Johnny's betrayals are **never premeditated, almost always relational, and structurally identical across his life.** He does not betray for gain. He betrays because he has reached for comfort and the comfort he reached for belonged to someone else.

The taxonomy:

**Betrayal-by-Substitution.** The Alicia/Lyja marriage is the type specimen. Ben was off-world. Johnny was suffering. "Alicia" was suffering. They consoled each other and the consolation became something else. Johnny knew, at every step of the descent, that he was doing something he should not be doing; he proceeded anyway because the immediate analgesic was too needed to refuse. **The betrayal was not of Alicia; it was of Ben,** and Johnny knew it, and Johnny did it. The retcon does not undo the choice he made in the moment.
