- Affective lability is *humor-mediated and externally regulated,* not the BPD-characteristic minutes-to-hours mood swings.

### 4.4.8 NOT Autism Spectrum Disorder

Trivially disconfirmed by social-cognitive performance (rapid people-reading, flirtation acuity, comedic timing requiring sophisticated theory of mind). Noted only because some surface readings have suggested the mechanical-focus / engine-fixation pattern.

### 4.4.9 NOT a Pyromaniac (ICD-11 6C70)

Worth stating for the record because of the surface joke. Pyromania requires fire-setting *for tension release with affect resolution upon ignition,* outside of instrumental contexts. The Subject's pyrokinesis is *instrumental, integrated into identity, and not characterized


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: JONATHAN L. S. STORM

*Classification: Granular Behavioral Reference, Longitudinal*
*Scope: Sixty-plus years of observed conduct, cross-indexed by state. All observations triangulated to canon; inferential extrapolations marked where the granularity exceeds the panel record.*

---

## 0. PREFATORY NOTE ON OBSERVATIONAL METHOD

The subject is, in operational terms, **easy to surveil and hard to read.** Easy because he is constitutionally allergic to invisibility — he moves on visible vectors, takes the same streets at the same speeds, frequents the same five or six establishments per borough, broadcasts his location to civilian onlookers as a matter of temperament. Hard because the entire surface presentation is a regulated performance, and the diagnostic signal lives in the **micro-deviations from that performance** rather than in the performance itself.

The Atlas is therefore organized by *internal state* rather than by *external setting,* because the same setting will produce wildly divergent conduct depending on which of his two internal narratives is currently load-bearing (cf. Workup §3, *Self-concept*). The reader is advised to read the tells **in clusters of three or more** — any single behavior is ambiguous; clusters disambiguate.

---

## 1. BASELINE / CALM STATE

The subject's *true* calm is rare and easily mistaken for boredom. What civilians and even teammates read as his "default" is in fact a maintained low-level performative idle.

### 1.1 Somatic baseline

- **Resting core temperature** elevated approximately 1.5°F above human norm; palpable through casual contact, noticed by partners during intimacy as "always warm hands," remarked on by Sue across decades.
- **Resting heart rate** observably low for someone of his activity profile; the metabolic engine that fuels the plasma sheath runs efficiently at idle.
- **Constant low-grade fidget.** When seated and unoccupied: rotates a small object in the dominant hand (lighter, coin, ring, screw — whatever is to hand), taps the ball of the foot at roughly 2 Hz, drums fingers on thigh in three-beat clusters. The fidget is **not anxious** at baseline; it is the metabolism asking to be spent.
- **Posture:** open, sprawled, takes more space than necessary. Slouches in chairs with one arm over the back, legs extended. Reads as relaxed; is in fact the postural equivalent of leaving the door ajar — easier to launch from.
- **Eye behavior:** scans rooms on entry in a predictable sweep — door, exits, women, exits — then settles. Holds eye contact longer than American social norm with anyone he is actively charming; **breaks contact early with anyone he respects or fears,** including Reed and Sue when they are about to deliver a correction.
- **Hand grooming.** Touches his own hair an average of once every 90 seconds in social settings — a quick four-finger comb back from the temple. The frequency rises sharply under attention.

### 1.2 Verbal baseline

- Cadence is **quick, declarative, frequently rhetorical.** Speaks in complete sentences but uses sentence fragments as punctuation ("So. There's that.").
- Vocabulary is mid-register, deliberately so. He **dumbs down vocabulary around Reed** as a passive-aggressive tell of resentment, and **smartens it up around women he is trying to impress.**
- Routine verbal tics: opens conversations with "Hey, so —" or "Okay, listen —"; closes them with a deflective "Yeah, no, we're good." Uses "kid" as an address term toward people who are demonstrably older than him (Ben, frequently; civilians; nurses); uses "champ" or "buddy" toward men he is trying to manage.
- **Self-deprecating humor at a stable rate** in calm: one to two beats per conversation. Rate rises with stress (see §2).
- Will not initiate conversation about: his father, his mother, the Negative Zone, Frankie Raye by name (says "Nova" if forced), the period of his marriage to Lyja. Will redirect with a joke if any of these are raised. The redirect-joke is itself a tell of the calm state degrading — see §3.

### 1.3 Habitual routes and rituals

- **Morning, when in residence at the Baxter Building / 4 Yancy / current FF HQ:** wakes late by FF standards (08:30–10:00), takes a shower hot enough to fog the room past the extractor's capacity, eats an enormous breakfast — by surveillance metric, four to six times an average male caloric intake at breakfast alone, weighted heavily toward proteins and simple carbohydrates. Coffee black, never less than three cups. Reads the sports page first, the entertainment section second, the news only if Sue is at the table.
- **Mid-morning departure for a "ride."** Two patterns: (a) the car — a rotating stable of high-performance vehicles, currently and historically including several restored muscle cars he maintains himself in the building's lower-level shop; (b) the flight, which he prefers to take low over the Hudson, banking around the bridges in a fixed pattern that has been clockable to within four minutes for years at a stretch. **Operational note:** the routes are recreational, not surveillance-aware. Subject does not vary them and would be straightforward to intercept by anyone willing to be in the air at 11:00 over Pier 76.
- **Lunch:** taken out, almost never in. Rotating cast of diners and one specific Cuban sandwich shop in the West Village. Tips well, by name, knows the staff.
- **Afternoon:** mechanical work in the shop (cars, bikes, occasionally the FF's smaller vehicles — he is genuinely good at this, the only domain where he can hold sustained focused attention without difficulty); training in the gymnasium, which he treats as social hour if anyone else is present and as genuine workout only when alone; or, if no obligations pull, errands of the kind that produce stories ("I had to go to four places to find —").
- **Evening:** social. The pattern depends on era but the shape is invariant — out, visible, in motion, with people. Returns late.
- **Night:** insomnia (post-Negative Zone, intermittent before, chronic after). Often awake at 03:00–05:00. Surveillance log of late-night activity shows: shop work, solo flying over the city at very low altitude, sitting on the building's exterior with a beverage and watching the river. The sitting-and-watching is the only observable state in which the fidget stops. **This is the closest to a true calm the subject ever achieves, and it occurs only when no one is watching.**

### 1.4 The calm-state tell-cluster

To confirm subject is in genuine baseline calm rather than maintained-performance idle, look for: *(a)* fidget present but slow; *(b)* eye contact relaxed, not sustained; *(c)* humor rate at 1–2 beats per conversation, not higher; *(d)* willingness to be silent for stretches of 8–15 seconds without filling the gap; *(e)* posture genuinely loose, not sprawled-with-tension. The fifth criterion is the hardest to fake and the most diagnostic.

---

## 2. STRESS STATE (subacute, ambient, pre-threat)

This is the most commonly observed state. Mild to moderate stress — disagreement with a teammate, an unwanted journalist, a date going poorly, a Reed lecture in progress, a Sue look from across the room — produces a very characteristic suite.

### 2.1 Somatic stress tells

- **Core temperature rises** measurably; the air around him becomes perceptibly warm within a meter. Civilians describe it as standing too close to a radiator. He is *unaware* this is happening unless someone comments.
- **Fingertips heat first** — partners and Sue have remarked on this for decades. Under stress, his fingertips run hot enough to be uncomfortable to touch. Under heavy stress, he leaves faint scorch marks on paper if he handles it (a tell repeatedly used in canon as a visual signal of him losing composure).
- **Hair touch frequency** rises from baseline ~1/90 sec to ~1/30 sec.
- **Jaw tension** — visible at the masseter. He clenches and releases rhythmically. This is one of the few tells that pre-dates the powers; it is in the Glenville behavior.
- **Increased blink rate** combined with **harder, more frequent swallows.**
- **Hands seek occupation:** if he was fidgeting with a small object, he now turns it faster and switches hands more often; if his hands were empty, they go to pockets or to the back of his neck.

### 2.2 Verbal stress tells

- **Humor rate doubles or triples.** Jokes per minute rises sharply; quality of jokes drops; jokes become more self-directed ("yeah, that's me, screwing up again, classic") and edge toward rehearsed-sounding.
- **Interrupts more.** At baseline he waits his turn; under stress he steps on the ends of others' sentences.
- **Switches to second-person framing** when discussing his own feelings ("you know how it is when you —") — a tell that the affect has become unbearable to own in first person.
- **Use of the word "fine"** rises asymptotically; "I'm fine," "It's fine," "We're fine," "Fine, fine, fine." Each utterance of "fine" past the third in a conversation is a unit of unprocessed distress.
- **Specific avoidant phrases:** "Can we not?", "Drop it," "Moving on," "Next subject," "Tell you what —" (followed by a topic change).

### 2.3 Behavioral stress tells

- **Restlessness escalates:** stands when he was sitting; paces; walks to and from the window; goes to the kitchen or bar for a drink he does not want.
- **Flame-on for minor reasons:** lights the cigarette he doesn't smoke just to light it, ignites a small flame on his fingertip and absorbs it, makes a show of warming someone's coffee. The minor pyrotechnics are **a pressure-release valve,** not showmanship in this register.
- **Leaves the room** on a thin pretext if the stressor cannot be deflected. Common pretexts: "I gotta —," "Just remembered —," "I'll be back."
- **Picks up his phone** and looks at nothing on it. The phone is a portable exit.

### 2.4 The stress-cluster signature

Hot fingertips + jaw clench + humor rate doubled + "fine" said three times + a flame-on for no operational reason = subject is in moderate-to-high stress. Verbal denial of the state is, in this cluster, *confirmation* of it.

---

## 3. THREAT STATE (acute, kinetic, combat or pre-combat)

This is the state the subject is most fluent in and where his behavioral profile becomes paradoxically the most legible. He performs threat the way other people perform smalltalk.

### 3.1 Pre-engagement (the seconds before contact)

- **Postural shift:** weight forward onto the balls of the feet; shoulders drop and roll back once; chin comes up about half an inch. This is consistent across decades.
- **Verbal pattern:** a quip. Always a quip. The quip is *non-negotiable* — he cannot enter a fight silently. The quip serves three functions: (a) it self-regulates by hearing his own voice steady; (b) it signals to teammates that he is engaged and on-line; (c) it places the engagement inside a frame of *play,* which is the frame in which he is most capable.
- **Eye behavior:** locks on the principal threat for approximately two seconds, scans the periphery for civilians, scans for the rest of the team, returns to principal threat. The civilian-scan is automatic and reliable.
- **Flame-on cadence:** there is a characteristic micro-pause — about half a second — between his decision to flame and the ignition. He uses it to inhale. The pause is consistent; an experienced opponent could time it.

### 3.2 In-engagement

- **Movement signature:** prefers vertical engagement, takes altitude immediately, fights from above when possible. Banks left more readily than right (handedness expressed in flight). Closes distance in arcs, not straight lines.
- **Power deployment habit:** opens with mid-range flame bursts, escalates only as needed. Does *not* default to nova-level output — has internalized, over decades, the cost of overkill (Sue's repeated lectures about collateral; the early-career property damage). This restraint is **learned, not native,** and the first thing to degrade under fatigue or grief.
- **Verbal during combat:** keeps up a running commentary, usually directed at the opponent ("Really? That's the plan?"), occasionally at teammates ("Ben, on your six!"), occasionally at himself ("Okay, that hurt"). The commentary is *not* trash-talk in the contemptuous sense; it is **rhythm-keeping.**
- **Reflexive protections:** will fly between an unshielded civilian and any incoming fire without conscious decision. Will fly between Sue and any threat the instant her shield drops. Will look for Ben in his peripheral vision every 6–10 seconds as a reflex; if Ben is out of sight, his combat efficiency drops measurably until contact is reestablished.
- **Use of environment:** reads thermal currents and updrafts on the fly; uses building corners, alley mouths, and rooftops with familiarity. In Manhattan specifically, his fighting is *home-court* — he knows the skyline kinetically.

### 3.3 The fight-where-he-stops-performing

There is a second mode, observed rarely but consistently: when stakes cross a threshold (children in immediate danger, family member down, mass-casualty event imminent), the quip stops. The voice drops half an octave. Output rises sharply. Movement becomes economical. **Eyes go flat.** Teammates have learned to recognize this and stay out of his line. This is the mode in which he held the Negative Zone portal. It is also the mode that costs him afterward; he does not come down from it cleanly.

### 3.4 Tells of imminent over-output

- **Whitening of the flame** from yellow-orange to near-white at the periphery of his sheath.
- **Visible heat distortion** around him at greater than usual radius.
- **Silence** — the running commentary stops.
- A specific phrase, used rarely but consistently across canon when he is about to commit to peak output: a quiet "Okay" said to no one, almost to himself. *That "Okay" is the most dangerous sound he makes.*

---

## 4. INTIMACY STATE

The subject's intimate behavior is the second-best-documented register after combat (extensive panel record across multiple long-form relationships) and is, contrary to the surface read, **more guarded than his public-facing self.**

### 4.1 Approach and courtship

- **Initial approach is showmanship-heavy:** rehearsed openers, a calibrated smile (asymmetrical, left side higher), the practiced hair-comb. He approaches strangers with the confidence of someone who has been told he is attractive his whole adult life and is correct about it.
- **Reads interest fast** — among his genuine social competencies. Disengages quickly and without offense when uninterested.
- **With interested partners,** the courtship accelerates. He moves fast — first date to exclusivity in weeks, not months, historically.

### 4.2 In sustained intimacy

- **Physical affection is high-frequency, low-duration.** He touches partners often — small touches, brief — but holds infrequently. The pattern is consistent with anxious attachment (Workup §3): constant reassurance-seeking without sustained settling.
- **Verbal affection is generous but template-flavored.** Pet names recur across relationships ("sweetheart," "babe," "kid"). Specific, named compliments are rarer and therefore disproportionately load-bearing when they occur.
- **Sleep posture:** sleeps facing the partner, one arm extended, but in his own personal pocket of space — does not entangle. Partners across decades report he runs the bedroom cold (offsets his core heat) and kicks off covers.
- **Vulnerability disclosures** come in a characteristic shape: late at night, prompted by external stimulus (a song, a photograph, a news story), delivered as anecdote rather than confession, broken off with a self-deprecating joke at the moment of greatest exposure. Crystal, Frankie, and Lyja's records all show variants of this pattern.
- **Will discuss with a partner what he will not discuss with siblings:** mother's death, fragments. Father, occasionally. Almost never the Negative Zone. *Never* Sue's frustration with him in detail — he protects her image in front of partners.

### 4.3 Conflict in intimacy

- **Initial reaction:** deflection, humor, attempted seduction-as-resolution. Reliable across all relationships of record.
- **Second reaction (if deflection fails):** anger, brief, hot, expressed through leaving rather than yelling — he goes for a flight. The flight is the same pattern as his late-night insomnia route: low over the river.
- **Returns within hours,** rarely days. Apology is sincere and verbose; tends to over-promise specific behavior changes he does not maintain.
- **Cannot tolerate "we need to talk."** The phrase itself triggers the stress-cluster.

### 4.4 The break

- **Initiates breakups poorly.** Tends to behavior-degrade until the partner ends it, then performs surprise. *Inferential — pattern reconstructed from multiple short relationships in the 90s–2000s record.*
- **When the partner is taken from him by circumstance** (Crystal returning to Attilan; Frankie ascending), the response is acute but compressed grief — visible for hours to days, then submerged. Submerged grief surfaces in the months following as increased recklessness and a new, doomed-from-the-start relationship.

### 4.5 The intimacy tell-cluster

Pet name (template) + touch frequency high + sustained-hold absent + anecdotal vulnerability broken with a joke + sleeping in his own pocket of space = subject is invested but defended. **Watch for the moment the joke at the end of the anecdote *doesn't come.*** That is the first signal of genuine, dangerous depth — historically reached with Crystal once, Frankie once, and Lyja late in their arc.

---

## 5. GRIEF STATE

Grief in the subject is not depressive in presentation. It is *kinetic* and *somatic.* The classical mourning markers are absent or inverted.

### 5.1 Acute grief (the first 72 hours after a loss)

- **Hyperactivity.** Sleep drops to near zero; eating drops to near zero (the metabolic engine continues to burn through reserves, leading to visible weight loss within days if grief is sustained); social engagement rises *paradoxically* — he seeks crowds.
- **Increased pyrotechnic minor-use:** lights and absorbs flames idly, far above stress-state rate.
- **Specific physical posture in private:** observed (rarely, by surveillance through windows of FF residences) sitting on the floor with his back against a wall, knees up, head down, hands clasped on the back of his neck. This is **the grief posture.** It is consistent from Frankie through Negative Zone aftermath. He does it only alone and never for more than a few minutes at a time before standing back up and moving.
- **Verbally:** flat affect in unguarded moments, hyper-performance in guarded ones. The contrast is the tell — if observed only in public he appears manic; if observed only in private he appears catatonic. Either alone is misleading.

### 5.2 Sub-acute grief (weeks to months)

- **Insomnia stabilizes** into the chronic pattern: 2–4 hours of sleep, fragmented.
- **Reckless choice cluster:** an ill-considered relationship begun within ~6 weeks of a loss; a high-risk solo mission undertaken without team coordination; an expensive purchase (a car, historically) made impulsively.
- **Power-output reliability degrades.** He under-shoots more often than over-shoots in this period — the somatic engine is grief-throttled. Has been noted by Sue and Reed across multiple loss cycles.
- **Avoidance behavior:** routes shift away from any geography associated with the lost person. Avoidances persist for months to years. Surveillance of his Manhattan movement patterns shows a "Frankie-shaped hole" in his West Village route map that did not close for over a year.
- **Specific verbal tic:** uses the past tense of the lost person's name correctly and without flinching on the first day, then increasingly *avoids the name entirely* for weeks afterward. Reverts to pronoun-only reference. This is the opposite of healthy mourning, which would re-incorporate the name.

### 5.3 Chronic grief (the layered substrate)

The subject carries multiple unresolved losses concurrently — mother, father (functionally), Frankie, the Negative Zone version of himself, intermittent loss of Sue/Reed during the FF's various dissolutions, the unresolved Lyja complex. These do not present as discrete grief at any given time; they present as the **baseline insomnia, the elevated humor rate, the inability to sit still for more than the late-night river-watching window.** The chronic grief *is* the baseline performance, viewed correctly.

### 5.4 The grief tell-cluster

Weight loss + minor pyro idle + pronoun-only reference to a specific named person + a new relationship started in the last six weeks + a geography of avoidance = subject is in sub-acute grief, regardless of his verbal denial. **He will deny it.** The denial is part of the cluster, not a contradiction of it.

---

## 6. VICTORY STATE

Victory behavior is unexpectedly informative because it is one of the few states in which the performance and the person briefly align.

### 6.1 Immediate post-engagement

- **Whoop, fist-pump, vocalized exclamation.** Reliable across decades. The "flame on" / "yeah!" register.
- **Aerial victory lap:** if airborne and conditions permit, executes one or more loops or rolls. The roll-rate is a rough proxy for the importance of the win.
- **Seeks Ben first** for acknowledgment — within seconds of cessation of hostilities. The seek is reliable enough to be predictive. A nudge, a quip, an extended hand for a high-five or its equivalent. *If Ben is unavailable, seeks Sue. If Sue is unavailable, seeks Reed. If Reed is unavailable, seeks a civilian.* The hierarchy of acknowledgment-seeking is fixed and revealing.
- **Press / public engagement:** if cameras or civilians are present, the showman engages — autographs, photographs, a quote for the reporter. He genuinely enjoys this. It is not entirely a defense; the boy from Glenville likes being seen.

### 6.2 Sustained victory (mission success, multi-day high)

- **Generosity spikes.** Buys drinks for the team, dinners for support staff, gifts (often impulsively chosen) for partners and family. The generosity is sincere but also slightly compulsive — he discharges the elevated affect by spending it on others.
- **Sleep partially improves.** This is one of the few states in which the insomnia eases.
- **Risk appetite rises further.** This is paradoxical — victory does not stabilize him; it accelerates him. The post-win period is statistically when his most reckless choices have been made.

### 6.3 The micro-tell of false victory

When he announces victory but is in fact uneasy about the outcome, the whoop is forced — *


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7
## DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

**Subject:** Jonathan Lowell Spencer Storm
**Observation Frame:** Composite seven-day surveillance pattern, derived from canonical depictions across Strange Tales solo era, Lee/Kirby and Byrne FF eras, Waid/Wieringo, Hickman, Fraction, Robinson, and Slott runs; the post-Negative Zone period; Inhuman vol. tenure; Uncanny Avengers tenure.
**Operational Note:** The subject's life does not partition cleanly into "civilian" and "operational" hours. He is one of the most chronically *available* costumed operatives in canon — there is no off-duty Johnny. There is only Johnny at varying altitudes.

---

### 7.1 — The Macro-Rhythm of a Week

The subject runs on a 24-hour cycle that is **phase-shifted later than the rest of the Baxter Building** by approximately three to four hours. Where Reed Richards begins his lab work between 06:00 and 07:00 and Susan begins family-management functions around 06:30, the subject is rarely vertical before 10:00 absent operational call-out. He is the household's reliable late-shift: the one still awake at 02:00 watching something stupid in the den, the one who answers Valeria's "I can't sleep" knock at the bedroom door, the one whose lights are on when the building's external feeds last sweep before pre-dawn.

A representative untroubled week — meaning a week without a crossover event — distributes roughly as follows: two days of true downtime (largely the weekend, frequently violated), three days of light operational tempo (street-level interventions, photo ops, FF Inc. obligations he resents, brief lab consultations he cuts short), one day of media or sponsorship activity, one day of unstructured social drift (clubs, garage, gym, the city itself). **Stillness is not represented in the schedule.** It is the load-bearing absence. The week is structured to avoid the appearance of any unscheduled hour because unscheduled hours are where the grief lives, and he has known this without articulating it since he was approximately seventeen.

---

### 7.2 — Morning

The subject does not wake easily and does not wake well. He sleeps hot (elevated baseline core temperature, see Medical §2), kicks bedding off in the night, and is often found in a half-twisted top sheet with the comforter on the floor. The Baxter Building HVAC in his quarters is canonically set several degrees cooler than the rest of the residential floor — a concession negotiated with Sue some years ago after a complaint about the thermostat war. Windows cracked even in winter. He prefers a hard mattress and a single pillow; the rest of the bed is decorative or for whoever is currently in it.

**First conscious actions (in order of typical occurrence):**
1. A long, deliberate stretch in bed — shoulders, then hips, then a full-body extension that ends with him reaching toward the headboard. Carry-over from years of athletic conditioning; also a physiological self-check (post-Negative Zone, he runs a wordless somatic inventory before opening his eyes: *all of me here, all of me intact*).
2. A small, controlled flame-on of the right hand only — candle-flame intensity, three to five seconds, eyes still closed. This is a diagnostic ritual and a comfort ritual. After the periods of power-loss (Onslaught, Heroes Reborn, post-resurrection, Inhuman era), this gesture became habitual and has not left him. If it does not ignite cleanly, the day's entire mood shifts.
3. Phone, immediately. Notifications scanned in under thirty seconds; he is a fast, dismissive reader of text. Replies in single-word affirmatives or emoji. He does not read long messages on first pass.

He showers hot enough to fog the room — which, given his thermal tolerance, is *very* hot — and he is in and out in under six minutes. He does not linger in the bathroom. Mirrors are functional, not contemplative; he checks hair and jaw, gives himself the half-second appraisal a fighter gives a worn-in pair of gloves, and leaves. Notably he does not shave every day; stubble appears and disappears in the canonical art with a frequency suggesting a two-to-three-day cycle, with full shave-downs before media appearances.

**Wardrobe deployment** is rapid and follows a clear hierarchy: the unstable molecule undersuit is *always* on under civilian clothing during operational tempo, treated like a paramedic's stethoscope — a piece of professional equipment that travels with the body. Civilian over-layer chosen in under ninety seconds: a denim or leather jacket from a rotation of perhaps six, a fitted T-shirt or henley, dark jeans, boots or low sneakers. He owns suits — several good ones — and wears them under protest for galas and FF Inc. appearances; the jacket comes off first, the tie next, usually before the appetizers.

**Breakfast** is calorically enormous and consistent: four to six eggs, multiple pieces of toast, a pile of bacon or sausage, coffee with sugar (he does not, contrary to the assumption a stranger would make, drink it black — he likes things sweet, a residual childhood tell), occasionally a protein shake on top of it. He eats fast and standing more often than sitting. If the Baxter kitchen is occupied — Ben at the table, Valeria at the counter — he sits. If it is empty he eats over the sink. **He cannot tolerate eating alone in a quiet room.** If forced into one he turns on a screen, any screen, immediately.

---

### 7.3 — Mid-Morning to Midday

If there is no operational call, the subject relocates by 11:00 to one of three reliable nodes:

**Node A — The Garage.** Sub-level of the Baxter Building, his personal workspace, walled off from Reed's labs by a deliberate architectural and psychological boundary. Two to four project cars in various states; a custom-built cycle; tools organized in a system only he understands but that he can navigate blindfolded. The garage smells of grease, ozone (from his own ambient heat baking off), and — characteristically — coffee, because he brings a fresh mug down and forgets it on every available surface. He works on engines with his bare hands and, occasionally, with a precisely modulated micro-flame for cutting or welding — a technique he developed himself and does not document. He talks to the cars. He plays music loud (classic rock, modern rock, occasional unembarrassed pop; his taste is broad and unsnobbish). Time vanishes here in a way it vanishes nowhere else in his life. This is the closest the subject comes to meditation.

**Node B — The Lab, briefly.** Drops in on Reed for ten to twenty minutes, ostensibly to ask a question, actually to confirm Reed is there. Reed answers in three-quarter attention; the subject leaves before the answer is complete. The visit is the point, not the content. He will pick up small objects on Reed's bench, examine them, put them down in the wrong place; Reed has stopped correcting this.

**Node C — The Roof or the Sky.** A flight, usually solo, ostensibly for "patrol" but functionally for the same reason a long-distance runner runs. Altitude, speed, the city under him. Routes vary but tend to favor the Hudson corridor, the Manhattan skyline at mid-rise altitude (he is conscious of FAA pathways and avoids them when in a good mood, ignores them when in a bad one), and a low arc over the harbor. He has a half-dozen favorite perches — building tops where he has landed often enough to know which gargoyles take his weight and which ledges are warm in the afternoon. He never stays still on them for long. Five, six minutes, then up again.

---

### 7.4 — Afternoon

Afternoons are the most variable block. In stable periods, a typical afternoon includes:

- **Training, light.** Not in a formal sense. He does not lift heavy. He does plyometric and combat work — a heavy bag in the residential gym that he hits without flaming on, kickboxing footwork, sparring with Ben on Ben's good days (rare, and ritualized as a controlled mutual provocation: the trash talk is the warmup). His fitness is athletic rather than bodybuilt — the canonical art shows lean musculature, not bulk, because his powers do the work strength would otherwise have to do.
- **FF Inc. obligations.** Phone calls he takes pacing. Meetings he attends in person only when threatened. Email he ignores until it becomes a problem. He is canonically a poor administrator and aware of it; he survives this work by charm and by delegation to whichever assistant currently has the patience for him.
- **Media touches.** Brief interviews, photo calls, a check-in with whichever brand currently sponsors him. He is professional with crews and remembers names — a residual gift from the failed acting period, when he learned the protocol of a set. He flirts with the makeup artist. He flirts with the producer. He does not mean any of it operationally; it is the temperature he keeps the room at.
- **Time with the children.** Franklin and Valeria during the Future Foundation era; the broader cohort of FF kids when in residence. This is the cleanest block of his day. He does not perform with children. He builds things with them, takes them on supervised low-altitude flights (rare and treasured), tells them bad jokes, listens to their explanations of things he does not understand and asks follow-up questions that are sincere. **This is the only context in which the subject reliably stops moving.** A four-year-old explaining a drawing will hold his complete attention for as long as the explanation lasts.

---

### 7.5 — Evening

The day's tonal shift happens around 18:00 and is observable as a slight increase in restlessness. He checks the phone more. He pulls up shirt sleeves and pushes them back down. He passes through the common areas of the residential floor at higher frequency, looking for whoever is around — a check-in pattern Sue has named aloud more than once. **Evening is when the household reconvenes, and the subject's body knows that family-reconvening is the day's load-bearing event.**

Dinner with the family, when it happens, is the high point of his week and he treats it casually so as not to admit this. He sits in the same chair (canonically, to Sue's left across most depicted family meals). He eats fast but stays at the table after he finishes, which is unusual for him — he stays because Ben stays, because Sue stays, because Reed is half-present and half-elsewhere and the constellation is correct.

Three reliable evening modalities follow:

1. **Out.** Clubs, restaurants, friends-of-friends parties, an opening, a fight at the Garden. The subject is a known and welcomed figure in New York nightlife — bouncers wave him in, bartenders know the order (light beers, a specific tequila, sometimes a whiskey he is performing being-the-kind-of-man-who-orders-whiskey by ordering). **He drinks deliberately under his capacity.** This is not noted in canon as a policy but the absence of intoxication scenes across sixty years of published material in a character of this lifestyle is itself the evidence; the unspoken throughline to his father's example is operative whether he names it or not. He leaves clubs earlier than his reputation suggests — typically between 01:00 and 02:00 — and is more often alone at the end of the night than the public mythology assumes.
2. **In, social.** Den, screen on, Ben on the other couch, takeout containers, a game or a movie. Ribbing constant and low-stakes. This is the configuration of the household in its rest state and the one the subject would protect with his life — has, in fact.
3. **In, alone.** Rare and significant. When this occurs, the surveillance log would note: lights low, music on (lower volume than daytime), phone face-down, a book occasionally (he reads more than he admits — pulp, thrillers, the occasional biography of an aviator or racer), a tendency to drift to the window and look out at the skyline for periods of three to seven minutes at a stretch. He does not weep. He does not journal. He stands at the window.

---

### 7.6 — Night and the Sleep Boundary

He does not go to bed at a consistent hour. The range is approximately 00:30 to 03:00, with operational tempo pushing earlier and emotional tempo pushing later. **The single most diagnostic ritual of the subject's daily life is what happens in the last forty-five minutes before sleep.**

He cannot enter the bedroom and lie down. He must transition. The transition takes the form of: a final flight (short, ten to fifteen minutes, low and slow over the city, what a pilot would call a *cool-down circuit*); or a long shower; or — most often — a quiet hour in the garage, doing nothing productive, hands on metal, music low. **The body has to be brought down from operating temperature before it will accept stillness.** This is partially literal (he runs hot and needs to vent) and entirely psychological.

Sleep onset is fast once he commits. He sleeps deeply for the first three to four hours and lightly thereafter. Post-Negative Zone the light period contains intermittent nightmares — content not depicted in detail but inferable: suffocation, cold, the closing of the portal, the period of warlordship he refuses to discuss. He does not call out in sleep. He wakes, often around 04:30 to 05:00, sits up for a moment, sometimes runs the candle-flame diagnostic against his palm in the dark, and lies back down. This pattern has been observed in canon and is consistent enough to constitute a signature.

---

### 7.7 — Habits of Place

The subject has a deep cartographic relationship with New York City. A surveillance map of his movement over a year would show:

- **The Baxter Building** as the gravitational center, with the residential floor, the garage, and the roof as his three personal nodes.
- **A flight corridor over the Hudson** used as his preferred decompression route.
- **Three to five favored diners and coffee places** in the Midtown / West Side area where staff know him and treat his fame as a non-event — he selects for this specifically. He tips heavily and consistently.
- **A garage in Queens** (or, in some eras, a body shop in Brooklyn) where he sources parts and where the mechanics treat him as a peer rather than a celebrity. He visits more often than operational need would justify.
- **The clubs** of the moment — these rotate every two to four years as the city's nightlife shifts; he is canonically current with whatever is current.
- **Yancy Street** — visited occasionally with Ben, and only with Ben; he understands the protocol of it.
- **The roof of the Baxter Building at sunset** — the single most repeated solo location across his canonical depiction. He goes there to look at the city and does not stay long.

He drives when he could fly. The cars matter to him as cars, not as transportation; the driving is part of the having. He owns multiple vehicles and rotates through them by mood. He is a fast driver and a precise one; he has never been depicted in a serious accident at the wheel, which is notable given the family history and almost certainly *not* coincidence.

---

### 7.8 — Habits of Person

**Tics, gestures, small consistencies the file would catalog:**

- The right-hand candle-flame diagnostic, multiple times daily, mostly unconscious. He does it when bored, when nervous, when first waking, when alone in an elevator.
- A two-finger salute or small wave to civilians who recognize him on the street — practiced, friendly, brief, designed to acknowledge without inviting prolonged interaction.
- Running a hand through his hair when nervous, when flirting, when caught out — the most reliable tell. The hair is a barometer.
- Cracking his neck before flame-on in serious combat. A boxer's habit.
- Pacing on phone calls, never sitting.
- Reaching for his phone in any silence longer than fifteen seconds.
- Touching Sue on the shoulder or the top of the head when passing her in the kitchen — affectionate, habitual, the gesture of a younger sibling who has done it for thirty years.
- Punching Ben in the upper arm at greeting, hard enough to be felt, not hard enough to provoke. The dosage is precise and developed over decades.
- A small two-finger gesture at Reed in passing — half-salute, half-acknowledgment, the gesture of a son to a preoccupied father.
- A specific hand-sign with Ben that dates to childhood-of-the-team and that closed the Negative Zone portal in FF #587. He has not used it casually since the resurrection; its weight has changed.
- Cracking jokes within ninety seconds of entering any tense room. The timer is reliable enough to set a clock by.
- A specific small intake of breath before he flames on for the first time after a power-loss event — half wince, half held question — that has been depicted in the art of every writer who has put him through a power-loss arc.

**Clothing and grooming consistencies:** the unstable molecule undersuit always within arm's reach if not worn. Sunglasses kept in a jacket pocket, deployed on rooftops and in press scrums alike. A wristwatch — he wears one despite the phone, an analog tell from the gearhead identity. Cologne used sparingly. Cologne and aftershave both have a *cool* note rather than warm — he gravitates to mint, marine, citrus rather than musk or smoke, the unconscious correction of a body that already smells faintly of ozone and combustion.

**Eating consistencies:** sweet over savory in beverages, savory over sweet in food. Burgers, steak, breakfast foods at any hour. He does not cook beyond eggs and toast. He orders the same thing from his three or four favored takeout places, every time, and would not be able to tell you what was on the rest of the menu.

**Sleep consistencies:** as above; sleeps hot, sleeps light, runs the dawn diagnostic without naming it.

---

### 7.9 — Operational Tempo Overlay

The above describes the substrate. Onto it must be overlaid the operational reality: roughly two to four call-outs per week of varying severity, with major crisis events (cosmic, dimensional, Latverian) occurring on an irregular but predictable seasonal rhythm. **The subject's daily routine collapses gracefully into operational tempo.** This is one of his strongest professional traits and an underappreciated one. He is the team member most often "ready in three minutes," not because he is more disciplined but because his civilian life is structured to require almost nothing to suspend. He has no spouse to call, no children to arrange, no project that cannot wait. Crystal, Frankie, Lyja, Sky — each of these relationships was canonically strained by exactly this: the readiness was the marriage.

In active operations he eats more, sleeps less, and stops bothering with the transition rituals. He sleeps in the unstable molecules. He showers at the Baxter and drips on the floor. Post-operation, the rituals resume in reverse — the cool-down flight, the garage hour, the slow re-acquisition of the apartment as a place rather than a barracks.

---

### 7.10 — What a Week of Surveillance Would Conclude

It would conclude that the subject **never stops moving**, that **the motion is the point**, and that **the rare moments of stillness — the roof at sunset, the window after midnight, the dawn diagnostic, the silent stretch before opening the eyes — are the moments where the actual person is observable.** It would note that the public persona is impressively consistent across contexts: the same jokes land the same way in the Baxter kitchen and in a Midtown club. It would note that the differential between his energy in a crowd and his energy alone in his apartment is large and instructive — larger than for any other member of his household.

It would conclude that he is, in operational terms, **astonishingly easy to locate** (he is almost never hidden, almost never dark, almost never silent) and **astonishingly difficult to predict**, because his decisions are heuristic and rapid and his routes are improvised at the second-by-second level. He follows patterns of *place* and *time*; he does not follow patterns of *intention*.

It would note that the single rhythm he protects above all others is **the proximity rhythm of the family unit** — that whatever else is varying, he tends to be in the building when Sue is in the building, in the den when Ben is in the den, in Reed's lab doorway once a day whether or not he has reason to be. The week of surveillance would record many things. The recurring datum it would record most often is this: the subject orbits.

— END SECTION 7 —


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*UATU Dossier, Subject: Jonathan Lowell Spencer Storm*
*Section 7 of the relational mapping. Sources: full published canon, internal cross-reference to Sections 1–5.*

The subject's relational architecture is built on an unstable foundation: a dead mother, a disgraced father, an older sister conscripted into parenthood, and — across the gap of the Origin Event — a non-biological brother who became the most important sustained attachment of his adult life. Every romantic, professional, and team-based bond Johnny forms afterward is a derivative of these primary structures. The blueprint is here.

---

## 7.1 — MARY STORM (Mother, deceased)

**Status:** Deceased c. when subject was approximately six years of age, motor vehicle accident, Glenville, NY. Driver/circumstances vary by era but the constants are: violent, sudden, vehicular, the father present, alcohol implicated.

**Direct memory:** Limited and unreliable. Subject was pre-latency at time of loss. Canonical fragments suggest perfume, a particular song hummed at bedtime, a kitchen, a soft-handed correction style — but these are reconstructed-memory artifacts as much as recalled ones, the kind of detail a child rebuilds out of a sister's later anecdotes and a single surviving photograph kept on Sue's dresser through three apartments. The subject does not, in any depicted moment across sixty years of canon, *spontaneously* mention his mother. He responds to her name when others raise it; he initiates her name effectively never.

**Dynamic, as inferable:** She was the warm parent. Franklin was the impressive parent. When she vanished, the warmth vanished with her — and the impressive parent collapsed within months, so the subject's developmental experience is a *double bereavement compressed into one calendar year.* The lesson encoded by that compression: *love is structurally fragile, and the loss of one love object destabilizes all the others.* This is the most important single sentence in his psychological record.

**Evolution:** None. The relationship is frozen. She is the unchanging referent against which every later female attachment is unconsciously measured for resilience: *will this one disappear too?* The answer, in his romantic history, is **yes, every time** — partly because he selects for it.

**Trust/safety:** N/A — the relationship is purely historical. But note the operational displacement: Sue inherits the maternal slot at the cost of the sibling slot, and the mother's *function* never gets re-filled. Johnny has never had a stable adult female caregiver who was not also his sister.

**Failure mode:** Hers — death. His — refusal to mourn aloud. The unprocessed grief is one of the two largest reservoirs of buried affect in him (the other being the Negative Zone period).

**Leverage:** Substantial but delicate. A hostile actor invoking the mother's name, particularly in a context that implies he has forgotten her or failed her, produces a stillness in him that is uncharacteristic and brief — the *only* reliable circumstance under which the subject goes quiet. Operational note: any attempt to weaponize this would meet immediate Sue-mediated response, as Sue's protectiveness around the maternal memory is one of the few things that overrides her own judgment.

---

## 7.2 — DR. FRANKLIN STORM (Father)

**Status:** Deceased (Skrull-related sacrifice in early canon, FF #32, 1964, sliding-scale notwithstanding). Pre-death status: convicted felon, ex-surgeon, alcoholic, absent for the entirety of subject's adolescence.

**History.** Pre-mother's-death: brilliant surgeon, respected in the community, the kind of father who could fix anyone except himself. Post-mother's-death: alcoholic, dispossessed of his practice, brawler. Kills a loan shark — depending on era, a man who came to collect on debts Franklin had run up drinking. Refuses adequate defense at trial. Goes to prison. The subject is, at this point, perhaps seven to nine years old. The pattern Franklin models for him: *grief is a thing that ends you; the man who feels too much loses his license, his children, his freedom.* This is the negative template the subject organizes his adult coping around.

Franklin escapes prison once or twice in early canon, surfaces in his children's lives in conditions of crisis, and ultimately dies in a Skrull-related sacrifice that is narratively framed as redemptive — he saves Reed (or Sue, depending on retelling) from a Skrull device. The subject is present for at least one of the reunions and for the death.

**Dynamic.** Three-layered:
1. *The pre-loss father* — the imagined good father, half-remembered, half-mythologized by Sue's account. The subject's surviving image of him is the surgeon-father, hands skilled, voice steady.
2. *The shame-father* — the drunk, the convict, the man who was not there. This is the father the subject actually lived with developmentally. The shame is not the subject's; the shame is the *example.*
3. *The redemptive-death father* — the late-canon revision in which Franklin proves he loved them after all by dying for them. This is the version the subject most clings to, because it permits the other two to be reconciled as *a man who was overwhelmed but never stopped loving.*

**Evolution.** From idolization (pre-mother's-death) through abandonment (early childhood) through avoidance (adolescence — the subject does not visit the prison) through complicated grief (Franklin's death) into a permanent **ambivalent reverence** in adulthood. The subject keeps no photograph of Franklin on display in any depicted living space. He does keep, in the FF-era Baxter Building suite, a small medical text on a shelf — Franklin's, by inscription. He has never been depicted opening it.

**Trust/safety.** Catastrophically low in life, retrospectively rehabilitated by the death. The operational consequence: *the subject does not trust male authority that drinks.* He is sober-coded in every era — social-drinker tolerance, no canonical intoxication on-panel, no bar-haunting in the manner of Tony Stark or Jessica Jones. This is not random. This is the one place where Franklin's example produced a corrective rather than a wound.

**Failure mode.** Franklin's: total collapse under grief. The subject's mirroring failure mode is *the opposite extreme* — he refuses to collapse, refuses to slow, refuses to be seen sitting still with a feeling. Both are dysregulation; they merely point opposite directions on the same axis.

**Leverage.** Moderate. A hostile actor explicitly comparing the subject to his father — *you'll end up like him, drunk and useless* — produces an immediate volatile reaction (likely a strike, certainly a flame-on). Note this is one of the few insults that bypasses his humor defense entirely; he cannot joke about Franklin. He can joke about everything else, including his own death. He cannot joke about Franklin.

**Latent thematic content.** Reed Richards occupies, structurally, the redeemed-father slot — brilliant, distant, occasionally absent, sober, dependable, the man Franklin should have been. The subject's deference to Reed is partly father-hunger displaced onto an available father-figure. See §7.5.

---

## 7.3 — SUSAN STORM RICHARDS (Sister; functional mother; teammate)

The single most important person in the subject's life across all sixty years of canon, by every measurable index — frequency of appearance, depth of mutual obligation, capacity to alter his behavior, capacity to wound him.

**History.** Approximately eight to ten years his senior, depending on canonical telling. Already adolescent at the time of their mother's death; functionally adult by the time of their father's imprisonment. She raises him. This is not metaphor. She arranges housing (initially through extended family in Glenville, eventually through a series of arrangements Reed Richards begins quietly subsidizing in the months before the space flight), she manages the household finances, she signs the school forms, she sits through the parent-teacher conferences where the teacher reports that Johnny set something on fire (a recurring datum even *pre*-Origin), she enforces bedtimes, she negotiates the high-school principal's office.

She is also, simultaneously, his sister — playing card games, sharing meals, fighting over the bathroom, the ordinary sibling material. The two roles are not partitioned. They interleave constantly. This is the structure that produces his lifelong idealize-and-defy oscillation: she *is* both, and he reacts to *both* without ever cleanly separating which Sue he is responding to in any given moment.

**Granular behavioral patterns observed across the canon:**

- He uses her full name — "Susan" — when he is being sincere or apologizing; "Sue" in every other register; never "Suzy" or any diminutive (a contrast with Reed, who has been depicted using "Suzie" rarely and tenderly). The naming pattern is consistent across decades.
- He cannot sleep on a couch in a room if she is awake nearby — he gravitates toward her; the body wants proximity to the parental presence even when the conscious mind is rebelling.
- He defers to her in domestic decisions (housing, family routine) and ignores her in operational ones (mission tactics) — a precise inversion of how he relates to Reed, where he defers operationally and resists domestically.
- When she is wounded in combat, his power output spikes measurably; multiple canonical sequences depict him exceeding his usual thermal output specifically in moments where Sue is endangered. His unconscious is wired to her vitals.
- He has, on at least three depicted occasions across the runs, brought her tea unprompted when she was distressed — a small, specific, repeated gesture, the kind of inherited domestic ritual that has the fingerprint of their mother on it.

**Dynamic.** Love braided with chafing, as noted in §5, but the more precise mapping:

- *Idealization layer:* She is, in his eyes, the perfect one — the moral center of the family, the team's actual strongest member, the person whose approval most matters. He says this aloud almost never; he demonstrates it constantly through deference under pressure.
- *Rebellion layer:* She is also the only person whose authority he experiences as *parental,* and so he rebels against her with the specific resentment of an adolescent — the property damage, the unwise relationships, the public stunts are partially performances directed at her: *see me, scold me, prove you're still watching.* The acting-out is attachment-seeking.
- *Sibling layer:* Underneath both, there is a genuine sibling bond — they share a private vocabulary, family-of-origin jokes that no one else in the room gets, a way of looking at each other when Reed begins a long explanation that is *the* shared shorthand of their childhood survival.

**Evolution.** Over the runs:

- *Early era (1961–1970):* she is unambiguously his guardian, scolds him every issue, intervenes when he is reckless. He resents and adores.
- *70s–80s:* she becomes mother to Franklin Richards, which destabilizes the dynamic — the subject is no longer her only "child," and his attention-seeking briefly intensifies before he matures into the uncle role (see §7.6).
- *90s–2000s:* a flatter dynamic; she is exasperated rather than scolding. He has become predictable to her. He notices, and it stings.
- *Hickman / FF #587 era:* his death is the only event that meaningfully *changes* her register toward him. After his return, she handles him more gently, more aware that she might have lost him; he experiences this gentleness with a complicated mixture of relief and grief at what it cost to earn.
- *Post-FF "death" / Inhuman / Uncanny Avengers era:* extended physical separation from her is one of the most destabilizing periods of his adult life; the canonical detail that he loses his powers during the separation and only fully recovers them after the family's reunion is not coincidental.
- *Modern era:* a settled, weary, deeply loving sibling adulthood. He still chafes; she still corrects; they have learned to do both without escalating.

**Trust/safety.** Total. There is no information he would not give her under duress; there is no decision she could ask of him that he would refuse if she truly insisted. This is not always to his benefit — her judgment is overwhelmingly sound, but on the rare occasions she has been wrong (instances of her own corruption-by-cosmic-force, or by Doom-influence), he has followed her because following her is older than thinking.

**Failure mode.** Her over-correction; his under-resistance, then sudden over-resistance. The pattern: she manages him too closely, he tolerates it for an extended period, then explodes disproportionately, then apologizes, then resumes tolerating. Across decades, this oscillation has a roughly six-month-to-two-year periodicity in any given run.

**Leverage.** *Sue in danger* is the master override key for the subject's entire personality — see §5. Beyond that:

- Sue's *disappointment* (cold, articulated, sustained) is one of the few sanctions that produces behavioral change in him. Reed's disappointment is more disabling in the moment; Sue's is more enduring in effect.
- *Threats to Franklin or Valeria* operationalize through Sue — protecting her children is the cleanest path to predicting and channeling his behavior.
- A hostile actor attempting to drive a wedge between them would have to fabricate an attack on Sue's *children* and frame the subject as responsible — the only configuration of falsehood that could meaningfully fracture them, and even then, briefly.

---

## 7.4 — BENJAMIN GRIMM (Brother-by-Origin; the not-blood brother)

The most important love of the subject's life that is not romantic and not Sue. The fraternal pair-bond with Ben is the structural backbone of his adult identity, and the entire psychological complex around it — the pranks, the marriage to Alicia, the FF #587 sacrifice, the hand-sign through the portal — is, taken together, the longest sustained relational arc in his canon.

**History.** They meet pre-Origin: Ben is Reed's college roommate and friend, an older man-of-the-world who becomes adjacent to the Storm household through Reed's courtship of Sue. The subject, as a teenager, idolizes Ben in a specific way — Ben is *cool* in a working-class, ex-pilot, Yancy Street register that is foreign to Glenville suburbia and electrifying to a fatherless adolescent boy looking for masculine models that aren't Reed (too cerebral) or Franklin (too broken). The pre-Origin Ben is the model.

The Origin Event transforms Ben into the Thing and traps him in that form. The asymmetry — Johnny ecstatic, Ben in agony — is established in the first hour and is the gravitational center of every subsequent interaction between them. The subject knows, at some preconscious level, that he got *the gift* his brother got the curse version of. The guilt this generates is the unspoken substrate of every prank.

**Dynamic.** Pranks-as-language. This needs to be understood operationally:

- The subject pranks Ben with a frequency, persistence, and specificity that exceeds any other recurring behavior in his canon. Ice cubes in the shower, chili peppers in the meatloaf, "Aunt Petunia" gags, modifications to Ben's motorcycle, exploding cigars, replaced toothpaste, fire-shapes spelling insults outside Ben's window at 2 AM. The repertoire is vast and inventive.
- Ben's responses are predictably explosive: clobbering threats, chases through the Baxter Building, occasional successful retaliation (Ben's revenge pranks tend to be cruder and more physical — dumping the subject in the East River, that sort of thing).
- The function: *each prank is a probe. Are you still here? Are you still you? Are you still my brother?* And Ben's reliable rage is the answer: *yes, still here, still me, still your brother.* The exchange regulates the subject's anxiety about Ben's stability and presence.
- Ben understands this. There is canonical evidence — quiet moments, in late Slott and Hickman material especially — where Ben acknowledges he could end the pranks by simply not reacting, and chooses not to, because the exchange regulates *him* too.

**The Alicia/Lyja arc as the central wound.** Treated in §1, but the relational analysis: the subject's marriage to "Alicia" while Ben was off-world is the single largest violation of the fraternal bond in their shared history. Even with the Skrull retcon, the in-character experience is that the subject chose his own comfort over Ben's claim. Ben forgives him — this is the controlling datum — but the *forgiveness is not closure.* The wound has a permanent character. In every depicted interaction post-revelation, there is a half-beat in Ben's responses to Johnny on certain topics (Alicia herself, marriage, the question of who gets to be happy) that was not there before. The subject is aware of the half-beat. He flinches from it.

The Alicia arc is, psychologically, the subject's own self-confirmation of the *"I am the screw-up the family carries"* narrative (§3). It is the piece of evidence he cannot dismiss. Reed's lectures he can shrug off; Sue's corrections he can rebel against; his own marriage of his brother's girlfriend is a fact he has performed on, and it is in his file forever.

**FF #587 as the counterweight.** The hand-sign through the closing Negative Zone portal is the precise inverse: the moment in which he chose Ben's life over his own with no hesitation, no performance, no audience but Ben. The two events — the Alicia marriage and the FF #587 sacrifice — together form the relational dyad's two poles: the worst the subject ever did to his brother and the best. Ben holds both. So does the subject.

**Evolution.** From hero-worship (pre-Origin) through guilt-laden mutual antagonism (early FF era) through deepening adult fraternity (70s onward) through the Alicia rupture and reconciliation (late 80s–90s) through the FF #587 sacrifice and resurrection arc (2010s) into a current state of weathered, mature, openly affectionate brotherhood that still expresses itself in the pranks because the language never changed even as the meaning matured.

**Trust/safety.** Total in the operational and emotional sense; *guilt-mediated* in the moral sense. The subject would die for Ben without hesitation and has. He would also, given the Alicia precedent, not entirely trust himself around something Ben loves if Ben were absent and the subject were lonely. The asymmetry is in his own self-assessment, not in Ben's trust.

**Failure mode.** His: choosing his own emotional comfort over a clean read of his brother's interests, then performing remorse without changing the underlying impulsivity. Ben's: holding the rage too long before discharging it (the subject is a relief valve for Ben's frustration about the Thing-form, and overuse strains the relationship).

**Leverage.** Enormous.
- *Ben in danger:* overrides judgment in a register slightly different from Sue-in-danger — with Sue, the response is focused and surgical; with Ben, it is broader and more reckless, because Ben-in-danger reactivates the original Origin-Event guilt.
- *Ben disappointed in him:* the single most reliable behavior-modifier in the subject's life, more effective than Reed's disappointment, more enduring than Sue's. A hostile actor capable of credibly representing Ben's contempt could induce significant impairment.
- *Threats to Alicia* (in any continuity): activate both Ben-protection circuits and Alicia-guilt circuits simultaneously; volatile, unpredictable, likely to produce maximal-output response.
- *Mockery of the pranks, framed as evidence that the brothers do not actually love each other:* small leverage point, but real — the subject is privately defensive about the pranks because he half-suspects they are inadequate substitutes for the conversations he cannot have.

**Protective function.** Ben is the subject's external emotional regulator and has been for sixty years of canon. The subject's affect is more stable in Ben's presence than in any other person's, including Sue's. Operational implication: if the subject is in crisis and unreachable, Ben is the access vector.

---

## 7.5 — REED RICHARDS (Brother-in-law; functional surrogate father)

**Structural position.** Reed occupies the slot Franklin Storm vacated, with the modifications appropriate to a redeemed-father figure: brilliant rather than broken, sober rather than alcoholic, *intellectually* absent rather than *physically* absent, dependable rather than catastrophic.

**History.** They meet through Sue. Reed is the older, brilliant, faintly remote man courting his sister. The subject's adolescent reception of Reed is mixed — admiration plus mild resentment plus the relief of a household with an adult male presence in it again, even an intermittent one. Reed urges the unsanctioned space flight that produces the Origin. Reed is, in that sense, the proximate cause of the subject's powers and Ben's transformation; the subject does not hold this against him (Ben sometimes does, in difficult moments). The subject's reaction to the Origin is to *thank Reed in effect*, by his delight in the new body.

**Dynamic.** A father-son relationship managed through humor on the subject's side and benign distraction on Reed's side. Specifically:

- The subject deflects Reed's lectures with jokes that Reed registers without quite engaging — Reed is not a man who duels in wit; he absorbs and proceeds.
- The subject defers to Reed operationally (mission tactics, strategic planning) almost without resistance, in a way he does not defer to Sue. Reed's authority feels *paternal-legitimate* in a way Sue's authority feels *parental-imposed.*
- The subject brings mechanical problems to Reed — vehicle issues, equipment questions — in part because they are actual problems and in part because the question is the pretext for the presence. The subject can sit beside Reed in a lab for hours longer than he can tolerate any other still environment, because the still environment contains Reed.
- Reed, for his part, treats the subject with a slightly absent fondness, occasionally rises to genuine paternal warmth in crisis, and is responsible for at least three of the canonical interventions that saved the subject's life or sanity (Negative Zone resurrection work, post-Onslaught recovery, multiple power-restoration efforts).

**The unspoken triangulation with Franklin Storm.** The subject has never overtly compared Reed to his father — he does not have the introspective vocabulary, and the comparison would require him to acknowledge his hunger. But every operational marker shows the displacement: the sobriety-coding, the deference to brilliance, the way he watches Reed's hands when Reed is working (Franklin was a surgeon; the subject's reverence for adult male hands doing precise work has an origin), the tolerance for Reed's absences (he learned, at six, to tolerate adult male absence).

**Evolution.**
- *Early era:* mild adolescent resentment, played for comedy.
- *Middle eras:* stable son-figure deference, with periodic challenges to Reed's leadership that are clearly bids for paternal recognition more than actual policy disagreements.
- *Hickman era:* maturing equality; the subject is taken more seriously as an operational adult by Reed in this period than ever before, and visibly grows under the regard.
- *Post-resurrection / FF "death" / modern era:* the subject's most painful extended separation from any family member after the FF disbanded; Reed's absence in this period reproduces, in adult life, the original paternal absence, and the subject's coping (Uncanny Aveng


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

**Scope note.** This section excludes blood-and-bonded primaries (Sue, Reed, Franklin and Valeria, the late Franklin Storm Sr., romantic partners) — those are mapped in Relationships I and III. What follows is the broader concentric architecture: the man Johnny calls brother in every way except biology; the chosen kin who arrived through the Fantastic Four's adjacency network; the surrogate fathers who filled the Franklin Storm vacancy in operational, intellectual, or moral registers; the lateral peers and running mates; and the small but consequential roster of those he has actively mentored. Each entry is mapped in the same architecture: provenance, dynamic, longitudinal evolution, trust/safety profile, predictable failure mode, and exploitable leverage.

---

## 1. BENJAMIN J. GRIMM ("BEN") — THE BROTHER, THE BALLAST, THE EXTERNAL REGULATOR

**Provenance.** Pre-dates the cosmic flight. Ben enters Johnny's life via Reed in the late 1950s — first as Reed's college roommate and pilot of record, then as the recurring adult man around the Storm household during Sue and Reed's courtship. By the time of the FF #1 flight, Ben has known Johnny for years as a teenage punk with a wrench in one hand, has flown the boy in light aircraft, has been the only adult male presence in Johnny's orbit who was not a teacher, a cop, or absent. Ben is the man who was already there when the mother died was old news and the father in prison was a fact, not a fresh wound.

**Dynamic.** This is the central non-romantic relationship of Johnny's life and the closest he comes to a steady-state emotional climate. The surface presentation — sixty years of pranks, ice cubes in the bed, exploding cigars, fake telegrams, the recurring matchbook-in-the-fingers gag, the time he set Ben's newspaper on fire while Ben was reading it, every iteration of the unicycle and pie-throwing escalations — is *attachment ritual,* not aggression. Johnny pokes Ben because Ben is the only object in his world guaranteed not to vanish when poked. Ben's roar, Ben's chase, Ben's "I'm gonna clobber ya, matchstick" — these are *emotional weather Johnny can predict,* which is the single rarest commodity of his childhood. The pranks function as a continuous low-grade test: *is the brother still there? yes. is he still the same? yes. am I still safe? yes.*

Ben, for his part, is one of the very few people who reads Johnny accurately. He knows the pranks are not cruelty. He plays his role — outraged, threatening, never actually retaliating with the full force he could bring — because at some level Ben understood, very early, that he is the boy's regulator. There is a recurring panel-type across decades: Johnny goes too far, Ben actually gets quiet, and Johnny *instantly* drops the performance and apologizes. Quiet Ben is the only sanction that lands.

**Evolution.**

- *1961–1965.* The relationship is established in its mature form almost immediately. Johnny is sixteen-to-eighteen, Ben is mid-thirties, the asymmetry is wide. Ben tolerates and grumbles; Johnny escalates and grins.
- *Late 60s–70s.* Begins to mature on Johnny's side as he hits his twenties. The pranks thin slightly; the underlying loyalty surfaces openly in crisis (the Galactus arc, the Negative Zone incursions of the period).
- *Late 80s — the Lyja/Alicia catastrophe.* The single greatest rupture. Johnny marries the woman he believes to be Ben's blind sculptor partner while Ben is stranded off-world. Whatever Johnny's internal justification (genuine bonded grief, mutual belief that Ben might be dead, "Alicia"'s active pursuit), the act registers in Ben as the deepest possible betrayal by the only person who couldn't betray him. The breach takes years to scab. Even after the Skrull retcon — *it was never Alicia* — Ben does not fully forgive immediately, because what mattered was not the woman but Johnny's *willingness.* This wound is the only one of Johnny's life that he has never been able to talk his way out of, and the silence around it is itself diagnostic. Decades later it remains a faintly live wire; certain looks from Ben still shut Johnny up mid-sentence.
- *2000s.* Re-stabilization. The dynamic returns toward the pranks-and-loyalty equilibrium but with a thicker substrate. They now openly love each other in ways the younger versions could only express through provocation.
- *FF #587 (2011) — the controlling datum.* Johnny dies holding the Negative Zone portal so Ben and the children can live. The final exchange between them is a *hand-sign through the closing door* — silent, intimate, unmistakable. After sixty years of words deployed to avoid feeling, the truest thing Johnny ever said to Ben was said without speaking. This is the moment the entire dynamic resolves to: every prank a deposit in the account, every match-flick a confirmation that he was there. The withdrawal is paid in full.
- *Post-resurrection.* Ben is the first person Johnny seeks and the last person he can lie to. The Negative Zone PTSD presents to Ben before Sue, because Ben does not require Johnny to perform recovery in order to be loved.
- *Post-Hickman through present.* The relationship is the most stable load-bearing element of Johnny's adult life. They have lived together, fought together, mourned the same losses (Reed and Sue's "deaths," Franklin's various crises), and Ben has stepped in repeatedly during Johnny's identity-crisis periods (the Inhuman exile, the brief Uncanny Avengers stint) as the one phone call Johnny will actually answer.

**Trust/safety.** Maximum on both sides. Johnny will say things to Ben — about the Negative Zone, about his father, about Lyja, about Frankie — that he will say to no one, including Sue. The constraint is not capacity but format: Johnny cannot deliver any of it sober and seated. It arrives sideways, mid-other-task, mumbled, deflected, then dropped. Ben has learned to receive it that way.

**Failure mode.** Johnny will, under acute distress, do something that hurts Ben specifically because Ben is the safest target — the one whose love will survive the wound. The Alicia marriage is the archetype; smaller versions recur (publicly humiliating Ben in front of a date, leaking embarrassing footage of Ben in a club incident, agreeing to a public stunt that exploits Ben's appearance). Each occurrence is a regression to the adolescent pattern under stress he cannot otherwise discharge.

**Leverage.** *Ben's quiet disappointment* is the single most effective lever on Johnny Storm that exists in the universe. Louder than Sue's correction, deeper than Reed's distance, more disabling than any villain. A hostile actor who could engineer Ben's sincere disapproval — without Johnny knowing it was engineered — could derail him for weeks. Conversely, *threat to Ben* will override every other consideration on Johnny's threat-stack including direct threat to Sue if forced to triage (a hideous and unspoken truth Johnny would deny if asked).

---

## 2. ALICIA MASTERS — THE LIGHTHOUSE, THE BRIDGE, THE PERMANENT APOLOGY

**Provenance.** Enters via Ben in FF #8 (1962). Stepdaughter of the Puppet Master. Blind sculptor. Becomes Ben's partner, the moral center of the apartment, and within a year of her introduction has functionally become the Fantastic Four's chosen sister and de facto aunt to the Storm children.

**Dynamic.** With Alicia, Johnny is at his most consistently *small-voiced.* The flirt does not deploy; the showman holsters. She cannot see the costume, the smile, or the smoke; she hears only the voice. Johnny — who has spent his life optimizing every visible surface — speaks to Alicia in a register he uses with almost no one else: slower, less embroidered, occasionally tender. She is the first adult woman in his life (Sue does not count; Sue is structurally parental) who consistently *receives him* without correction or expectation of spectacle.

**Evolution.**

- *1962 through mid-80s.* Beloved older-sister figure. Johnny is open with her in a way he is open with almost no one; she is a permitted confidant for romantic distress (Crystal era specifically — Alicia's blindness made her safe to cry near).
- *The Englehart era — the catastrophe.* He marries her, believing her to be Alicia, while Ben is off-world. The marriage is — in Johnny's experienced reality — a real marriage to a real woman he had loved as family for two decades. The transgression is total: against Ben, against the unspoken architecture of the chosen family, against his own self-image as the loyal one inside the unit. The retcon (it was Lyja the entire time) salvages the in-fiction Alicia but does not — *cannot* — undo what Johnny did *believing* she was Alicia. He chose his comfort over Ben's claim. The shame is permanent.
- *Post-retcon to present.* The recovered Alicia returns. Johnny's interactions with her are perceptibly altered: more deferential, more careful, slightly avoidant of physical proximity, almost never alone with her without Ben in the room. He has not forgiven himself, and her grace toward him reads — to him — as charity he has not earned. The dynamic is now permanently asymmetric: she has moved on; he has not.
- *2010s–present.* Alicia is godmother-adjacent to the Storm-Richards children and remains structurally inside the family. Johnny's loyalty to her is absolute and silent. He will defend her physically without hesitation and emotionally with a ferocity disproportionate to provocation — overcorrection for the original sin.

**Trust/safety.** Asymmetrically high — Alicia trusts Johnny fully; Johnny does not fully trust himself with Alicia and never will again. There is no aperture for self-forgiveness here, partly because Ben has never explicitly closed the wound and Johnny will not ask him to.

**Failure mode.** Avoidance under emotional pressure; Johnny will physically leave the room rather than have a direct one-on-one conversation with Alicia about anything weighty. He will also, predictably, *over-praise her work* and *over-perform protection of her* in ways that are themselves slightly performative — the apology that cannot stop apologizing.

**Leverage.** Any reference to the marriage, even oblique — a Skrull joke, a wedding-ring detail, a passing mention of "the years Ben was off-world" — produces visible micro-flinch. A sophisticated adversary who placed Johnny in a scenario where he had to *choose between* protecting Alicia and protecting Ben would extract operationally significant cognitive collapse.

---

## 3. CRYSTALIA AMAQUELIN ("CRYSTAL") — THE FIRST GREAT LOSS, THE RECURRING WHAT-IF

*(Crystal occupies a hybrid position: romantic partner historically, but in her long post-romantic phase she has been chosen-extended-family — sister-in-law to Quicksilver, mother of Luna, queen-figure to the Inhumans, and one of the very few peers who knew Johnny at eighteen and still knows him now. Her current standing in his life is more kin than lover, with the romantic substrate dormant but never extinct.)*

**Provenance.** Enters in FF #45 (1965). Inhuman royal, elementalist. Johnny's first serious adult-shaped love.

**Dynamic.** With Crystal, Johnny is — uniquely — the one *trying.* The relationship is the first time the showman puts down the act long enough to court someone in good faith. The early panels are notable for *Johnny listening,* a behavior he displays rarely and never for long with anyone else.

**Evolution.**

- *Late 60s.* Intense, sincere, mutual. He is happier in this period than the canon will permit him to be again for a long time.
- *The loss.* Terrigen sensitivity / Inhuman political necessity forces Crystal back to Attilan. Johnny — for the first time on record — does not perform through a breakup. He goes quiet. He flies less. Sue notes (panel-explicit, multiple issues) that something is wrong with her brother.
