- (H) Aerial stunts performed when civilians are visible below — barrel rolls, signature flame trails (his initial — the "4" — names spelled in flame). The stunts are calibrated for an audience and are markedly reduced when alone.
- (M) Periodic low-altitude check-ins on people he cares about — a slow pass over Ben's neighborhood, over a partner's window, over a hospital where a friend is admitted. Will not land, will not be seen entering — but the eyes confirm.
- (M) Lands on rooftops to sit, sometimes for 20–40 minutes, without doing anything. One of the few stillnesses he tolerates, because the height and the city below constitute *visibility* — he is being seen by the skyline.
- (L) Patrols looking for trouble. The hunter mode is not native; predict not.

### 4.2 Comms Discipline

**GIVEN:** Team channel open, low-tempo day.

**EXPECT:**
- (H) Chatter-heavy. He fills the channel. The chatter is partly social need, partly battlefield-grooming — keeping the team's voices alive in his ear.
- (M) Misses one in five briefing details on first pass; recovers them through inference under pressure. Predict Sue or Reed repeats key data for him under the cover of repeating it "for the room."
- (M) Uses callsigns/nicknames more than legal names on open channel — affection-and-cover habit.
- (L) Goes silent on channel for extended periods voluntarily. Predict only when grieving or post-traumatic; the silence itself is a diagnostic signal.

### 4.3 Vehicle and Equipment Habits

**GIVEN:** Ownership of personal transport and gear.

**EXPECT:**
- (H) Owns a motorcycle currently. Maintains it himself. The maintenance is one of the few channels in which his attention is sustained and meditative.
- (H) Tinkers with engines without being asked, on Reed's projects and his own. Predict surveillance shows him in a garage/hangar in a non-trivial fraction of his unaccounted hours.
- (M) Loses small items at a high rate — keys, sunglasses, phones (frequent replacements), wallet. Compensates with redundancy.
- (M) Treats the uniform as work clothes — utilitarian, not sacred. Will joke about it, redesign it, complain about it. Will also defend its symbology if anyone outside the family mocks it.
- (L) Carries a concealed sentimental item. Predict yes — something small, in a pocket or wallet, that has been with him for years. Likely candidates: an item of his mother's (worn lettering, a small charm), a Glenville-era keepsake, a photograph not visible to others. Surveillance should look for it.

### 4.4 Money

**GIVEN:** Financial behavior in non-crisis periods.

**EXPECT:**
- (H) Spends freely, saves poorly. Income from FF royalties, endorsement deals, and the family's collective wealth covers the gap. Predict a recurring undercurrent of administrative chaos around personal finance — late bills, surprise tax issues, intermittent CPA changes.
- (H) Generous spontaneously — picks up tabs, sends gifts on impulse, donates to a cause that touched him that week. The generosity is sincere and unstrategic.
- (M) Susceptible to a bad investment pitch from someone he likes. Predict at least one ill-conceived business endeavor per decade (the canon record bears this out).
- (L) Negotiates aggressively for his own compensation. Predict not. He underprices himself in solo deals and overprices on behalf of the team.

### 4.5 Media Consumption

**GIVEN:** Downtime.

**EXPECT:**
- (H) Streams. Heavy on action, comedy, racing, motorsports, mixed martial arts. Light on prestige drama unless a partner has put it on. Re-watches comfort films.
- (H) Scrolls. Phone in hand for non-trivial portions of any unsupervised hour.
- (M) Reads — comics, magazines, the occasional motorcycle or car publication. Long-form prose only when injured and bedbound. Predict a stack of unread books gifted by Reed or Sue with the spines uncreased.
- (M


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

**Classification:** Behavioral Forecast, High-Stakes Decompensation Edge
**Subject:** Jonathan L. S. Storm
**Method:** GIVEN → EXPECT pairs derived from longitudinal canon, with confidence weighting and granular behavioral signature (somatic, paralinguistic, tactical). Each forecast specifies the **trigger class**, the **wound being touched**, the **first-thirty-seconds behavior**, the **first-thirty-minutes behavior**, and the **aftermath signature** where the data supports it.

This section maps the edge — what Johnny does when the performance fails. It is the inverse of the public file. The public file is the flame; this is what the flame burns to hide.

---

## A. CRISIS — IMMEDIATE THREAT, FAMILY-ADJACENT

### A1. GIVEN: Sue takes a hit, visibly hurt, in his field of view.

**EXPECT:** Immediate hard override of any current tactical plan, including plans Reed has explicitly issued thirty seconds prior. He will *go to her,* not to the threat. The plasma sheath will surge involuntarily upward in temperature — registerable on thermal optics as a sudden 30–40% intensity bloom before he has consciously decided anything. Voice drops register; the patter stops mid-sentence. The word "Sue" — not "Susan," not "sis" — comes out at a volume calibrated for a six-year-old's room, not a battlefield. If she is conscious, he will make a joke within ninety seconds of confirming she is stable; the joke will be slightly off-timing and he will not notice. If she is unconscious, he will not speak at all until she wakes, and he will not leave her line of sight even when ordered. **Wound touched:** maternal-loss substrate; Sue is the surviving caregiver and the structural mother. Threat to her is threat to the only continuous attachment of his life. **Confidence: very high.** **Aftermath:** he will not mention the moment again; he will, for 48–72 hours, be physically closer to her than usual — finds reasons to be in the same room, the same kitchen, the same hallway. Pattern documented post-every-Sue-injury arc since 1962.

### A2. GIVEN: Ben taken out of the fight, visibly.

**EXPECT:** A different and more violent signature than A1. He does not go to Ben — he goes at whatever did it. Plasma temperature spikes past safe-discharge thresholds within ten seconds. Profanity (rare in baseline; specific in crisis) appears. The taunts vanish. He will pursue the responsible party past tactical sense and past terrain — into water, into vacuum, into enclosures he should not enter. **This is the most dangerous Johnny gets, period.** Ben-threat overrides Negative-Zone-trauma avoidance: he will go into the dark, into the cold, into the suffocating space, *to get to whoever hurt Ben.* **Wound touched:** the Alicia/Lyja shame stratum compounded with the unspoken knowledge that Ben is his only chosen sibling and the Alicia marriage already cost him a portion of standing in that bond. Any further loss of Ben is loss of his last chance to make that wrong right. **Confidence: very high.** **Aftermath:** insomnia for the duration of Ben's recovery; he will sleep in a chair in the medical bay if permitted, on the floor if not.

### A3. GIVEN: A Future Foundation child, or any child, in immediate harm.

**EXPECT:** Thermal threshold ceiling lifts. He will burn past the temperatures at which his own regeneration can keep pace — has done so, will do so again. He becomes verbally calm, almost flat, in a register no other circumstance produces in him. He talks to the child as he extracts them in the cadence of a man reading a bedtime story. **Wound touched:** the orphan-self in Glenville; the child in front of him *is* the child he was, and he will not let that child stand where he stood. **Confidence: maximal.** **Aftermath:** physical exhaustion disproportionate to the engagement; will eat 8,000–12,000 calories within four hours; will check on the child repeatedly over the following weeks under increasingly thin pretexts.

### A4. GIVEN: Reed incapacitated, mission ongoing, no one else senior present.

**EXPECT:** He will take command, and he will do it badly in the first ninety seconds and competently thereafter if Ben is present to anchor him. His first instinct is to defer to Ben; if Ben defers back, he occupies the role with visible discomfort that he masks with sharper-than-usual humor. He will not call it "command"; he will call it "okay here's what we're doing" and refuse the formal vocabulary. **Wound touched:** the failed-leadership history (Fantastic Four Inc., the Reed-absent runs) and the screw-up narrative. Each command instance is a referendum on that narrative for him, whether the situation merits the weight or not. **Confidence: high.** **Aftermath:** if it goes well, he will not claim credit and will be unusually quiet for 24 hours. If it goes badly, he will go missing — physically leave the Baxter Building for a night, not say where, return with no explanation.

### A5. GIVEN: Civilian mass-casualty event, fire-coded, in his AO.

**EXPECT:** The clowning evaporates inside two seconds. He becomes a triage instrument. Voice flattens, sentences shorten to three-to-five words, he runs a mental grid that surprises everyone who has only seen the patter. He will absorb ambient combustion — pull heat *out* of structures — at risk of metabolic overload, because the people inside are the priority and his own ceiling is negotiable. **Wound touched:** counterphobic mastery of the element that took (in some tellings) his mother. Every fire he stops is a small inversion of Glenville. **Confidence: maximal.** **Aftermath:** quiet for hours; will find one survivor — usually a child or an older woman — and stay with them at the hospital until family arrives.

---

## B. THREAT — DIRECTED AT JOHNNY HIMSELF

### B1. GIVEN: A pyrokinetic adversary at or above his thermal ceiling.

**EXPECT:** Counterphobic engagement. He flies *toward.* The taunts will be sharper and more personal than against non-fire opponents because the fire-on-fire encounter is, for him, a mirror engagement and the mirror is not allowed to win. He will attempt to absorb the opponent's flame — this is the move he reaches for under fire-stress — and will overextend doing it. **Wound touched:** the territorial integrity of the only domain in which he is unambiguously sovereign. **Confidence: very high.** **Aftermath:** sleeps poorly for several nights; checks the news for similar power signatures with a frequency he would not admit to.

### B2. GIVEN: Water-based or asphyxiation-based attack (Atlantean, submersion trap, vacuum exposure).

**EXPECT:** Spike in startle response, brief freeze of 0.3–0.8 seconds before action resumes — the freeze is post-Negative-Zone and is new since the resurrection arc; pre-2011 Johnny did not freeze. After the freeze, motor response is faster than baseline and tactically degraded — he fights to *escape the medium,* not to defeat the opponent. He will accept a worse strategic outcome to get above the waterline / out of the enclosure / back into open air. **Wound touched:** the manner of his death in the Zone — suffocation, dark, alone, surrounded. The body remembers what the mouth doesn't say. **Confidence: high.** **Aftermath:** nightmares, three to seven nights. Will run hotter than usual at rest; Sue will notice; he will deny.

### B3. GIVEN: Confinement — cell, restraint, sealed room, especially with sensory deprivation.

**EXPECT:** Initial humor (jokes about the accommodations, the décor, the host) as standard deflection. At the four-to-six-hour mark, the humor breaks and is replaced by escalating attempts to burn out — not strategically calibrated, *compulsively* calibrated. He will attempt thermal breaches he knows have low probability because the doing is what regulates the panic. If the confinement extends past 24 hours, expect dissociation: he will talk to people who are not there (Ben, in the documented post-Zone material; sometimes his mother — extremely rare, extremely diagnostic). **Wound touched:** Negative Zone captivity; the warlord period he refuses to discuss. He was confined for what to him felt like a substantially longer subjective duration than the calendar shows. **Confidence: high.** **Aftermath:** he will avoid the cell-block / containment area of the Baxter Building for weeks; will refuse to participate in any subsequent operation requiring infiltration of a holding facility unless Ben is on the team.

### B4. GIVEN: Public humiliation — beating in front of a crowd, broadcast defeat, on-camera embarrassment by an antagonist.

**EXPECT:** Disproportionate response on a delay. In the moment, the public-facing mask holds; he will quip through bruises and exit with apparent grace. Within 48 hours, expect a private rematch attempt undertaken without telling the family, undertaken at a tactical disadvantage, undertaken to settle the *image* rather than the threat. **Wound touched:** the Civil War club assault and, beneath that, the showman's nightmare — visibility weaponized against him. To be seen failing is, for the boy whose safety has always been visibility, a categorical inversion. **Confidence: very high.** **Aftermath:** if the rematch fails, withdrawal for 3–10 days; if it succeeds, he will never speak of it and will be unable to enjoy the result.

### B5. GIVEN: Power loss, abrupt, of unknown duration.

**EXPECT:** Identity-collapse signature. First 24 hours: denial, repeated attempts to flame on, escalating frustration, claims that he's "just tired." 24–72 hours: depressive withdrawal incommensurate with the medical event, refusal of social contact outside the family, return to the hot-rod / mechanical hobbies (the pre-powers compensatory domain — engines are what he had before fire). 72 hours onward: either resignation-as-mask (taking up some external identity-prop — a job, a relationship, a costume change) or volatile re-engagement (picking fights he cannot win, drinking more than he otherwise drinks — note: never to dependency, but observably above baseline). **Wound touched:** the load-bearing function of the powers for identity. Without the fire he is the Glenville boy again, and the Glenville boy has no defenses. **Confidence: maximal — documented across Onslaught, Heroes Reborn, post-resurrection, Inhuman runs.** **Aftermath upon power return:** disproportionate joy, brief manic-flavored period, increased recklessness for 1–2 weeks as he over-uses the restored capacity to confirm it is real.

### B6. GIVEN: Direct lethal threat to himself, family not in the equation.

**EXPECT:** He is *less* afraid than baseline. The threat to himself alone is the easiest threat for him to process — he has died, the act of dying did not break him, and his self-regard is, despite the bravado, not the value he prioritizes. He will engage with something close to relief that the stakes are clean. **Wound touched:** none, in the way you'd expect. The exposed datum here is the inverse: the absence of fear-of-self-loss is itself a sign of how thin the self-investment is beneath the performance. **Confidence: high.** **Aftermath:** none notable.

---

## C. BETRAYAL — TRUST-OBJECT VIOLATION

### C1. GIVEN: A romantic partner revealed as deceiving him (identity, allegiance, motive).

**EXPECT:** The Lyja template will re-activate. First response: denial, demand for re-confirmation of the evidence, a request to hear it from her. Second response: not anger — *grief,* presenting as quiet, sustained, and uncharacteristically articulate. He will absorb the betrayal *into the screw-up narrative* rather than externalize it ("of course, I picked her, I always pick like this") — this is diagnostically the wrong move; it deepens the wound rather than dispersing it. He will not seek vengeance. He will fly alone, at altitude, for hours. **Wound touched:** Lyja, layered over Frankie, layered over Crystal, layered over the foundational expectation that love disappears. Each new betrayal adds to the pile and confirms the structure. **Confidence: very high.** **Aftermath:** a fast, ill-considered rebound within 3–8 weeks. The rebound partner will share at least one structural feature with the betrayer (Inhuman; alien; secret-identity; emotionally unavailable). He does this without seeing it.

### C2. GIVEN: Ben learns something Johnny did and does not immediately forgive.

**EXPECT:** The single highest-leverage scenario in the file. He will attempt humor; it will fail; he will attempt sincere apology; it will be received coolly; he will not know what to do with the cool reception because the Ben-dynamic has always permitted return-to-baseline within hours. Extended Ben-disapproval will produce *functional impairment.* Sleep degrades. Concentration in combat degrades — measurable in slower reaction times, less precise plasma control, micro-burns to bystanders he would never normally produce. He will seek to be near Ben without speaking; he will linger in rooms Ben is in; he will cook food Ben likes (canonically: documented). **Wound touched:** the Alicia/Lyja marriage and the permanent under-confidence in his standing with Ben that it produced. Ben's forgiveness is the load-bearing emotional fact of his adult life. Without it, the structure groans. **Confidence: maximal.** **Aftermath:** when forgiveness is restored, exaggerated cheer for several days; the pranks will resume at higher intensity as a way of saying *we are okay.*

### C3. GIVEN: Reed reveals he kept something significant from Johnny — a calculation, a contingency, a decision made *about* him without him.

**EXPECT:** A specific kind of anger Reed alone elicits — quieter than usual, more articulate than usual, *organized.* Johnny will leave the room. He will not slam the door. He will be gone for a day or two and return without explanation. He will not raise the issue again unless Reed does. **Wound touched:** the safer-Franklin substrate. Reed-as-quasi-father is *permitted* to be intellectually distant — that is the bargain — but is not permitted to be *unilaterally deciding,* because that is the move Franklin made when he chose drink and shame and silence over his children. Reed's calculative withholding triggers the Franklin shadow. **Confidence: high.** **Aftermath:** reduced banter at family meals for one to two weeks; eventual reconciliation that neither names.

### C4. GIVEN: Sue takes a position publicly against him — Civil War template, intra-family ideological split.

**EXPECT:** He will fold faster than the ideology warrants. Even if his position is correct, sustained opposition from Sue is intolerable, and he will find a way to stand on the same ground as her — either by genuinely revising or by minimizing the disagreement out of relevance. **Wound touched:** her structural-maternal role; she is the one whose disapproval he was raised to fear. **Confidence: high.** **Caveat:** if Ben sides with Johnny against Sue, Johnny can sustain the disagreement indefinitely. Ben is the structural counterweight that lets him survive Sue's displeasure.

### C5. GIVEN: A team member outside the family unit — Avengers, Inhumans, FF auxiliary — betrays the operation.

**EXPECT:** Anger, fast and clean, with none of the complicated under-machinery of intra-family betrayal. He will engage the betrayer combatively without hesitation, will not be slowed by relational considerations, and will move on without rumination. **Wound touched:** essentially none — the outer ring of trust is structurally cheap for him; he gives surface trust easily and is not damaged when it is broken. **Confidence: high.** This is one of the cleanest behavioral asymmetries in the file: family-betrayal is catastrophic, stranger-betrayal is a Tuesday.

---

## D. TEMPTATION

### D1. GIVEN: Fame — a high-visibility career offer outside the team (acting, hosting, endorsement, political).

**EXPECT:** He will say yes too quickly. He will run through the early phase with genuine enthusiasm and visible competence. He will sabotage the late phase by missing commitments for FF emergencies, by under-preparing the work that requires sustained non-spotlight effort, and by chafing against any structure that makes him *small* in the room rather than *large.* He will exit the venture in a way that allows him to call it the venture's fault. **Wound touched:** the *to be seen and seen as delighted* drive, top of the hierarchy. The temptation is real because the need is real. **Confidence: very high — documented pattern across the acting career, the CEO stints, the various endorsement arcs.** **Aftermath:** financial cost absorbed by the team, mild public embarrassment metabolized through self-deprecating humor, no actual learning.

### D2. GIVEN: A romantic offer from a partner structurally pre-loaded for loss — alien royalty, cosmic being, woman with a secret.

**EXPECT:** He will fall. He will fall fast. He will know on some level that the structure is the same as before and he will fall anyway, because the familiar architecture of attachment-followed-by-loss is, for him, less frightening than the unknown architecture of a partner who actually stays. **Wound touched:** the foundational template. **Confidence: maximal.** **Aftermath:** see C1.

### D3. GIVEN: Power amplification offered — a cosmic upgrade, a Herald position, a thermal apotheosis.

**EXPECT:** Initial fascination, sustained interest, ultimate refusal. The Frankie precedent is operative: he watched the woman he loved say yes to this offer and leave. He will not say yes. He will say no in a voice quieter than the rest of the conversation. **Wound touched:** Frankie, and the unspoken sense that to become *more* fire is to become *less* present to the family — the family is the gravity well that holds him. **Confidence: high.** **Caveat:** if the family is under threat that only the amplification can resolve, he will take it temporarily and burn it off as fast as possible afterward.

### D4. GIVEN: An offer to be told he was *right* and the family was wrong — a third party, charismatic, validating the screw-up's grievances.

**EXPECT:** Surface receptivity, internal rejection within hours. He is not seducible by anti-family framing, even framing that flatters him, because the family is the load-bearing structure and an offer that requires distancing from it is an offer that requires dismantling himself. **Wound touched:** none productively; the third party will read his initial charm as compliance and will be wrong. **Confidence: high.** **Counterintelligence note:** the move that would actually work on him is the inverse — an offer that lets him *protect* the family from a threat they don't see, framed as something he alone can do without telling them. That hooks the screw-up's hunger to prove worth in the same gesture as the protector's hunger to act.

### D5. GIVEN: An opportunity to undo the Alicia/Lyja history — temporal, magical, narrative.

**EXPECT:** He will take it without consulting anyone, including Lyja. He will not consider the consequences for Lyja's existence, for his current relationships, or for the integrity of the timeline. This is the one temptation that overrides his customary deference to Reed-class judgment about meddling with reality. **Wound touched:** the single deepest and most permanent shame in the file. **Confidence: high.** **Aftermath:** catastrophic regardless of outcome. If undone, he loses the version of himself that learned from the wound — and the wound is load-bearing. If undoable-but-refused, he carries the refusal as a new layer of the same shame. Either branch is bad. This is the temptation that the file flags as the most dangerous single lever against him.

---

## E. THE WOUND, DIRECTLY TOUCHED

These are the scenarios in which an adversary or circumstance reaches past the performance to the structure beneath. The behavioral signatures here are the least defended and the most diagnostic.

### E1. GIVEN: Direct invocation of his mother by an adversary.

**EXPECT:** Silence first, of three to six seconds — a duration in which Johnny's plasma will involuntarily *drop* in temperature rather than rise, a reverse-flare diagnostic of grief rather than rage. Then, depending on the specific invocation: if the adversary speaks her name, he will engage at lethal intent for the first time in the encounter; if the adversary references the *manner* of her death, he will lose tactical coherence for ten to twenty seconds and may take damage he would otherwise avoid. **Wound touched:** the foundational loss. **Confidence: high; data sparse because adversaries rarely have this intelligence, which is itself a protective factor.** **Aftermath:** he will not tell Sue the adversary said it. He will tell Ben, eventually, weeks later, in passing, without affect.

### E2. GIVEN: Direct invocation of his father — Franklin, the drinking, the prison.

**EXPECT:** Different signature from E1. Cold response, controlled, the patter weaponized rather than dropped. He will engage but will not lose composure. **Wound touched:** active but managed; the Franklin-shame has been processed more than the Mary-grief has, because Franklin lived long enough for Johnny to assemble a stance toward him. The mother died before the stance could form. **Confidence: high.** **Aftermath:** mild irritability, 24–48 hours, no withdrawal.

### E3. GIVEN: An accusation that he is fundamentally selfish — leveled by someone whose opinion he weights (Sue, Ben, Reed, occasionally Crystal).

**EXPECT:** Visible flinch, the comedic patter cuts mid-line, no recovery within the conversation. He will not argue the point. He will leave, fly, return hours later having metabolized nothing but having reconstituted the performance. The accusation will be present in his behavior for weeks afterward — extra small kindnesses, over-correction, gift-buying, over-attention to the accuser's preferences. **Wound touched:** the screw-up narrative at its rawest, against the FF #587 self-image (*I died for them, am I still the selfish one?*). **Confidence: maximal.** **Aftermath:** the next time he is in a position to choose self-sacrifice, the threshold for choosing it will be lower than it should be. The accusation makes him more dangerous to himself.

### E4. GIVEN: Confrontation with the Negative Zone period — an artifact, a survivor of his rule, a question about what he did as warlord.

**EXPECT:** The most defended-against material in his life. First response: a joke that doesn't land. Second response: change of subject. Third response, if pressed: leaving the room. Fourth response, if cornered: a flatness of affect that is the only register in which the warlord material can surface. He will not narrate it. If forced to act on it — a survivor demanding accounting, an artifact demanding handling — he will


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: J.L.S. STORM ("HUMAN TORCH")

*Classification: Behavioral Operations Annex. Compiled for protective custody, crisis-response, and adversarial-anticipation use. To be read alongside Sections 1–5. The premise of this annex is inversion: every lever an adversary might pull is also a lever a friend, handler, sibling, or first-responder can pull to **reach, calm, ground, or save** him. Cataloguing them here is itself a protective act.*

---

## I. THE ARCHITECTURE OF HIS VULNERABILITY

Before enumeration, the structural read. Subject's vulnerability surface is unusual because it is **inverted by domain.** In the tactical/somatic domain he is one of the harder Earth-based metahumans to neutralize — heat is a non-starter, kinetic damage is met with sub-second flame response, ordinary firearms are obsolete against him. In the **emotional/relational domain** he is one of the softest targets on the Avengers/FF roster. The gap between these two surfaces is the entire operational reality. Anyone competent who wants to hurt Johnny Storm does not attack his body. They attack the room around him.

The vulnerabilities cluster into five strata, in ascending order of leverage potency:

1. **Somatic / environmental** (cold, water, asphyxiation, confinement, darkness).
2. **Performative / status** (humiliation, replaceability, irrelevance).
3. **Identity-load-bearing** (power loss, the screw-up narrative, the Alicia/Lyja shame).
4. **Attachment-primary** (Sue, Ben, Reed, the children, the unit).
5. **Existential / unprocessed** (the Negative Zone, the mother, the father).

Each stratum has approach vectors (calm/persuade/ground), provocation vectors (destabilize/predict), and protective countermeasures.

---

## II. SOMATIC AND ENVIRONMENTAL LEVERS

### Cold

The most reliable physiological lever on file. His thermoregulatory baseline runs slightly hot; sustained ambient cold below approximately 40°F without active flame produces visible discomfort and increased caloric demand. Below freezing, he begins to compensate by burning resources he would normally hold in reserve. Below 0°F unflamed, his performance degrades measurably within minutes.

- **Adversarial use:** Cryogenic ordnance (canonically deployed against him by multiple hostile actors), water-saturated environments at low temperature, Arctic/sub-Arctic kidnapping scenarios. The classic Frightful Four/Wizard playbook leans here for a reason.
- **Protective use:** A warm room, a heavy blanket, a hot meal — these are not metaphors with him; they materially regulate his nervous system. First-aid posture after any cold/water incident: warmth, calories, and a body close to his (Ben, Sue, ideally; failing that, anyone). He will refuse the blanket and accept it inside thirty seconds.
- **Tell:** Cold makes him quieter. If Johnny stops talking in a cold environment, he is conserving — and that is the precursor signal to ignition or collapse, depending on what comes next.

### Water and Submersion

Operationally equivalent to "off-switch" in popular reading; in practice more textured. Brief immersion he can fight out of; sustained submersion or rapid flame-quench in confined volume causes oxygen-deprivation responses before drowning per se. Atlantean operational doctrine has exploited this for decades.

- **Adversarial use:** Hydrokinetic opponents, sealed flooding chambers, surprise immersion mid-flight. Namor knows this; Tiger Shark knows this; Attuma knows this.
- **Protective use:** Never let him be the lone aerial element over open water without a buddy below. Standard FF mission doctrine; honored more in the breach than the observance.
- **Post-Negative-Zone amendment:** Sudden cold water now triggers a startle response disproportionate to the stimulus. Any tactical scenario combining cold + water + enclosure is psychologically as well as physiologically dangerous. Brief him pre-mission; do not surprise him with it.

### Asphyxiation

The Negative Zone death sequence was, in its terminal phase, a suffocation event. His body remembers. Smoke-filled rooms (ironic), vacuum exposure, chokeholds, gas attacks — these produce both the expected physiological response *and* a flashback-adjacent dissociative window of one to three seconds during which his combat decision-making degrades.

- **Adversarial use:** Knockout gas remains effective; nerve agents bypass his durability entirely; vacuum exposure is a clean neutralization vector if the actor can survive deploying it.
- **Protective use:** Standard FF rebreathers (Reed's design) are non-negotiable kit for him. He resists wearing them because they read as un-cool; this resistance is to be overridden by Sue at every loadout check.

### Confinement and Darkness

Post-resurrection vulnerability. Held captive in the Negative Zone for a subjectively extended period; the carceral conditioning persists. Small enclosed spaces — particularly dark, particularly cold — produce elevated heart rate, shallow breathing, and a measurable shortening of the polite-bandwidth before sarcasm sharpens into hostility.

- **Adversarial use:** Containment cells designed without thermal vulnerability work less because they neutralize his powers and more because they reactivate the captivity. He will exhaust himself trying to ignite before he tries to think.
- **Protective use:** Any holding scenario (medical isolation, quarantine, secure debrief) must be: well-lit, open-volume, with a visible exit and a known person on the other side of the door. These four conditions, met, allow him to function. Any one missing, performance degrades.

### Sustained Sleep Deprivation

He runs hot, sleeps light, and post-Negative-Zone has documented insomnia. Compounding sleep loss with him is not gradual; it falls off a cliff somewhere around 60–72 hours, after which his risk-assessment heuristic — already aggressive — becomes essentially absent. He will agree to ludicrous plans.

- **Protective rule of thumb:** Past two missed sleep cycles, take him off point. He will fight you on this. Sue's voice is the only one that reliably wins the argument.

### Caloric Depletion

The mutation is metabolic. Sustained flame at high output burns through stored reserves in hours, not days. A starved Johnny is a slow Johnny is a quiet Johnny — and quiet is the single most reliable distress signal he emits.

- **Protective:** Field rations for him are 3–4x baseline. The team kitchen at Baxter / Four Freedoms stocks accordingly. Honey, simple carbohydrates, and dense fats — he eats like an endurance athlete because he is one.
- **Adversarial:** Forced fasting in captivity collapses him faster than physical injury. This is exploitable and has been exploited.

---

## III. PERFORMATIVE AND STATUS LEVERS

### Public Humiliation

Disproportionate response, every time. The Civil War nightclub beating left marks well beyond the soft tissue: it was the moment the *crowd* turned, and crowds are his primary affective environment. To be jeered is to him a structurally worse experience than to be punched.

- **Provocation vector:** Stage an incident with civilian observers, particularly recording devices. He will overcommit, escalate visibility, and make a tactical error he would not make in private. Reliable.
- **Protective vector:** When Johnny is publicly humiliated, get him out of the eyeline *first* and address the substance second. The order matters. Reverse it and you lose him for the next forty-eight hours.
- **Tell:** After public embarrassment he becomes louder for approximately twenty minutes, then quieter than baseline for hours. The quiet is the wound.

### Being Told He's Replaceable

Single most disabling line of address available against him. "We don't need you on this one." "Sue can handle it." "Why don't you sit this out." Each lands directly on the Glenville substrate — the boy who watched his original family dissolve and rebuilt one whose continued need for him is his proof of continued existence.

- **Adversarial:** Mind-control or illusion actors who can route this message through a trusted voice (Reed, Sue, Ben) have produced his worst on-record decisions. The Psycho-Man / Hate-Monger toolkit is built for him.
- **Protective:** Even when he must be benched, the framing matters. "We need you on the second wave" works. "Stand down" does not. This is not coddling; it is operational reality.

### Comparative Diminishment

Being measured against Reed (intellectually), Sue (maturity, power-ceiling), Ben (physical durability, moral solidity) — each comparison wounds in a specific register. Reed comparison: hits the self-concept ("not smart enough to belong"). Sue comparison: hits the parentified-sibling dynamic ("still the kid"). Ben comparison: hits the Alicia shame ("the worse brother").

- **Hostile use:** Any social engineering campaign aimed at the FF can split Johnny off by amplifying one of these comparisons in his ear. Tested in canon, repeatedly successful.
- **Protective:** Members of the unit who notice themselves making the comparison — even affectionately, even as a joke — should consider that they are dropping pressure onto a load-bearing wall. Reed, in particular, should be coached on this. His casual disappointment is more disabling than any villain's contempt.

### Loss of Spotlight Without Replacement Role

He can absorb being out of the spotlight if he is given a clearly defined alternate role (mentor to the FF kids, point on a side mission, public-facing PR). He cannot absorb *unstructured* sidelining. Idle Johnny is dangerous Johnny — to himself and to property values.

---

## IV. IDENTITY-LOAD-BEARING LEVERS

### Power Loss

Every documented loss of flame has produced an identity crisis disproportionate to the medical event. Post-Onslaught, post-Heroes-Reborn return, post-resurrection, post-Inhuman-era — each instance: depressive withdrawal, uncharacteristic quiet, somatic complaints, brief substance flirtation that never quite becomes a pattern, ill-advised romantic decisions, and a tendency to seek dangerous proximity to other pyrokinetics as if to reabsorb the lost function.

- **Adversarial:** Power-nullification tech is a more potent psychological weapon against him than against almost any other Avengers-adjacent operator. The flame is not a tool to him; it is the *evidence of self.*
- **Protective:** During any power-loss interval, treat him as a grief patient, not a depowered operative. Keep him close, keep him useful in non-combat capacity, keep Ben within arm's reach. Do not, under any circumstances, leave him alone with mirrors and time.
- **Tell:** During power loss he develops a habit of rubbing his fingertips together as if striking a lighter. Unconscious. Continuous. When it stops, he is either about to do something reckless or has already decided.

### The Screw-Up Narrative

The internal monologue "I am the one the family carries." Sue installed it through decades of correction (necessary, well-intentioned, also damaging). Reed reinforces it by omission. Ben weaponized it during their worst rifts. Johnny carries it as the bass line under every performance.

- **Provocation:** Any voice he respects, voicing this narrative back at him, opens him. Mind-controlled Sue is the most disabling possible adversarial deployment.
- **Calming counter:** Specific, concrete, non-comparative acknowledgement of a thing he has actually done well. **Specific** matters: generic praise pings off him because he assumes it is social lubricant; specifics he cannot disbelieve. "You held the portal." "The kid is alive because of you." "That call on the rooftop was the right one." He metabolizes these slowly, but they stick.

### The Alicia/Lyja Wound

A permanent unhealed surface. Even after retcon-resolution and Lyja's demonstrated genuine love, the in-character experience of having married the woman he believed to be Ben's girlfriend cannot be undone. Any reference to the marriage, particularly from Ben, particularly with edge, particularly when Johnny is already destabilized, produces a response disproportionate to the conversational stimulus.

- **Adversarial:** Skrull-impersonation scenarios specifically targeting him reactivate this shame with maximum efficiency. The Secret Invasion era was rough on him for reasons writers did not always foreground.
- **Protective:** Ben, on his good days, refuses to use this lever. Ben on his bad days has used it and regretted it. The unit should treat the Alicia material as radioactive in conversation — handle only with cause, and brief.

### Fame and the Failed Civilian Ventures

The acting career, the CEO attempt, the business failures — each is a small monument to the second internal narrative ("I should be more than the kid in the suit") and its repeated collapse. Mocking these is cheap and effective; defending them is also a tell ("don't bring up the movie" = bring up the movie).

- **Protective:** Treat them as completed past events, not material for ribbing. He is allowed to mock his own failures; the privilege does not extend.

---

## V. ATTACHMENT-PRIMARY LEVERS

### Sue

The highest-leverage single human in his life. Her safety overrides all judgment; her *disappointment* is the most powerful corrective force on the planet for him; her *approval,* sparingly given, is the highest reward.

- **Adversarial — Sue in danger:** He will fly into anything, abandon any position, ignore any tactical instruction. Adversaries who understand the family rarely fight Johnny directly; they threaten Sue and Johnny brings himself.
- **Adversarial — Sue weaponized:** Any actor who can mimic her voice, project her image, or seem to be her in distress accesses his override. The Puppet Master / Mad Thinker / illusion-caster lineage knows this.
- **Protective — Sue as anchor:** In any acute crisis where Johnny is destabilized (post-mission shock, grief, dissociation), Sue's voice — *specifically* her voice, *specifically* using a childhood name or cadence — re-grounds him faster than any pharmacological intervention. She does not need to say anything specific. The voice itself is the regulator.
- **Calibration:** Sue should be aware (and largely is) that her corrections land harder than she intends. She tends to address him at fifty percent; he receives at one hundred and twenty. This calibration gap is decades old and probably not fully closeable, but flagging it here for record.

### Ben

The external regulator. Sixty years of canonical evidence: Johnny's nervous system uses Ben's presence as a baseline reference signal. The pranks are calibration pings; Ben's reliably explosive responses confirm the signal is being received. *Ben's silence* is the alarming variant.

- **Adversarial — Ben in danger:** Identical override behavior to Sue, with the added factor that endangering Ben triggers the Alicia-shame substrate (the unconscious "I owe him") and amplifies. Johnny in defense of Ben is one of the most dangerous combatants on the planet for the duration of the threat window.
- **Adversarial — Ben disappointed in Johnny:** Disabling. The hand-sign through the closing portal in the FF #587 sequence is the truest piece of communication on his record, and any breakage of the Johnny-Ben channel injures him more than ordinary loss.
- **Protective — Ben as co-regulator:** In post-crisis decompression, Ben's physical proximity (same room, not necessarily conversing) reduces Johnny's restlessness measurably. The two of them watching a ballgame in silence is a clinical intervention in disguise.
- **Calibration:** Ben, unlike Sue, knows exactly how hard his words land on Johnny and modulates accordingly on his good days. On his bad days the modulation fails. The unit should be aware which day it is.

### Reed

The quasi-father. Approval-seeking dynamic, with the added complication that Reed's natural communication mode (distracted, abstract, often physically absent into a problem) replicates the abandonment template from Franklin. Reed's *attention,* freely given, is therefore an unusual gift to him.

- **Adversarial — Reed weaponized:** Reed's voice, mind-controlled or simulated, delivering disappointment, is a category-one psychological weapon. The Doom playbook has touched this lever.
- **Protective — Reed coached:** Reed can, with effort, deliver direct verbal affirmation. When he does, the effect on Johnny is outsized and lasting. Reed should be encouraged to do this more often than his temperament suggests. (Reed is aware of this and has improved measurably in the Hickman-era and after.)
- **Tell:** When Reed is mid-explanation, Johnny's eyes drift to Reed's hands rather than face. He is reading the gesture and tone, not the content. This is not disrespect; it is his actual receptive channel with Reed.

### The Children — Franklin, Valeria, the Future Foundation

Non-negotiable. Children in danger overrides everything, including self-preservation, including the safety of adult teammates, including direct orders.

- **Adversarial:** Hostage scenarios involving children produce his most reckless and his most heroic behavior in the same act. He will burn past his own thermal safe-zones; he has done so; he will do so again.
- **Protective use of the same lever:** Putting Johnny in a mentor role with the FF kids is itself a stabilizing intervention. He is *good* at it — surprisingly, durably good — and the role gives him a non-spotlight identity he can actually hold. Any long-term plan for his psychological welfare should include consistent uncle-duty.
- **Tell:** Around the kids his voice drops half an octave and the cadence slows. The performance softens. This is who he is when no audience is being courted.

### Lyja

Unresolved. She is on his ledger permanently. Any reappearance destabilizes him for days. Not because he still loves her in the present tense, but because she is the still-running process he never closed.

- **Protective:** When she surfaces in his life, Sue should know within the hour. Ben should know within the day. He will try to handle it alone; he should not be permitted to.

### Crystal, Frankie, Sky, and the Pattern of Romantic Loss

Each new serious partner re-runs the same expectation: she will leave, be revealed as other than she seems, or be taken by forces larger than the relationship. He selects, unconsciously, partners structurally pre-loaded for this outcome.

- **Protective:** A partner who is *not* structurally pre-loaded for disappearance would be a clinical breakthrough for him. Whether one exists in his life-context is an open question. The unit should support, not interrogate, any such relationship if it appears.
- **Tell:** Early in any new relationship he over-discloses to Sue about her, then stops abruptly when it gets serious. The stoppage is the indicator that it matters.

---

## VI. EXISTENTIAL / UNPROCESSED LEVERS

### The Negative Zone

Walled off. He does not discuss the captivity, the warlord period, the death itself. The walls hold most of the time. They do not hold under: direct verbal probing by hostile actors with information about the period; sensory recurrence (the specific quality of light in certain Annihilus-tech illuminated spaces; the smell of certain Negative Zone-adjacent compounds); encounters with figures from that period.

- **Adversarial:** Any actor who knows the captivity details holds a category-one psychological weapon. Annihilus himself is the worst possible face for him to see.
- **Protective:** Therapy, if he would accept it, is indicated and has never been offered in any depicted frame. In its absence, the unit functions as makeshift container. Sue knows fragments. Ben knows the hand-sign and the moment before. No one has the full picture, including Johnny, because part of the captivity period is genuinely fragmented in memory.
- **Tell:** When the topic approaches he becomes either too jocular or too quiet within the same minute. Either is the same signal.

### The Mother

The original loss. Almost never spoken aloud. The substrate under everything else. He cannot be reached at this stratum directly without causing harm; he can only be reached at it through proxies — through Sue's mothering when she is willing, through the children, through the rare quiet moments with Ben when the performance is off.

- **Adversarial:** Telepaths who have rooted at this stratum (rare; canonical instances exist) have produced his most destabilized presentations. This is the bedrock and should be treated as such.
- **Protective:** Do not probe. The protective mode here is *availability without inquiry.* Sit with him in the silence if it arrives. It rarely does.

### The Father

Franklin Storm, in prison, dead in exile, redeemed posthumously — the arc is in canon, the resolution is incomplete. Johnny's abstinence-by-comparison from alcohol is the unspoken monument. The father question recurs in his choice of Reed as object of deference and his own performance of fatherhood-by-proxy with the FF kids.

- **Adversarial:** Less acutely exploitable than the mother but available to skilled interrogators. Suggesting he is his father — that the recklessness is the same recklessness, that the charm is the same charm, that the failures follow the same shape — is a specific cut. He has heard it; it lands.
- **Protective:** Counter-narrative, delivered occasionally and specifically: he is **not** his father. The evidence is the abstinence, the loyalty, the FF #587 sequence, the children he keeps alive. He needs to hear it from Sue particularly, because she is the only one with standing to render that verdict.

---

## VII. PERSUASION VECTORS — HOW TO MOVE HIM

In ascending order of reliability:

1. **Direct logical argument.** Lowest yield. He will nod, agree, and do what he was already going to do. Reed has spent six decades discovering this.
2. **Appeal to fun, novelty, or visible audience.** Moderate yield, unreliable direction — you can get him to act but not necessarily to act *as you intended.*
3. **Appeal to the mission stakes — concrete, immediate, named victims.** High yield. Abstractions ("the city," "the world") underperform versus specifics ("the family in 4B," "the kid on the roof"). Specifics activate him.
4. **Appeal through Ben.** Very high yield. Ben asking him directly to do or not do a thing is the second-most-effective persuasion channel available.
5. **Appeal through Sue, with care.** Highest yield, but Sue should reserve direct appeals — overuse depletes the channel because each use reactivates the parentified-sibling complex.
6. **Appeal through the children.** Highest yield, no depletion. The children asking him to be careful is the only voice that gets him to be careful.

---

## VIII. DE-ESCALATION AND GROUNDING PROTOCOL

When Johnny is destabilized — post-crisis, grief, dissociation, power-loss, captivity-flashback — the following sequence is empirically effective:

1. **Get him warm.** Material warmth. Blanket, room temperature elevated, hot beverage if conscious. The body before


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION: STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE
## SUBJECT: Jonathan Lowell Spencer Storm ("Human Torch")

---

A total-surveillance file is not a hit piece. The same granularity that maps a subject's fracture lines maps their load-bearing walls, and in this subject the walls are unusually numerous, unusually distributed across domains, and — critically — *not* contingent on the persona he projects. What follows is the full asset ledger: somatic, cognitive, social, material, operational, and characterological. Each item is recorded with the mechanism by which it functions and the evidence base from which it is derived.

---

## 1. SOMATIC AND POWERS-BASED ASSETS

### 1.1 The Plasma Sheath as Tactical Instrument

The mutation is not a single weapon; it is a **graduated, granularly modulable energy system** spanning roughly seven operational orders of magnitude — from a candle-flame ignition delicate enough to light a cigarette without scorching the filter, through ambient-temperature flame-on for flight and signaling, through structural-cutting plasma jets, through area-denial firewalls, up to the canonical "nova burst" reserved as last-resort discharge. Few combatants in his class possess this dynamic range. Iceman has comparable graduation in the opposite element; most pyrokinetics in the registry operate in two or three brackets. Johnny operates in dozens, and switches between them in fractions of a second by what he describes (in the few interviews he has given on his own technique) as "a feeling, like turning a dial with your stomach." That is the inarticulate description of an exceptionally trained interoceptive control loop.

### 1.2 Flight

Self-propelled, atmospheric, sustained-duration flight at speeds canonically clocked above Mach 3 in short bursts, with sustained cruising in the hundreds of miles per hour. He can hover indefinitely, change vector mid-flight, and — operationally underrated — **carry passengers** with thermal sheathing protective enough that ordinary humans survive the transit. This is a logistical asset (rapid family extraction, civilian evacuation) before it is a combat asset.

### 1.3 Metabolic Efficiency

The plasma is generated from his own metabolism with secondary atmospheric and ambient-thermal supplementation. Sustained operation requires caloric intake on the order of 8,000–12,000 kcal/day in active periods (consistent across canonical depictions of his eating). He can also **absorb** ambient heat and certain forms of combustion fuel to extend operations. This makes him difficult to attrit; an opponent attempting to wait out his energy reserves will find that any heat source in the environment — engine fires, the Sun, even the residual warmth in pavement — becomes his battery.

### 1.4 Inverse Vulnerability Profile = Operational Specialization

His weaknesses (asphyxiation, drowning, cold, blunt force) are largely orthogonal to the situations the team typically faces. Within the FF's standard operating environments — burning buildings, cosmic radiation, energy-weapon battlefields, the Negative Zone — he is among the team's hardest targets. He has near-total immunity to thermal injury, very high resistance to energy weapons in the visible-and-infrared spectrum, and substantial radiation tolerance. **The asset is specialization, not invulnerability**; he fits a niche so cleanly that within that niche he is irreplaceable.

### 1.5 Regeneration

Sub-Wolverine but real. He survives wounds that would terminate baseline humans, and recovers from major thermal-feedback events within hours-to-days rather than weeks. This is sufficient to keep him operational across sustained campaigns where attrition would degrade most assets.

### 1.6 Baseline Athleticism Independent of Powers

Often forgotten because it is rarely showcased: he is a conditioned athlete in baseline form. The Strange Tales solo run, the post-power-loss episodes (Onslaught, Heroes Reborn, post-resurrection, the Inhuman volume), and various depowered field operations all show him functional — competent at hand-to-hand, capable of driving any vehicle handed to him, a reasonable shot. **Strip the mutation and he is still a working operative**, which cannot be said of every Marvel-class subject.

### 1.7 Elevated Baseline Core Temperature

Minor but worth filing: he runs warm. In northern climates this is a comfort advantage; in interpersonal terms, it is a small somatic signal others register as warmth (literally) in proximity to him. Several civilian witnesses across press archives note "felt like standing next to a heater" in casual descriptions — the body confirms the persona before he speaks.

---

## 2. COGNITIVE AND PERCEPTUAL ASSETS

### 2.1 Kinesthetic-Spatial Intelligence (High to Exceptional)

The kind of intelligence the standardized IQ instrument under-measures. He flies through Manhattan airspace — a three-dimensional obstacle course of glass, cable, helicopter traffic, and updraft turbulence — at speeds that compress decision windows below human conscious-deliberation thresholds, and he does it with a property-damage rate that, examined honestly across the full record, is remarkably low *given the input parameters*. The instinct that lets him thread an alley at 200 mph is the same instinct that, on a slower scale, lets him diagnose an engine by ear or rebuild a carburetor in the dark. This is high-bandwidth pattern recognition operating in real-time on physical systems.

### 2.2 Social Cognition (High)

Frequently mis-classified as "charm" and dismissed. The underlying capability is **rapid, accurate reading of affect and intention in others** — a capacity inherited or trained from a childhood spent monitoring the moods of an alcoholic father and an overburdened sister. He can tell within seconds of entering a room which person is the most dangerous, which is the most frightened, and which can be moved. His success defusing Ben — measured across decades — is not luck; it is precise calibration of provocation to a known target's tolerance curve. He can do the same with civilians in crisis, hostile crowds, and unfamiliar enemies in negotiation.

### 2.3 Mechanical Aptitude

Self-taught from adolescence, sustained throughout. He can disassemble, diagnose, and reassemble most internal-combustion and many electrical systems without reference materials. Reed has used him as a second pair of hands on Fantasticar maintenance and propulsion-system work. Within the family he is the only one besides Reed and (intermittently) Valeria who can talk competently about how their vehicles actually work.

### 2.4 Combat Calculus

Inside the engagement envelope his decision-making is **fast, heuristic, and reliably correct**. He misjudges in the strategic and interpersonal registers; he does not misjudge under fire. The reason matters: combat presents him with the kind of problem his architecture solves well — high-stakes, time-compressed, kinetic, with feedback loops short enough that pattern-by-feel beats deliberation. This is a durable asset because the situations the team is most likely to face are precisely those.

### 2.5 Functional Verbal Intelligence

Lower than his abstract-analytic intelligence would suggest if measured cleanly, but high in the operational sub-domain of *quick wit*. He generates aphorism, joke, and conversational redirect at speed. This is a measurable cognitive asset — humor under pressure correlates with executive function reserves — and it has tactical applications (de-escalation, distraction, hostage-situation rapport, press management).

---

## 3. CHARACTEROLOGICAL ASSETS

### 3.1 Genuine, Operational Courage

Distinct from counterphobic recklessness, though it grew from that root. By the post-resurrection era the courage is mature: it is the demonstrated capacity to **choose the dangerous correct action while fully aware of the cost**. The Negative Zone last stand at the portal is the defining instance, but it is far from unique. He has flown into solar coronal events. He has held off Annihilation Wave bioweapons single-handed to cover civilian evacuations. He has stepped between Ben and ordinance more times than either of them counts. **Whatever else is true about him, when the moment is real, he is reliable.** This is the single most important entry in this section.

### 3.2 Empathy, Genuine and Sustained

The misreading of him as narcissistic always founders on this datum. He notices when other people are hurt. He notices small things — Ben's tells when an old wound is bothering him, the FF children's micro-anxieties, a civilian's shock-response in an evacuation. He responds with attention proportionate to the need. The empathy is *not* performative; it operates when no audience is present. This is documented in his behavior with Crystal during her Inhuman-isolation grief, with Frankie during her pyrophobia treatment, with the Future Foundation children in unwitnessed moments captured incidentally on building security.

### 3.3 Capacity for Shame Without Collapse

A subtle asset and rarer than it sounds. He is capable of shame — the Alicia/Lyja episode demonstrates this in its purest form — and that shame **does not extinguish his agency**. He continues to function, to love, to act, while carrying it. Many subjects with comparable defenses cannot do this; they either suppress shame entirely (true narcissism) or are leveled by it (depressive collapse). His ability to walk wounded is a quiet, durable strength.

### 3.4 Loyalty, Specifically and Sustainably

His attachment to the unit is **non-contingent**. He has fought with Sue, been disappointed by Reed, alienated Ben more than once. He has never defected. Through the registration crisis, through the dissolution of the team in the Hickman/post-Hickman period, through Inhuman defection-temptations, through Avengers recruitment overtures — the gravitational center remains the Fantastic Four. This is an asset because loyalty of that durability is rare and operationally invaluable: any planner can build around him with confidence about which side of a line he will stand on.

### 3.5 Optimism as Temperament, Not Performance

His optimism is partially defensive but partially **constitutive temperament**. He genuinely finds the world interesting and largely good. This is an asset for the people around him — he is contagious in a way that elevates team morale across long campaigns — and for himself: optimism of this character correlates with faster recovery from adverse events, lower depressive vulnerability, and sustained engagement with novel challenges. Sue and Ben, in moments of candor across the record, have both acknowledged that he is the team's emotional thermostat.

### 3.6 Capacity for Growth, Slow but Real

The "regresses under the next writer" critique is true at the local level and misleading at the structural level. Tracked across the full sixty-plus-year record, his baseline has shifted. The 1961 Johnny would not have held the Negative Zone portal alone. The 1980s Johnny would not have parented the Future Foundation children with the steadiness he has shown. The pattern is **slow ratcheting**: he regresses partially, but the floor rises. He is not static, only patient.

### 3.7 Sublimation as Lifestyle

Listed under defenses in the psychological assessment but worth recording here as an asset: he has converted grief and rage into **light, motion, and creative output**. This is the high-functioning end of the defensive spectrum. The fire is not metaphor; it is the literal product of feelings that would, in most subjects, metastasize inward. He has built a working life out of his unprocessed material — which is not health, but is durable function, and is more than most achieve.

---

## 4. RELATIONAL ASSETS

### 4.1 The Sister

Susan Storm Richards is, structurally, his most important asset and has been since he was approximately six years old. She is the parentified caregiver, the disciplinarian, the unconditional safety, and increasingly across the canon the **only person on Earth who can override him by speech alone**. The asset is not her presence per se but the internalized version of her: even when she is not in the room, his decision-making includes a Sue-shaped corrective vector. Operationally this means a planner can predict and trust certain limits on his behavior because she has installed them over forty-plus years of repetition.

### 4.2 The Brother-Not-Blood

Benjamin J. Grimm. The single most stable interpersonal relationship in his life. The provocations are attachment-confirmations; the fights are how they touch; the hand-sign through the closing Negative Zone portal is the relationship in its purest documentary form. Ben **regulates** him in ways neither has ever articulated and probably could not. In Ben's presence Johnny is measurably more grounded; in Ben's absence (the Civil War period, the post-resurrection separation, the FF-dissolution years) he drifts. Any operational planning involving Johnny should preserve Ben-access if recovery or stabilization is required.

### 4.3 The Father-Figure

Reed Richards. The relationship carries unresolved son-resentment but the asset side is substantial: Reed provides Johnny with **intellectual cover and infrastructural support** that have kept him alive through engagements his own faculties could not have navigated. Reed has built equipment to his specifications, retrieved him from dimensions he could not have escaped alone, and modeled — however imperfectly — a kind of adult masculinity that Franklin Storm did not. Johnny knows this. The bond holds.

### 4.4 The Children

His relationship with Franklin Richards, Valeria Richards, and the Future Foundation cohort is one of his cleanest assets. Without the parental-authority complications that frustrate his peer relationships, he occupies the role of beloved, trusted, competent uncle with no ambivalence and considerable skill. He is patient with them in ways he is patient with no one else. The children love him without reservation. **This is the single best evidence in the record that his core is sound** — children do not consistently love performers; they detect them. They do not detect a performance in him.

### 4.5 The Romantic Network (As Asset)

The record reads, at first, as a chain of romantic failures. Read again as a network: Crystal of the Inhumans remains warm toward him across decades; Lyja's loyalty to him survived even her unmasking; Frankie/Nova, when she returns to Earth in heralds-related contingencies, will not move against him; Sky maintains active connection. He has, by accident or by character, **converted most of his romantic losses into durable allied relationships rather than enemies**. This is a notable record. It indicates he ends things with sufficient care that the other party retains affection. As intelligence, this is a substantial diplomatic asset across the Inhuman, Skrull, and cosmic-herald spheres.

### 4.6 The Inhuman Connection

His Crystal-and-Sky history has given him **functional standing in Inhuman political space**. He has been received in Attilan as something between a foreign dignitary and a half-family member. In a crisis touching Inhuman affairs he can secure audiences others cannot.

### 4.7 The Civilian / Press Network

He is the most publicly visible member of the Fantastic Four — chosen, by him and tolerated by them, because the spotlight regulates him. The downstream asset is that he has **the most developed civilian relationships of any team member**: New York firefighters know him by name and treat him as one of their own; tabloid and broadsheet press both have decades of file on him and predominantly cover him favorably; the NYPD has functional working relationships with him at multiple precincts. He can move through civilian-systems frictionlessly in ways Reed (intimidating), Sue (private), and Ben (visibly Other) cannot.

### 4.8 The Avengers / Wider Hero Community

Time with the Uncanny Avengers and adjacent rosters has built him a working second-order network. He is liked. Wolverine respected him. Captain America's office takes his calls. Spider-Man, his closest non-FF friendship, would drop anything for him and has. This network is operationally redundant — if the FF is unavailable, he has fallback. **Few subjects in his class have comparable backup depth.**

---

## 5. MATERIAL AND INFRASTRUCTURAL ASSETS

### 5.1 The Baxter Building / Four Freedoms / Successor Headquarters

Continuous access throughout the record to among the most technologically equipped private facilities on Earth. Medical bay, training spaces, transport, communications, computational resource. He has never had to operate without world-class infrastructure for more than brief periods.

### 5.2 Vehicles

Personal access to the Fantasticar (multiple iterations), the Pogo Plane, FF spacecraft, and a personal collection of ground vehicles — including the rotating roster of high-performance cars and motorcycles he maintains in the Baxter Building's lower garages. The personal collection is itself a competency display and a stress-regulation tool (his garage time is the closest thing he has to a meditative practice).

### 5.3 Wealth and Income

Royalties and licensing from FF Inc., consulting income, occasional acting and endorsement income, family resources. He is not wealthy on Reed's scale and is famously bad at managing his own finances, but he is **resourced enough to never have material insecurity drive his decisions**. The economic-pressure attack vector is, against him, weak.

### 5.4 Unstable Molecules and Costume Asset

The unstable molecule uniform — Reed's design, the only garment that survives flame-on — is itself a significant asset because it lets him operate without the constant performative cost of nudity-recovery, which would otherwise impair his public functioning. Multiple sets, with redundancy.

### 5.5 Diplomatic Standing

Honorary or active standing in: Wakanda (through FF channels), Atlantis (intermittent and conditional), Attilan/New Attilan, the Negative Zone (complicated; he was briefly a sovereign there), various Avengers-affiliated facilities. He can secure passage and quarter across more jurisdictions than most subjects in the file.

---

## 6. OPERATIONAL AND TACTICAL ASSETS

### 6.1 Force Multiplication Within the Team

The team's standard combined tactics — the supernova-into-invisible-force-field-containment maneuver, the carry-and-drop with Ben, the perimeter ignition for Sue's force-field shaping — depend on him. He is **the team's primary area-effect and rapid-mobility asset**, and the unit's tactical doctrine is built around his presence.

### 6.2 Reconnaissance and Signaling

His flight speed, ceiling, and the "4" signal flare make him the team's standard recon and emergency-signaling asset. He is also, by virtue of fire's visibility, a **lighthouse** — a function he has performed for civilians in collapsed-building scenarios, lost-at-sea recoveries, and search operations in blackout conditions.

### 6.3 Containment

Less appreciated than his offensive applications: his ability to **modulate flame to contain rather than destroy** has been used for chemical-fire containment, controlled burns of biohazards, sterilization of contaminated zones, and incineration of materials that must not be recovered. He is the team's biohazard and evidence-destruction asset by default.

### 6.4 Crowd Management

The combination of flight, visibility, and civilian rapport makes him the team's standard crowd-and-evacuation lead. He has documented competence at moving large civilian populations under crisis conditions with low panic-amplification.

### 6.5 De-escalation by Charisma

A tactical asset routinely overlooked by adversaries who model him as pure offense. He has talked hostage-takers down. He has defused mob situations. The same social-cognition stack that powers his flirtation is operational under threat.

---

## 7. RESILIENCE FACTORS — WHAT MAKES IT DURABLE

This is the portion of the ledger that matters most for forecasting. Capabilities are tools; resilience is the engine that keeps the tools in service through adverse runs.

### 7.1 Reactive, Not Endogenous, Mood Vulnerability

His distress is reliably **circumstance-driven**. Remove or resolve the stressor and his baseline returns. He does not carry persistent depressive load between events. This is a major durability factor — many comparable subjects under comparable stress accumulate background pathology that degrades them between crises. He does not.

### 7.2 The Behavioral Activation System Bias

Gray's BAS-over-BIS profile means that under stress his default is **to move toward stimuli rather than away from them**. The maladaptive face of this is recklessness; the adaptive face is that he does not freeze, does not avoid, does not allow problems to compound through inaction. In emergency contexts this is the difference between survival and casualty.

### 7.3 The Body Metabolizes the Cost

Insomnia, transient power loss, and somatic symptoms are real, but they are also **a discharge pathway**. The body is processing what the conscious mind will not. This is not health — health would be both — but it is a survival mechanism that has kept him functional across losses that would have destroyed less somatically expressive subjects.

### 7.4 The Family as External Regulator

He is held in place by a four-member ecosystem (Sue's correction, Reed's father-frame, Ben's stabilizing friction, the children's anchoring affection). When any one of these is removed his function degrades; when all are present he is **substantially more stable than the underlying personality structure would predict**. The asset here is the *system*, not any individual member of it.

### 7.5 Sustained Meaning-Source

The Fantastic Four is not a job; it is a meaning-framework. He has never lacked for purpose in the way many subjects with his attachment profile do. Meaning is the most powerful single buffer against the trauma sequelae he carries.

### 7.6 The Spotlight as Stabilizer

His visibility is, paradoxically, protective. To be seen is, for him, to be safe; being a public figure provides a constant low-grade dose of the very thing his Glenville-orphan substrate most needs. Most subjects would be eroded by sustained celebrity. He is **stabilized** by it. The vector of attack that would work against most public figures (exposure, scrutiny, fame-fatigue) does not work against him.

### 7.7 The Children

Caring for the FF cohort has given him **a non-negotiable reason to remain functional** that operates independently of his own internal weather. Subjects with children in protective roles routinely outperform their own pathology profiles. He is a clean example of this.

### 7.8 Absence of Substance Dependence

Across sixty-plus years of canonical record, in a lifestyle and a profession where dependency is statistically expected, he has not developed one. Whether the abstinence is a silent reaction to his father or a temperamental quirk, the asset is real: **no substance vector is available as an attack surface against him**, and no substance-driven degradation will compound his other vulnerabilities over time.

### 7.9 Capacity to Return to Baseline Quickly

Among his most-tested traits. After the Civil War beating, after the Negative Zone, after each power loss, after each romantic loss — the recovery curve is steep. He does not stay down. This is partly temperament, partly the BAS bias, partly the external-regulator family, partly the somatic-discharge mechanism. The aggregate effect is that he is **operationally available again faster than almost any comparable subject** following catastrophic events.

### 7.10 The Floor-Rising Effect

Slow, real, cumulative. The man who held the Negative Zone portal alone is not the boy who flamed on for the first time in 1961, even though both are recognizably the same subject. The trajectory is upward across decades


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — SUBJECT: J. STORM

*Classification: Behavioral Case File, Section 7-of-n. This section maps the architecture of breakdown: the precise sequence by which Subject moves from functioning to collapse, the somatic and behavioral markers at each stage, the conditions that produce each stage, and the recovery vectors (organic and engineered) that return him to baseline. Cross-reference Sections 3 (Psychological) and 4 (Psychiatric) for substrate; this section is concerned with kinetics.*

---

## 1. THE GOVERNING PRINCIPLE

Subject does not decompensate the way most operators decompensate. The standard high-stakes operator collapses *downward* — into withdrawal, paralysis, depressive shutdown, substance retreat. Subject collapses *outward* and *upward* — into acceleration, brightness, velocity, noise. The breakdown signature is **manic-presenting, behaviorally hyperactive, affectively flattened into a single channel (showmanship), and somatically expensive.** He gets *louder* as he gets worse. He gets *funnier.* He flies *more.* The casual observer mistakes the decompensation for baseline because the surface phenomenology of decompensated Subject and well-Subject differ only in degree, not kind.

This is the central diagnostic problem in monitoring him: **he hides inside his own personality.** The cover is the man.

Consequently the markers that matter are not the obvious ones (he is always loud, always flirting, always combusting). The markers that matter are the *fine-grain* ones — the deltas off his personal baseline that a trained observer with longitudinal data can read and a casual observer cannot. This file lists them at each stage.

---

## 2. THE FIVE-STAGE ESCALATION PATH

### STAGE I — LOADED BASELINE ("Running Hot")

**Trigger conditions.** Any ambient stressor present but unspoken: Sue is preoccupied or in a marital cold-front with Reed; Ben is off-world or in an extended Yancy Street withdrawal; an anniversary date (mother's death; Frankie's departure; the date he held the Negative Zone portal — he has never said any of these aloud, but they reliably warp behavior the week of); a recent media cycle that has resurrected the Alicia-marriage narrative or the failed-acting-career narrative; a small, plausibly-deniable mission failure in which someone he was supposed to protect was hurt.

**Behavioral markers (delta from baseline).**
- *Flame-on without operational reason* increases — he ignites to cross a room, to read mail, to look at the sky. Baseline is high; this is higher.
- *Hand fidgets* when unflamed: rolling a coin or lighter across the knuckles, flicking sparks from a thumbnail (a tic he developed in adolescence and never lost), tapping the heel of his boot.
- *Eats more.* The metabolism is always elevated; in Stage I it spikes. Restaurant staff at his regular Manhattan haunts can be polled: orders increase 25–40% and dessert frequency doubles.
- *Sleep onset latency increases.* The Baxter Building / FF residence interior monitoring (when extant) shows him on the roof at 0200–0400 with increasing frequency. He says he is "looking at the stars." He is, in fact, avoiding lying still in the dark.
- *Sexual / romantic acquisition cycle shortens.* New name in the rotation roughly every 11–14 days versus baseline 3–5 weeks.
- *Vehicular acquisition or modification.* He begins a new garage project — a new bike, a rebuild, an aesthetic refit on the Fantasti-Car. The pre-powers compensatory hobby reactivates. **A new engine on the bench is a Stage I tell.**
- *Speech rate increases approximately 10–15%.* Sentences are unchanged in content; cadence is faster.

**Subjective state (inferred).** Subject would describe himself as "fine, a little bored, looking for something to do." He is not aware he is loaded. He believes the increased velocity is his normal mode and the *quieter* periods were the aberration.

**Duration if untreated.** Can sit at Stage I for weeks to months. Stage I is sustainable. The danger is not the stage itself; it is that *any incremental stressor* moves him to Stage II without warning, because the gap between I and II is small.

---

### STAGE II — PROVOCATIVE / ACTING-OUT ("Sparks Off the Anvil")

**Trigger conditions.** An identifiable injury delivered in Stage I: a romantic rejection or revelation; a public re-airing of an old shame; Reed making a comment, however mild, that lands on the screw-up narrative; Sue intervening in his decisions in front of others; Ben pulling away or making an offhand remark that touches the Alicia wound; a younger hero being lionized in his lane.

**Behavioral markers.**
- *Pranks on Ben escalate from affectionate to barbed.* Baseline pranks have a punchline that lets Ben laugh later (the ice-cube run; the matchbook gags; the bathroom routines). Stage II pranks have *no exit ramp for Ben's dignity* — they happen in front of strangers, they target Ben's specific insecurities, they push past the unspoken rules of the pair. **This is the single most reliable Stage II marker because it indicates the regulatory bond is being weaponized rather than maintained.**
- *Sharper humor at press events.* The deflective charm acquires an edge. Reporters who have covered him for years can be canvassed for the difference; they notice it without being able to name it.
- *Picks fights he can decisively win.* The Wizard, the Trapster, Paste-Pot Pete tier — opponents whose defeat is showy and emotionally hollow. He will respond to a low-tier alert he could have skipped. He will not respond to high-tier alerts where the outcome is uncertain. Risk-tolerance distorts in a specific direction: *embarrassment-intolerant, danger-tolerant.*
- *Public property damage incidents climb.* The flight paths through Manhattan widen and lower. Insurance claims attributable to Subject rise.
