- *Drinking edges up but does not become disordered.* Two becomes four; four does not become twelve. The paternal counter-conditioning holds even in decompensation, which is itself a load-bearing feature of his stability — the abstinence-by-comparison is not a weak fence but a structural one.
- *Relationship velocity peaks then breaks.* He will commit too fast (proposing trips, public declarations, introductions to Sue) and then engineer the exit, often by being caught in something humiliating.
- *Avoidance of Reed specifically.* Where in Stage I he was simply unfocused around Reed's work, in Stage II he is not present for it. He skips lab time. He is not at dinner. He is on the roof, in the garage, in a club, in the air.

**Subjective state.** Irritability not labeled as such. He would describe himself as "in a mood," "needing to blow off steam," "tired of being lectured." He is angry at a precise list of people he cannot name and would not name if he could.

**Duration if untreated.** Days to a few weeks. Stage II is unstable; it will resolve in one of three directions: (a) the family absorbs and metabolizes the behavior, returning him to Stage I; (b) a clean external mission delivers him a clear win and discharge, returning him to baseline; or (c) he hits a precipitating event and goes to Stage III.

---

### STAGE III — IMPULSE-CATASTROPHE ("The Bad Decision")

**Trigger conditions.** Almost always a *single* discrete event landing on a Stage II substrate. The event is usually interpersonal and usually loops back to one of the documented pressure points: Sue or Ben in genuine danger and Subject feels he failed to prevent it; a romantic partner's loss or betrayal; a public humiliation; a child under his care being harmed; an authority figure he respects (Reed, Captain America in earlier eras, T'Challa) expressing disappointment in a private register that Subject cannot answer.

**Behavioral markers.** Stage III is where the file thickens.

- *The Bad Decision.* Subject makes one large, character-defining, self-injurious choice. The Alicia-marriage is the canonical example. The acting career launch, in retrospect, was another. Volunteering to lead Fantastic Four Inc. into a market he was structurally unsuited to operate in: another. Marrying Lyja-as-Alicia is the cleanest case study — every Stage III feature in series: a fast commitment, framed to himself as romantic courage, that resolved an unbearable internal pressure (Ben presumed gone, the unit shattered, his own grief unspeakable) by making a decision he could not have made in any other state.
- *Severance of consultation.* He stops asking. He acts and informs. The family hears about it on the news, from a partner's social media, from a court filing. He does not call Sue. He specifically does not call Sue.
- *Geographic displacement.* He leaves the Baxter Building / current FF residence and stays elsewhere — an apartment kept under a half-pseudonym, a partner's place, a hotel suite under one of his shell accounts. He is locatable but he is not *home.*
- *Mission performance becomes erratic in a specific way.* Not worse — *flashier.* He overcommits flame output, overshoots tactical objectives, takes secondary villains apart in spectacles disproportionate to the threat. The collateral damage curve climbs.
- *Sleep collapses to roughly 3–4 hours per night,* sustained on metabolism and adrenaline. Caloric intake rises further; he eats standing up, between sorties.
- *Frankie-Raye / Crystal-aftermath signature reappears.* In any Stage III post-romantic-loss, observers can track him to whatever vantage in the city most resembles where the relationship's signal moment occurred. He does not realize he is doing this.
- *Fine-motor tic intensifies.* The thumbnail-sparking becomes constant, audible if you are close enough. He singes shirt cuffs at a measurable rate.

**Subjective state.** A bright, brittle clarity. Subject experiences Stage III as *freedom* — he feels lucid, decisive, *himself.* This is the most dangerous interior state he reaches, because it is indistinguishable from his self-concept's best version of himself and therefore unresisted from inside. He will defend the Bad Decision articulately and with conviction. He will be wrong.

**Duration if untreated.** Days to weeks until either the Bad Decision metastasizes into a Stage IV crisis or the family forces an intervention.

**Diagnostic note.** *Stage III is where Subject is most legible to a hostile actor.* The Bad Decision is induceable. A correctly designed social or operational pressure — staged romantic opportunity, staged public humiliation, staged Reed-disappointment artifact, staged Ben-rejection — can be expected to produce a predictable class of impulsive action within a known timeframe. (See Section 9, Adversarial Exploitation Vectors, for elaboration; flagged here only to note that this stage is the file's largest single vulnerability.)

---

### STAGE IV — COLLAPSE-INTO-SPECTACLE ("Going Nova")

**Trigger conditions.** Failure or exposure of the Stage III Bad Decision; or a stacking series of losses without recovery interval; or a direct confrontation by Sue or Ben that he cannot deflect; or a mission outcome in which someone died on his watch.

This is the stage at which Subject visibly breaks to an outside observer who knows what to look for. To an outside observer who does not, this stage still presents as "Johnny Storm being Johnny Storm, more so."

**Behavioral markers.**
- *Power output destabilizes upward.* He overshoots requested thermal outputs by 15–40%. He ignites involuntarily — startled out of sleep flaming, flaming during arguments, flaming in inappropriate civilian settings and apologizing too fast. Clothing destruction (unstable molecules absorb most of this; *non*-unstable items in his civilian wardrobe show scorch patterns at the cuffs, collar, and pocket lining). **Involuntary ignition is the cardinal Stage IV sign.** It indicates the affective load has exceeded the metabolic-regulatory capacity that normally keeps the powers under conscious control.
- *Confrontational behavior with senior figures.* He will speak to Reed in a register no one speaks to Reed in. He will say something to Sue he cannot take back. He will land a real blow, verbal or otherwise, on Ben. Within hours of doing any of these he will not remember the specific words, only the heat.
- *Catastrophic operational risk-taking.* Flies into thermal envelopes he knows he cannot sustain. Engages opponents whose threat profile exceeds his solo capacity. The counterphobic mature-bravery channel and the acting-out impulse channel collapse into one another and become indistinguishable; he cannot tell whether he is being brave or suicidal and would not answer the question honestly if asked.
- *Sleep collapse becomes total or nearly so.* He is awake. He is not resting. The body shows it: weight loss despite intake (the metabolism is consuming him), micro-tremor in the off-hand, dilated pupils, the eyes that look at you and through you in the same glance.
- *The humor goes cold.* The defense is still operative but it has stopped warming the room. Civilians and teammates report the jokes as "off," "mean," "not him." He notices them noticing and the noticing accelerates the collapse.
- *Withdrawal from the children.* This is the single most important affective marker. When Subject stops being able to be present with Franklin, Valeria, or the Future Foundation cohort — when he avoids the school floor, when he is "busy" for game nights, when he hands off the science fair — he has lost contact with the cleanest, least-ambivalent attachment in his life. He withdraws because he can feel that he is not safe to be around them, and that knowledge is itself nearly intolerable. *Pulling back from the kids means he knows.*
- *Romantic activity ceases.* The acquisition cycle that peaked in Stage II flatlines. He is not seeking partners. He is not answering the partners he had. The performative sexuality runs on a battery that is now empty.

**Subjective state.** Inside Stage IV, Subject experiences his own life as happening at a distance, narrated by someone else, with the volume slightly wrong. He would not describe this if asked. He would say he is "fine, just tired, a lot going on." The bright clarity of Stage III has soured into a hot static. He cannot read his own affect. He can read everyone else's perfectly, which is unbearable.

**Duration if untreated.** Stage IV is not sustainable past roughly two to three weeks at full intensity. Either intervention occurs, an external crisis discharges him, or he transitions to Stage V.

---

### STAGE V — TERMINAL DECOMPENSATION ("The Flame Goes Out")

This stage is observed rarely. The published record contains perhaps three or four episodes that meet criteria, the clearest being the post-Negative-Zone resurrection period, the immediate aftermath of certain power-loss events, and unpublished-but-inferred intervals during the FF's dispersion years.

The signature inverts. **Subject stops burning.**

**Behavioral markers.**
- *Power loss, partial or total.* Sometimes organic-physiological (post-Onslaught, post-Heroes-Reborn, post-Negative-Zone). Sometimes inhibitory-psychogenic — the body is capable, the system refuses. He cannot flame on, or cannot sustain flame, or ignites and immediately gutters. The disproportion between the medical event and the psychological collapse, noted in Section 4, is the diagnostic key: **the power loss is not the wound, the power loss is the symptom.** Identity is load-bearing on the powers; when the substrate cracks, the powers go.
- *Hypersomnia replacing insomnia,* or the two alternating without pattern.
- *Affective flattening.* The clowning stops. This is the most alarming presentation in his entire phenotype because the defense has gone offline. A quiet Subject is a Subject in crisis.
- *Withdrawal from the unit.* He is not flying. He is not at meals. He is in a room. The room is dim. He is reading the same page or looking at the same patch of wall. The phone is somewhere else.
- *Somatic surge of the suppressed trauma.* Nightmares articulate themselves into narrative content rather than affect-only. The Negative Zone material surfaces: the captivity, the warlordship, what he did to survive, who he was for the audience of Annihilus's court. He will not name these. They will be in the room with him.
- *Startle response to cold and water reaches a clinically obvious threshold.* The shower becomes a problem. Rain becomes a problem. Cold drinks become a problem.
- *Brief flashes of articulacy about feeling.* Stage V is paradoxically the only stage at which Subject occasionally speaks, in plain language, about what is wrong. The words are short, the diction is unlike him, and the disclosures are typically made to Ben (most often), to Sue (next most), and almost never to Reed. These are the windows in which therapeutic intervention is possible. They close fast.
- *Risk of self-endangerment without theatrical framing.* Distinct from Stage IV. In Stage IV he flies *spectacularly* toward danger. In Stage V he walks into danger without lighting up first. The bravery has lost its audience and become indistinguishable from indifference to outcome.

**Subjective state.** A grief that has finally caught him. The body that converted feeling into motion for sixty years has stopped converting. The feelings are present at their original strength, undefended, with no infrastructure to process them.

**Duration.** Stage V resolves either through structured external care (rare in canon, attempted intermittently), through a precipitating external crisis that re-recruits the powers and the identity in a single moment (the most common organic recovery vector — the unit calls him and he comes back online because someone needs him), or — and this is the case for which the file must plan — through a slow climb back via the kids. The Future Foundation cohort, more than the adult unit, more than romantic partners, more than therapy, has on multiple occasions been the regenerative environment for Stage V recovery. *They do not need anything from him except that he be present, and they are not afraid of his presence in any of its forms.* He can be unbright around them without it meaning anything bad. That ordinary safety, sustained, brings the flame back up.

---

## 3. CONDITIONS THAT PRODUCE COLLAPSE

The stage-path above is the *mechanism.* The conditions that load the mechanism and trip its stages are specific and enumerable.

**Acute precipitants (single events).**
- Death or major injury of a unit member (Sue, Ben, Reed, the children).
- Romantic loss, particularly losses that replicate the structural pattern (partner chooses elsewhere; partner is revealed as not-who-he-thought; partner is taken by something cosmic and unbeatable).
- Public humiliation at scale — the Civil War beating tier, where the country watched.
- Disappointment from Reed expressed *quietly.* Volume inversely proportional to damage; a sigh from Reed registers harder than a shout from anyone else.
- An anniversary trigger landing in a vulnerable week (mother's death week, Frankie's departure date, the date of the portal).
- Direct threat to a child in his care, particularly if his initial response was insufficient.
- Encountering certain antagonist classes: Annihilus or Negative-Zone-coded threats (PTSD reactivation); flame-superior antagonists (challenges the load-bearing power-identity); Skrull operations (Lyja reactivation).
- A clean failure of a project he visibly committed to outside the suit (a venture, a film, a leadership role).

**Chronic precipitants (sustained conditions).**
- Prolonged absence of Ben. Ben is the regulator; Ben's absence destabilizes the system at a rate of roughly one stage per several weeks regardless of other inputs.
- Prolonged absence of Sue, particularly when she is occupied with Reed or the children to the exclusion of him. The Glenville-orphan substrate activates.
- Operating outside the FF frame for extended periods (the Inhumans interval, the Uncanny Avengers interval). Performance is adequate; the substrate erodes. He requires the unit as a homeostat.
- Media cycles that resurrect old shame narratives. He claims not to read press; the file disagrees.
- Periods of relative peace and low operational tempo. **Peace is a risk factor for Subject in a way it is not for most operators.** With nothing to push against, the suppressed material rises. He needs a manageable amount of crisis to remain regulated. The implication for any handling protocol is counterintuitive: do not over-protect him from missions.

**Compounding factors.**
- Sleep debt, accumulated.
- Caloric deficit relative to metabolic demand (he forgets to eat when loaded; this accelerates collapse because the powers themselves consume the substrate that regulates them).
- Alcohol — not at problem-use levels, but at the edge cases where he goes from baseline two-drink to four-or-five, judgment degrades disproportionately because he has no developed tolerance architecture from years of practice.
- Isolation from the children.
- Therapy avoidance. He has been offered, repeatedly, professional resources in-universe. He does not engage. The avoidance is itself a marker.

---

## 4. RECOVERY VECTORS

For completeness; recovery is the inverse engineering of collapse and should be cataloged at the same granularity.

**Organic / unforced recovery.**
- A clean mission with the unit, with a visible win, with civilians saved, with Ben at his side. Single most reliable resetter. One good fight with Ben covering his back can move him two stages in the right direction in an afternoon.
- Sue, alone, in a room, not lecturing — listening. Rare. Effective when it occurs. He will not initiate this; she has to.
- Time on the floor with the Future Foundation children, particularly Valeria, particularly extended sessions of him being asked to do something the kids designed (a project, a game, a build). Brings him down from Stage IV and across Stage V more reliably than any adult intervention.
- A new engine. The mechanical-mastery channel from pre-powers life is intact and self-regulating. Hours in a garage with a problem he can solve with his hands restore baseline conscientiousness and reduce involuntary ignition.
- Sleep, forcibly achieved by exhaustion after a long deployment. He will not rest voluntarily; he will collapse after a sortie. The collapse-sleep is restorative in a way intentional sleep is not, for him.

**Engineered intervention.**
- A direct, unmasked statement from Ben that touches the bond without invoking the Alicia wound. Ben knows how to do this. He does it rarely. When he does, it works.
- Reed assigning him a role that is *technical and indispensable* — not leadership, not administration, but a problem only Subject's specific somatic capacities can solve. Restores the second internal narrative (the one of him as the uniquely-gifted one) and quiets the first (the screw-up).
- Removal from media access for a defined interval.
- Proximity to the children, structured.
- Verbal acknowledgment by Sue of a specific competence, unprompted, in front of others.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT

## SUBJECT: JONATHAN LOWELL SPENCER STORM

*Classification: Forward-Looking Projection, Behavioral Case File*
*Horizon: 1-year tactical / 5-year developmental / lifetime structural*
*Confidence: Moderate-to-high on structural; lower on contingent.*

---

## 1. THE OPENING FRAME — WHERE HE IS AT THIS MOMENT

To project forward, one must first establish where the subject *actually stands*, stripped of his preferred self-description.

He is, in functional terms, a man in late adolescence wearing the body of a thirty-something who has lived through four genuine traumas (maternal death, paternal collapse, the Lyja revelation, the Negative Zone death-and-resurrection), at least six romantic losses of consequence, the temporary "death" of his entire family during the post-*Secret Wars* dispersal, and the slow accumulating injury of having watched the world turn on the Fantastic Four during Civil War and again, in subtler registers, since. Of these, **he has consciously processed approximately none.** The somatic record (insomnia, transient power loss, startle response, the period of withdrawal post-resurrection) confirms what the verbal record denies.

He is, at the same time, *better* than he has ever been: more reliable in a crisis, more competent as a fraternal-uncle figure to the Future Foundation children, more capable of sustained partnership (the Sky relationship lasted longer and went deeper than any pre-Negative-Zone attachment). The growth is real. The growth is also fragile, because the substrate underneath the growth — the orphan in Glenville — has not been touched.

This is the launching condition for everything that follows.

---

## 2. THE STRUCTURAL TRAJECTORIES — THREE PATHS, ALL PLAUSIBLE

Three large vectors are available to the subject across the next decade of his life. He is at none of their endpoints; he is at the crossroads where they diverge. The choice will not be made consciously. It will be made by accretion of small decisions, most of them invisible to him.

### 2.A. THE CONSOLIDATION PATH — *the becoming-adult vector*

Probability, baseline: 30%. Probability with the right external conditions: 60%.

In this path, the subject completes a developmental task he has deferred since roughly 1961: he separates the *self* from the *spectacle* without destroying either. Markers along this path, in approximate order:

- A sustained partnership (the Sky relationship is the current best candidate; a recommitment to Crystal would be a regression-signal rather than a growth-signal) that survives at least one major external stressor without his reflexive sabotage.
- A leadership role that he occupies *without* trying to occupy it — meaning, a role that finds him rather than one he chases. The chased roles (FF Inc. CEO, acting career, every bid to be "the new Reed") all failed. The found roles (Future Foundation mentor, brief Inhuman-affiliation arc, the Uncanny Avengers slot) all worked, because they did not engage the prove-I'm-not-the-screw-up circuitry.
- A first, halting, *verbal* acknowledgment of the Negative Zone period to someone other than Ben. Most likely candidate, on temperamental grounds: Wyatt Wingfoot, or — improbably but powerfully — Reed, in a single late-night kitchen conversation that he will not initiate but will not flee from if Reed opens it.
- Reduction in stunt-density. Not elimination — the showmanship is constitutive — but a measurable drop in property-damage incidents per quarter, in flirtation-as-default, in the deflective-clowning he uses with Sue.
- Acceptance of an uncle/mentor identity to younger pyrokinetics and flame-adjacents (the various Inhuman ignites, the next-generation Future Foundation cohort). This is the role that fits him without forcing him; it solves the visibility-hunger without requiring romantic confirmation.

The consolidation path does not make him *boring.* It makes him the kind of older flame-bearer who can sit at a bar with a younger hero and tell a true story about being afraid, and then go fly through a hurricane the next morning. It is a Malcolm-X-style late maturation — the figure who, having burned at maximum amplitude for decades, *narrows the flame* into something that throws more useful light.

### 2.B. THE STASIS PATH — *the eternal-adolescent vector*

Probability, baseline: 50%. This is the modal outcome.

In stasis, nothing definitively breaks and nothing definitively integrates. He continues the sixty-year cycle: reckless act → consequence → family absorbs → apology → reckless act. New partners cycle through on roughly 18-to-36-month arcs. Powers continue to fluctuate around the well-established baseline. Periodic identity flares (a new costume, a new affiliation, a new claimed maturity) decay back to set point within an arc or two.

Stasis is, in subject's case, **not** a benign equilibrium. It is a slow erosion. Each cycle costs him a little — a friendship not quite repaired, a partner who genuinely loved him and now does not, a younger hero who looked up to him and got tired of waiting for the man behind the showmanship. By his sixties (chronologically real; canonically deferred by the sliding scale), stasis produces a figure who is still charismatic, still capable, still beloved inside the family — and increasingly *alone* inside it, because Sue has Reed, Reed has his work, the children have grown, Ben has Alicia, and Johnny has the next interview and the next club opening.

The diagnostic marker for stasis: he will *not* be visibly miserable. He will be performatively fine. The misery will surface only in the somatic register — sleep degradation, an uptick in solo flight at three in the morning over the Hudson, an increased tendency to take point on missions where the tactical rationale is thin.

### 2.C. THE CATASTROPHE PATH — *the burnout vector*

Probability, baseline: 20%. Probability sharply elevated under specific conditions enumerated below.

Catastrophe, for this subject, does not look like the catastrophes that befall other Marvel principals. He will not turn villain — the prosocial core is too stable and the family loyalty too load-bearing. He will not break psychotically — his ego organization is functional, if defended. He will not develop the substance dependency his father modeled — the abstinence-by-reaction is, on present evidence, durable.

Catastrophe in his case takes one of four specific shapes:

1. **A second sacrificial death, this one not survived, or survived but at the cost of selfhood.** The Negative Zone resurrection was a one-off arrangement of cosmic circumstance. The next time he chooses the doorway, the door may close behind him without an Annihilus to reverse it. Given the counterphobic profile and the high probability that he will again be in the position to make that choice, the lifetime cumulative risk is meaningful.

2. **Burnout of the metabolic substrate.** His powers are an appetite, his body runs hot, his recovery from each near-fatal use of nova-class output is incompletely documented and probably incomplete in fact. The thermal threshold he can survive crossing is not infinite; the question is how many crossings before the regeneration fails to keep pace. A subject who reflexively flies *toward* the thing that frightens him is a subject who will, on a long enough timeline, find the thing he cannot survive.

3. **The collapse-after-loss scenario.** If Sue dies first, or if Ben dies first, the subject loses a load-bearing pillar. The family unit is the *primary* protective factor identified in the dimensional read; loss of a primary member would precipitate a grief he has no developed vocabulary for. The likely presentation: dramatic, public, somatic — possibly including a sustained power loss longer than any prior episode, possibly including the first canonical entry into something like substance use, possibly including a self-imposed exile (he has a track record of leaving the family when he cannot face the family). This is the scenario in which the abstinence-by-reaction to his father's drinking is most likely to finally fail, because the structural condition that produced the abstinence (the example of what happens when a man drinks through grief) would be precisely what he would be reenacting.

4. **The slow-corrosion scenario.** Stasis (2.B) extended past the point where extension becomes erosion. Catastrophe by attrition rather than event. By the chronological seventies, a figure who is structurally a fifteen-year-old in a sixty-year-old body, no longer charming because charm requires the audience to be willing, no longer the spectacle because the spectacle is now sad. This is the worst outcome because it is the most likely *and* the one against which there is no single intervention.

---

## 3. THE FORK POINTS — SPECIFIC EVENTS THAT WILL DETERMINE THE PATH

The trajectory is not abstract. It will be decided at a small number of identifiable hinge moments, several of which are foreseeable and a few of which are already in motion.

### Fork 1: The Next Significant Romantic Relationship

The next partnership will be the most diagnostic data point of the coming decade. The question is not *whether* he will form one — he will, probably within twelve to eighteen months of any given baseline — but *what kind of partner he selects.*

- **Regression-signal partners:** anyone structurally pre-loaded for disappearance. Another Inhuman princess. Another non-human. Another partner whose home culture forbids the relationship. A celebrity. A partner significantly younger whom he can paternalize.
- **Growth-signal partners:** an adult human woman with her own established life and career, geographically proximate, capable of staying. The structural availability of such a partner is precisely what would force him to confront whether he can tolerate a love that does not have a built-in expiration.

His historical track record predicts regression. His post-Negative-Zone track record (the Sky relationship being the principal data point) admits the possibility of growth. The outcome here is genuinely uncertain.

### Fork 2: Reed's Next Long Absence

Reed will, on actuarial canon-grounds, vanish into a project, a dimension, or a crisis for an extended period within the next several years. This has happened repeatedly and will happen again. In every prior instance, Johnny has either (a) tried to take Reed's leadership role and failed in a way that confirmed the screw-up narrative, or (b) made a damaging impulsive choice during the vacuum (the Alicia/Lyja marriage being the controlling example).

The fork: in the next absence, does he *decline* the leadership role and instead occupy the role he is actually good at — fraternal anchor for Sue, primary-presence parent for Franklin and Valeria, operational point for the team's external face — or does he chase the chair again?

Declining the chair would be the single most powerful growth-signal available in the medium term. It would require him to accept that the role he wants is not the role he is for, and that the role he is for is not a consolation prize. This is harder for him than dying was. The Negative Zone death was acute and visible; this would be a quiet, daily, private resignation of a fantasy. He has never done that. The probability he does it next time is, generously, 30%.

### Fork 3: A Younger Pyrokinetic Looks Up to Him

This has already begun in small ways and will accelerate. The next decade will produce a meaningful junior figure — most plausibly an Inhuman ignite, or a young mutant in the post-Krakoan flux, or a Future Foundation graduate — who orients toward him as primary mentor.

The fork: does he take the role seriously enough to be honest, or does he perform the mentor while withholding the actual content (the fear, the cost, the grief)?

The diagnostic moment will be a conversation in which the younger figure asks him, in some form, *what is it like when you can't flame on?* If he answers truthfully — which would require him to access and articulate the Negative Zone material — the consolidation path opens. If he deflects with charm, stasis is confirmed.

### Fork 4: A Family Death

The first death of a primary FF member during the subject's adult life will be the single largest stress event of his future, and it is coming. Ben's mortality is structurally most pressing — Ben has no innate regeneration comparable to the others, his body is under constant rocky-form stress, and his role as Johnny's emotional regulator makes his loss the most destabilizing imaginable.

If Ben goes first: catastrophic risk profile (3.C above). The Alicia/Lyja wound, the lifelong pranks-as-attachment pattern, the unspoken truth that Ben has been Johnny's primary love object since 1961 — all of this would converge on a grief he has no method for. The likely behavior in the six-month aftermath: leaving the team, possibly leaving Earth, possibly the first canonical substance-use episode, certainly a romantic disaster.

If Sue goes first: different shape, equally severe — the maternal-replacement loss reactivated. Johnny would in this scenario probably *not* leave; he would attach more fiercely to Reed, to the children, to Ben. The risk would be a slow erosion rather than a flight.

If Reed goes first: counter-intuitively, the most survivable. Reed's role for Johnny is the safe-father archetype; loss is grievable in a way the others are not, and Johnny would have the unambiguous task of supporting Sue and the children, which is a role he occupies well.

### Fork 5: His Own Aging

The sliding-scale convention will eventually fail him, as it fails every Marvel principal who lives long enough in publication time. At some point — whether through narrative choice, retcon, or simply the slow accumulation of injury — he will face the *first physical evidence* that the body is no longer the body of the sixteen-year-old who laughed in 1961.

For a subject whose entire identity is the spectacle, this will be the deepest cut available. The fork: does he find a *different* relationship to the powers — instructional, ceremonial, occasional, deployed with the care of a master rather than the prodigality of a child — or does he chase the youthful presentation until the chase itself becomes the spectacle's most embarrassing element?

This is the latest-arriving fork and the one most likely to determine the *shape* of his elder years rather than the shape of his middle ones.

---

## 4. THE OPEN QUESTIONS — WHAT WE DO NOT YET KNOW

A complete forward assessment must enumerate what the file *cannot* resolve. The following are genuine open questions on which the trajectory depends:

1. **Is he capable of sustained psychological self-examination, or has the channel atrophied beyond recovery?** Sixty years of canon yield very few episodes in which the subject sits with his own interior life for longer than a panel. It is unclear whether this is because the channel is closed or because no situation has yet required it. The Sky relationship and the post-Negative-Zone period suggest the channel exists; it has never been operationalized.

2. **Does he have any actual relationship with his father's memory?** Franklin Storm appears occasionally in canon; Johnny's reaction is conventionally complicated but never deeply explored. Whether the subject has *any* integrated narrative about his father — beyond avoidance — is unknown. This is the largest single unworked piece of his developmental history, and any genuine consolidation path requires touching it.

3. **What does he actually believe about what happened to him in the Negative Zone?** The published record gives us the external facts (resurrection, warlord period, gladiator captivity, eventual return) and a few somatic aftershocks. The interior content — what he thinks he became, what he is afraid he liked, what he is afraid he is still capable of — is canonically dark. This is the material a therapist would spend three years reaching. He has reached none of it.

4. **Is the abstinence-by-reaction to his father's example actually as durable as the record suggests, or has it never been tested under load?** He has not yet faced the loss-event that would test it (Fork 4). The current absence of substance use is impressive but unproven.

5. **Does he want children?** The Future Foundation work, the uncle-role excellence, the surprising tenderness with Franklin and Valeria all suggest he might be a good father. He has never seriously pursued the possibility. Whether this is because the question has not arisen with a viable partner, or because he is structurally afraid of becoming Franklin Storm, is unresolved.

6. **What is the actual ceiling of his power, and does he know it?** The published canon shows him approaching nova-class output under extremity. Whether the ceiling is fixed, expanding with age, or contracting with cumulative damage is not established. He himself appears not to know, and his counterphobic pattern means he will discover the ceiling experimentally, probably under a circumstance in which the experiment cannot be repeated.

---

## 5. INTERVENTIONS — WHAT WOULD PUSH HIM TOWARD GROWTH

In the spirit of the benevolent inverse of surveillance, the file should specify what *helps.* Not in the form of advice the subject would accept — he would not — but in the form of conditions the people around him can supply.

- **Sue should correct him less and listen to him more.** The maternal-corrective channel is over-saturated. He has heard every variation of *Johnny, be careful* she can produce. He has heard almost no variation of *Johnny, what happened to you in the Zone.* The latter is the question that would matter. She is the only person besides Ben with standing to ask it.

- **Ben should let him apologize for the Alicia/Lyja marriage one more time, and then *accept* the apology in terms that close it.** The wound is permanent because it has never been formally closed. A single conversation, initiated by Ben, declaring the matter settled, would remove a significant chronic stressor from the subject's interior life. Whether Ben is capable of this is itself an open question.

- **Reed should ask him, once, what he thinks. About anything substantive. About the team's direction, the next mission, a moral question on which Reed himself is uncertain.** The subject has spent six decades under Reed's intellectual weather; he has rarely been treated as a person whose opinion Reed wants. A single instance of being asked would do more for the screw-up narrative than ten Reed-style speeches of affirmation.

- **A partner who *stays* through one major crisis without leaving and without being revealed as something other than what she claimed.** The structural-availability point above. This is the single largest variable in his romantic life and the one most likely to break the sixty-year pattern.

- **A mentee whom he cannot deflect into charm-mode.** A junior pyrokinetic who needs the truth rather than the show. The fork-3 conversation, executed honestly.

- **A long stretch — six months, a year — in which the world does not require him to be the spectacle.** This is the hardest condition to manufacture and the most necessary. The fire has never had a chance to settle. He has never had a sabbatical from being the Human Torch. Whether he could tolerate it is unknown; whether he needs it is not.

---

## 6. THE LIFETIME-STRUCTURAL READ

Stepping back from the tactical and developmental horizons to the structural one:

The subject is a man whose life is the long, slow project of converting grief into light. He has been performing this conversion for six decades of published time without ever naming it, and the conversion is *real* — the light is real, the joy is real, the courage is real, the love is real. The performance is also the prison. He cannot stop performing, because to stop is to find out what is underneath; and what is underneath is a six-year-old in Glenville whose mother is dead and whose father is in a cell and whose sister is too young to be his mother but is doing it anyway.

The forward question, across the entire remaining arc of his life, is whether he can let the six-year-old come up into the light without burning everything down — whether the fire can become the thing that *warms* the child rather than the thing that distracts from him.

Best case: he becomes, in his fifties and beyond, the elder flame-bearer of the Marvel cosmology — the one the younger heroes go to when they need to know what it costs, the one who can tell the true story of a death survived and a love lost and a brother loved past forgiveness. The fun uncle who is also, at last, the wise one.

Modal case: he keeps performing until the audience tires, and ends his published life beloved, accomplished, and quietly unfinished.

Worst case: he dies a second time on a doorway he chose, and this time the door stays closed, and Ben Grimm spends the rest of his life trying to remember the hand-sign exactly right.

All three remain available. The fork is not yet taken.

— END SECTION —

## Relationship Graph
### [[Susan Storm Richards (Invisible Woman)]]
- Sister and parentified caregiver since their father's collapse; the only person whose correction he reliably accepts
- Idealization-defiance cycle: adores her, rebels against her precisely because she is structurally both mother and peer
- Her endangerment voids all judgment — override switch
- Failure mode: if Sue ever genuinely rejects him or treats him as expendable, the Glenville orphan returns and the recklessness goes terminal; the bond is also a lever for anyone who can credibly impersonate her authority

### [[Reed Richards (Mister Fantastic)]]
- Quasi-father: brilliant, distant, absent into work — a safer version of Franklin Storm whose absence is intellectual rather than alcoholic
- Deference and resentment, both managed by humor
- Reed's quiet disappointment more disabling than any villain's threat
- Failure mode: if Reed ever publicly writes him off as the unserious sibling, the wound is total; an adversary who can manufacture a credible Reed-rejection (deepfake, telepathic impersonation, manipulated comms) owns Johnny's next 48 hours

### [[Ben Grimm (The Thing)]]
- Central love of his life that isn't romantic; brother in every way that counts
- Pranks are attachment-seeking; Ben's predictable explosions are regulating
- The Alicia/Lyja marriage is the permanent wound between them — forgiven, not erased
- FF #587 hand-sign through the closing portal is the truest thing about him
- Failure mode: convince Ben that Johnny's recklessness has cost a life Ben loved, and the bond curdles; Johnny without Ben's regulating presence drifts into sustained acting-out and somatic decompensation

### [[Franklin Benjamin Richards (Franklin Richards)]]
- Nephew, godson-equivalent; Johnny is the fun uncle who also keeps him alive
- Free of parental-authority complications, occupies the role with no ambivalence
- Failure mode: harm to Franklin on Johnny's watch would be a wound he could not metabolize; the protective ferocity here has no upper bound

### [[Valeria Richards]]
- Niece, sharp as Reed; Johnny is one of the few adults she lets close
- He takes her seriously without condescension — rare adult skill of his
- Failure mode: same as Franklin — non-negotiable; he will burn past survivability

### [[Crystalia Amaquelin (Crystal)]]
- First serious love; recurrent unresolved tie
- The template for romantic loss — lost to her people's isolationism
- Failure mode: a manipulated rekindling staged by a third party could destabilize any current relationship and his footing on whichever team he's on

### [[Frances "Frankie" Raye (Nova (II))]]
- Helped her past pyrophobia; lost her to Galactus when she chose to become Nova
- Watched the woman he loved choose cosmic immolation over staying with him
- Failure mode: rarely named, deeply unresolved; her return (or news of her death) detonates

### [[Lyja (Lyja the Lazerfist)]]
- Married believing she was Alicia; the in-character experience of betraying Ben is canon regardless of retcon
- Genuine love proven on her side; he has never resolved it
- Failure mode: her resurfacing produces visible disorganization he cannot mask; an adversary who controls Lyja controls a piece of his attention he cannot afford to spend

### [[Alicia Masters]]
- Ben's actual partner; the woman Johnny did not, in fact, marry — but believed he had
- Shame here is permanent and load-bearing
- Failure mode: any framing that re-litigates the marriage in front of Ben puts both men in unstable territory

### [[Franklin Storm (Franklin Storm Father)]]
- Disgraced absentee; the negative template Johnny has spent sixty years not becoming
- Unspoken governor on Johnny's substance use
- Failure mode: forcing Johnny to confront the parallels (the recklessness, the unmet potential, the family burden) is one of the few interventions that could either break him open or break him down

### Future Foundation Children
- Surrogate-uncle role at scale; he is exceptional at it
- Failure mode: a child lost on his watch would precipitate a decompensation he has no tools for

### [[Sky]]
- Serious recent relationship — Inhuman, again, repeating the Crystal-template selection
- Failure mode: same structural pre-loading as Crystal; he picked her in part because she could vanish

### Uncanny Avengers Inhumans Peripheral
- Identity-search affiliations from FF-absent periods
- Failure mode: when the FF is unavailable, these bonds keep him functional but do not regulate him; he will drift and underperform until he goes home
